Bringing forth the water of the earth by digging channels is easier and nearer than letting it flow from a distant place lower than it. And because it is present in the heart yet forgotten due to preoccupation away from it, God Almighty named all the knowledges of faith "remembrance," saying: "Indeed, it is We who sent down the Remembrance, and indeed, We will be its guardian" (15:9). And He said: "That those of understanding may be reminded" (14:52). And He said: "And We have certainly made the Qur'an easy for remembrance, so is there any who will remember?" (54:17).

This is the remedy for patience against whisperings and distractions, and it is the final degree of patience. Indeed, patience in severing all attachments takes precedence over patience against passing thoughts. Junayd, mercy of God upon him, said: "The journey from this world to the Hereafter is easy for the believer, but abandoning people for the love of the Truth is severe. The journey from the self to God Almighty is difficult and severe, and patience with God is more severe." He mentioned the severity of patience against the distractions of the heart, then the severity of abandoning people, and the most severe attachment upon the soul is attachment to people and love of status. For the pleasure of leadership, dominance, exaltation, and having followers is the most overpowering of pleasures in this world upon the souls of the rational. How could it not be the most overpowering, when its object is an attribute from the attributes of God Almighty, which is Lordship?

The heart naturally loves and seeks this, due to its correspondence with matters of divine lordship. This is alluded to in the saying of God, exalted is He: "Say, 'The spirit is from the command of my Lord.'" The heart is not blameworthy for loving that. Rather, it is blameworthy for an error that befalls it due to the deception of the accursed Satan, who is distanced from the world of the Command, for he envied it for being from the world of the Command, so he misled and seduced it. How could it be blameworthy for it, when it seeks the happiness of the Hereafter? It seeks nothing but an everlasting life in which there is no annihilation, a might in which there is no humiliation, a security in which there is no fear, a richness in which there is no poverty, and a perfection in which there is no deficiency. All of these are from the attributes of divine lordship. It is not blameworthy for seeking that. Rather, it is the right of every servant to seek a great dominion that has no end. And the seeker of dominion inevitably seeks elevation, might, and perfection. However, dominion is of two kinds: a dominion mixed with various pains and followed by swift termination, but it is immediate, and it is in this world; and an everlasting, permanent dominion, not sullied by any trouble or pain, nor cut off by any cutter, but it is deferred.

Man was created hasty, desirous of the immediate. So Satan came and approached him through the medium of the haste inherent in his nature, and seduced him with the immediate, and made the present world appealing to him. And he approached him through the medium of folly, and promised him delusion regarding the Hereafter, and made him covet the dominion of the Hereafter along with the dominion of this world, as He said: "And the fool is he who follows his soul's caprice and wishes upon God vain wishes." So the forsaken one was deceived by his delusion and busied himself with seeking the might and dominion of this world to the extent of his ability. But the divinely-guided one did not grasp the rope of his delusion, for he knew the avenues of his guile, so he turned away from the immediate. He described the forsaken ones with His saying, exalted is He: "No! But you love the immediate and neglect the Hereafter." And He said, exalted is He: "Indeed, these love the immediate and leave behind them a heavy Day." And He said, exalted is He: "So turn away from him who turns away from Our remembrance and desires not but the life of this world. That is their attainment of knowledge."

When the guile of Satan spread among all creation, God sent the angels to the messengers, and they revealed to them what had befallen creation from the destruction and seduction of the enemy. So they busied themselves with calling creation to the true dominion, away from the metaphorical dominion which has no reality if it is safe, and no permanence at all. So they called out among them: "O you who have believed, what is [the matter] with you that, when it is said to you, 'Go forth in the cause of God,' you adhere heavily to the earth? Are you satisfied with the life of this world rather than the Hereafter? But what is the enjoyment of worldly life compared to the Hereafter except a little."

Thus, the Torah, the Gospel, the Psalms, the Criterion, the Scrolls of Moses and Abraham, and every revealed book were sent for nothing but to call creation to the permanent, everlasting dominion. What is intended for them is that they be kings in this world and kings in the Hereafter. As for kingship in this world, it is through asceticism in it and contentment with little from it. As for kingship in the Hereafter, it is through proximity to God, exalted is He, attaining an everlasting life in which there is no annihilation, a might in which there is no humiliation, and a coolness of the eye which is hidden in this world, which no soul knows. And Satan calls them to the dominion of this world, knowing that the dominion of the Hereafter is thereby missed, for this world and the Hereafter are co-wives, and knowing that this world will not be safe for him either—for if it were safe for him, he would envy him for it as well—but the dominion of this world is not free from disputes, troubles, prolonged anxieties in management, and likewise all the causes of status. Then, however much one attains safety and the causes are complete, the lifespan ends: "Until, when the earth has taken its ornament and is adorned and its people suppose that they have capability over it, Our command comes to it by night or by day, and We make it as a harvest, as if it had not flourished yesterday."

So God, exalted is He, struck a similitude for it, saying: "And present to them the similitude of the life of this world: [It is] like water which We send down from the sky; the plants of the earth absorb it, then it becomes dry stubble which the winds scatter."

And asceticism in this world, since it is a present dominion, Satan envied him for it and turned him away from it. The meaning of asceticism is that the servant masters his passion and his anger, so that they submit to the motive of religion and the indication of faith. This is a dominion by deserving, for by it its possessor becomes free, and by the domination of passion over him he becomes a slave to his private parts, his stomach, and all his other desires, thus being driven like a beast, owned, with the reins of passion pulling him by his throat to where it wills and desires. How great is the delusion of man when he thought he attains dominion by becoming owned, and attains lordship by becoming a slave! Can such a one be anything but inverted in this world and overturned in the Hereafter? For this reason, a certain king said to a certain ascetic: "Do you have a need?" He said: "How can I ask you for a need when my dominion is greater than your dominion?" He said: "How is that?" He said: "Whoever you are a slave to, he is a slave to me." He said: "How is that?" He said: "You are a slave to your passion, your anger, your private parts, and your stomach, and I have mastered all of these, so they are slaves to me." This, then, is the dominion in this world, and it is what leads to the dominion in the Hereafter.

As for the Hereafter, those deceived by the devil's delusion have lost both this world and the next, while those who were granted success in holding fast to the Straight Path have won both this world and the Hereafter. Now, if you have come to understand the meaning of sovereignty and lordship, the meaning of subjugation and servitude, the point of error therein, and the manner of the devil's blinding and deception, it will become easy for you to turn away from sovereignty and status, to avert yourself from it, and to be patient when it is lost. For by abandoning it, you become a sovereign in the present moment and hope for sovereignty in the Hereafter. As for one to whom these matters are unveiled after he has become accustomed to status, familiar with it, and firmly rooted in it through the habitual practice of its means, mere knowledge and unveiling will not suffice for his cure. Rather, he must add action to it. His action lies in three matters:

First, that he flee from the place of status so as not to witness its means, for patience in the presence of its means becomes difficult, just as one overpowered by lust flees from gazing upon arousing images. Whoever does not do this has been ungrateful for God's favor in the vastness of the earth, as He, Exalted is He, said: "Was not the earth of God spacious enough for you to emigrate therein?" (Qur'an 4:97). Second, that he compel himself in his actions to perform deeds contrary to what he is accustomed to, thus replacing affectation with simplicity, and the attire of dignity with the attire of humility. Likewise, every posture, state, and action in dwelling, clothing, food, standing, and sitting that he was accustomed to in fulfillment of the demands of his status, he should replace with their opposites, until through habituation to that, the opposite of what was previously ingrained in him through habituation to its contrary becomes firmly rooted. For there is no meaning to treatment except through opposition. Third, that he observe gentleness and gradual progression in this, not shifting all at once to the extreme limit of simplicity, for human nature is averse and cannot be shifted from its dispositions except gradually. So he leaves off some and consoles himself with some. Then, when his soul is content with that some, he begins by leaving off some of that some until it is content with the remainder. He does this little by little until he subdues those traits that were ingrained in him. To this gradual progression points the saying (of the Prophet, peace be upon him): "Verily, this religion is firm, so enter into it gently, and do not make the worship of God hateful to yourself, for the one who overburdens (his mount) neither covers ground nor spares his riding beast." And to it points his saying, peace be upon him: "Do not be harsh with this religion, for whoever is harsh with it will be overcome by it."

Therefore, add what we have mentioned concerning the treatment of patience against insinuating thoughts, against lust, and against status, to what we have mentioned of the governing principles of the paths of spiritual struggle in the Book of "Disciplining the Soul" from the Quarter of the Destructive Matters. Take it as your guide to know thereby the treatment of patience in all the categories we previously detailed, for detailing each one would be lengthy. Whoever observes gradual progression, patience will elevate him to a state where being patient without it becomes difficult for him, just as being patient with it was difficult before. Thus his affairs are reversed: what was beloved to him becomes detested, and what was disliked becomes a pleasant drink from which he cannot bear to be patient. This is known only through experience and taste. It has a parallel in habits, for a child is compelled to learn in the beginning by force, and patience from play and patience with learning become difficult for him. Until, when his insight is opened and he becomes familiar with knowledge, the matter is reversed: patience from knowledge and patience with play become difficult for him. To this points what is narrated from one of the knowers, that he asked al-Shibli about patience: "Which is the most severe?" He said: "Patience in God, Exalted is He." He said: "No." He said: "Patience for God." He said: "No." He said: "Patience with God." He said: "No." He said: "Then what?" He said: "Patience from God." Al-Shibli let out a cry such that his soul was nearly destroyed. It has been said concerning the meaning of His saying, Exalted is He: "Be patient, and outdo others in patience, and be steadfast" (Qur'an 3:200): "Be patient in God, outdo others in patience by God, and be steadfast with God." And it is said: Patience for God is sufficiency, patience by God is permanence, patience with God is fidelity, and patience from God is estrangement. It has been said in its meaning:

"Patience from You has blameworthy consequences,
While patience in all other things is praiseworthy."

And it is also said:

"Patience is borne in all situations,
Except concerning You, for it is not becoming."

This is the end of what we wished to explain concerning the sciences and secrets of patience.

The Second Half of the Book is on Gratitude, and it has three pillars:
The First: On the virtue of gratitude, its reality, its divisions, and its rulings.
The Second: On the reality of blessing and its specific and general divisions.
The Third: On clarifying which is superior: gratitude or patience.

The First Pillar: Concerning Gratitude Itself
(Clarifying the Virtue of Gratitude)

Know that God, Exalted is He, coupled gratitude with remembrance in His Book, even though He said: "And the remembrance of God is greater" (Qur'an 29:45). So He, Exalted is He, said: "So remember Me; I will remember you. And be grateful to Me and do not deny Me" (Qur'an 2:152). And He, Exalted is He, said: "What would God do with your punishment if you are grateful and believe?" (Qur'an 4:147). And He, Exalted is He, said: "And We will reward..."

And He, the Exalted, said, informing about the accursed Iblis: "I will surely sit in wait for them on Your straight path." It is said this is the path of gratitude. Due to the elevated rank of gratitude, the accursed one attacked creation, saying: "And you will not find most of them grateful." And He, the Exalted, said: "And few of My servants are grateful." And Allah, the Exalted, has decreed increase with gratitude without exception, saying: "If you are grateful, I will surely increase you." He made exceptions in five things: enrichment, response, provision, forgiveness, and repentance. He, the Exalted, said: "Then Allah will enrich you from His bounty if He wills," and said: "He removes that for which you supplicate Him, if He wills," and said: "He provides for whom He wills without account," and said: "And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills," and said: "And Allah turns in forgiveness to whom He wills." And it is a created attribute from the attributes of Lordship, as He, the Exalted, said: "And Allah is Appreciative and Forbearing." And Allah has made gratitude the key speech of the people of Paradise, as He, the Exalted, said: "And they will say, 'Praise to Allah, who has fulfilled for us His promise,'" and said: "And their final call will be, 'Praise to Allah, Lord of the worlds.'"

As for the narrations, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: "The grateful eater is in the status of the patient faster." It is narrated from 'Ata that he said: "I entered upon 'A'ishah, may Allah be pleased with her, and said, 'Inform us of the most amazing thing you saw from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him.' She wept and said, 'And which of his affairs was not amazing? He came to me one night and entered with me in my bed'—or she said, 'in my cover'—until his skin touched my skin. Then he said, 'O daughter of Abu Bakr, allow me to worship my Lord.' She said, 'I said, "I love your closeness, but I prefer your desire." So I permitted him. He stood up to a water skin, performed ablution without using much water, then stood to pray. He wept until his tears flowed onto his chest. Then he bowed and wept, then prostrated and wept, then raised his head and wept. He continued like that, weeping, until Bilal came to give the call to prayer. I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, what makes you weep when Allah has forgiven your past and future sins?' He said, 'Should I not be a grateful servant? And why should I not do that when Allah, the Exalted, has revealed to me, "Indeed, in the creation of the heavens and the earth..."' the verse." This indicates that weeping should never cease. To this secret points what is narrated that one of the prophets passed by a small stone from which much water was flowing. He was amazed by it, so Allah, the Exalted, gave it speech. It said, 'Since I heard His saying, "Its fuel is people and stones," I weep from fear of it.' He asked it to seek refuge for him from the Fire, so it did. Then he saw it after a period in the same state and said, 'Why do you weep now?' It said, 'That was weeping of fear, and this is weeping of gratitude and joy.' The heart of the servant is like stone, or harder, and its hardness does not depart except by weeping in states of both fear and gratitude. And it is narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he said: "It will be proclaimed on the Day of Resurrection, 'Let the praisers stand.' So a group will stand, and a banner will be erected for them, and they will enter Paradise." It was said, "Who are the praisers?" He said, "Those who thank Allah, the Exalted, in every circumstance." In another wording: "Those who thank Allah in ease and hardship." And he, peace be upon him, said: "Praise is the cloak of the Most Merciful." And Allah, the Exalted, revealed to Job, peace be upon him: "I am pleased with gratitude as recompense for My allies," in a lengthy discourse. And Allah, the Exalted, also revealed to him regarding the attribute of the patient that their abode is the Abode of Peace; when they enter it, He inspires them with gratitude, which is the best of speech, and at gratitude, He increases them more, and by looking at His increase. And when what was revealed about treasures was revealed, 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said, "What wealth should we acquire?" He, peace be upon him, said, "Let one of you acquire a remembering tongue or a grateful heart." So he commanded acquiring a grateful heart instead of wealth. And Ibn Mas'ud said, "Gratitude is half of faith."

(Explanation of the Definition and Reality of Gratitude)
Know that gratitude is among the stations of the wayfarers, and it also comprises knowledge, state, and action. Knowledge is the foundation, which begets the state, and the state begets action. As for knowledge, it is recognition of the blessing from the Bestower. The state is the joy resulting from His bestowal. The action is the fulfillment of what is intended and beloved by the Bestower. That action pertains to the heart, the limbs, and the tongue. All of that must be explained so that comprehension of the reality of gratitude is achieved through their combination, for everything said in defining gratitude falls short of encompassing the perfection of its meanings. The first foundation: knowledge, which is knowledge of three matters specifically: the blessing itself, the aspect by which it is a blessing for him, and the essence of the Bestower and the existence of His attributes through which bestowal is perfected and issued from Him upon him. For there must be a blessing, a Bestower, and one upon whom the blessing is bestowed, to whom the blessing reaches from the Bestower by intent and will. These matters must be known. This is regarding other than Allah, the Exalted. As for regarding Allah, the Exalted, it is not complete except by knowing that all blessings are from Allah, and He is the Bestower.

The intermediaries are subjugated by His command, and this knowledge lies beyond sanctification and divine unity, for sanctification and divine unity are encompassed within it. Indeed, the first rank in the knowledge of faith is sanctification. Then, when one recognizes a sacred essence, he knows that there is none sanctified except the One, and all else is not sanctified—this is divine unity. Then he learns that everything in the universe exists solely from that One, so all is a blessing from Him. This knowledge falls into the third rank, as it enfolds within it, along with sanctification and divine unity, the perfection of power and exclusive agency. Concerning this, the Messenger of God ﷺ expressed when he said: "Whoever says 'Glory be to God' receives ten good deeds, and whoever says 'There is no god but God' receives twenty good deeds, and whoever says 'Praise be to God' receives thirty good deeds." And he ﷺ said: "The best remembrance is 'There is no god but God,' and the best supplication is 'Praise be to God.'" And he said: "No remembrance is multiplied as 'Praise be to God' is multiplied." Do not suppose that these good deeds correspond merely to moving the tongue with these words without their meanings taking root in the heart. For 'Glory be to God' is a phrase indicating sanctification, 'There is no god but God' is a phrase indicating divine unity, and 'Praise be to God' is a phrase indicating gratitude for blessings from the One True God. The good deeds correspond to these knowledges, which are among the gates of faith and certainty.

Know that the completion of this knowledge lies in negating partnership in actions. For if a king among kings bestows a favor upon someone with something, and that person sees that his minister or agent had a role in facilitating and delivering it to him, this is associating partners with the king in the blessing. Thus, he does not see the blessing as entirely from the king, but partly from him and partly from another, dividing his joy between them, and he is not a monotheist in relation to the king. However, it does not diminish his monotheism regarding the king or the perfection of his gratitude to recognize that the blessing reached him through the decree written with his pen and on the paper he wrote upon, for he does not rejoice in the pen and paper nor thank them, because he does not attribute to them any independent role as self-existing entities, but rather as instruments subjugated under the king's power. He may also know that the delivering agent and the treasurer are compelled by the king's command in the delivery, and that if the matter were referred to him without the king's authority, he would face coercion and a decisive order whose consequences he fears, and thus he would not hand over anything. When one knows this, his view of the delivering treasurer is like his view of the pen and paper, and this does not lead to partnership in his monotheism by attributing the blessing to the king. The same applies to the scribe. Indeed, animals with free will are subjugated in their very choice, for God Almighty is the One who imposes motives upon them to act, whether they will or not, like the compelled treasurer who finds no way to disobey the king. If left to himself, he would not give you a speck of what is in his hand. Thus, everyone through whom a blessing from God Almighty reaches you is compelled, for God has imposed the will upon him, stirred motives within him, and placed in his heart that his good in this world and the next lies in giving you what he gave, and that his desired objective in status and wealth is not attained except through it. After God has created this belief in him, he finds no way to abandon it. Therefore, he gives you for his own purpose, not for yours. If he had no purpose in giving, he would not give, and if he did not know that his benefit lies in your benefit, he would not benefit you. Thus, he seeks his own benefit through benefiting you; he is not a benefactor to you but rather takes you as a means to another blessing he hopes for. The One who has bestowed favor upon you is He who subjugated him for you and placed in his heart beliefs and desires that compel him to deliver to you. If you understand matters thus, you have known God Almighty and His action, and you are a monotheist, capable of thanking Him. Indeed, with this knowledge alone, you are grateful. For this reason, Moses, peace be upon him, said in his intimate discourse: "My God, You created Adam with Your hand and did such and such, so how can I thank You?" God Almighty said: "He knew that all of that is from Me, so his knowledge was gratitude." Therefore, you do not give thanks except by knowing that all is from Him. If doubt assails you in this, you are not knowledgeable of the blessing nor the Benefactor, so you do not rejoice in the Benefactor alone but also in others. With the deficiency of your knowledge, your state of joy diminishes, and with the deficiency of your joy, your action diminishes. This is the explanation of this principle.

The second principle: The state derived from the root of knowledge, which is joy in the Benefactor with an attitude of submission and humility. This in itself is gratitude in its pure form, just as knowledge is gratitude, but it only becomes gratitude when it fulfills its condition. Its condition is that your joy be in the Benefactor, not in the blessing nor in the act of bestowal. Perhaps this is difficult for you to comprehend, so we present an example: A king who intends to depart on a journey bestows a horse upon a person. It can be imagined that the recipient rejoices in the horse from three aspects:

The first is when one rejoices in the horse merely because it is a horse, as property to benefit from, a mount that suits his purpose, and a noble steed of value. This is the joy of one who has no regard for the king; his desire is solely for the horse. Had he found it in a wilderness and taken it, his joy would be akin to that joy. The second aspect is when one rejoices in it not because it is a horse, but because it serves as evidence of the king's care for him, his compassion toward him, and his concern for his standing. Had he found this horse in a wilderness or received it from someone other than the king, he would not rejoice in it at all, either because he has no need for the horse whatsoever or because he deems it insignificant compared to his objective of attaining a place in the king's heart. The third aspect is when one rejoices in it in order to ride it to go out in service to the king and endure the hardship of travel to attain closeness to him through that service, perhaps even rising to the rank of vizier. For he is not content merely that his place in the king's heart is such that the king gives him a horse and shows him this measure of care; rather, he desires that the king bestow no favor from his wealth upon anyone except through his mediation. Moreover, he does not desire the vizierate for the sake of the vizierate itself, but desires to behold the king and be near him, such that if he were given the choice between closeness without the vizierate and the vizierate without closeness, he would choose closeness. These are three degrees.

The first involves no meaning of gratitude whatsoever, because its possessor's consideration is confined to the horse; his joy is in the horse, not in the Giver. This is the condition of everyone who rejoices in a blessing because it is pleasurable and conforms to his desire—he is far from the meaning of gratitude. The second enters into the meaning of gratitude because he rejoices in the Benefactor, yet not for His Essence, but for the awareness of His care that prompts Him to bestow favors in the future. This is the condition of the righteous who worship God and thank Him out of fear of His punishment and hope for His reward. However, complete gratitude lies in the third joy, which is that the servant's joy in the blessing of God Almighty stems from being enabled by it to draw near to Him, to abide in His proximity, and to gaze upon His Face perpetually. This is the highest rank. Its sign is that he rejoices in nothing of this world except what is a seedbed for the Hereafter and assists him in it, and he grieves over any blessing that distracts him from the remembrance of God Almighty and turns him away from His path. For he does not desire the blessing because it is pleasurable, as the one who desires the horse desires it because it is a noble and swift steed, but rather because it carries him in the company of the king so that his beholding him and closeness to him may endure. Therefore, al-Shibli, mercy of God upon him, said: "Gratitude is seeing the Benefactor, not seeing the blessing." And al-Khawwas, mercy of God upon him, said: "The gratitude of the common folk is for food, clothing, and drink, while the gratitude of the elect is for what enters the hearts." This is a rank not attained by anyone whose pleasures are confined to the belly and private parts and the perceptions of the senses—colors and sounds—and who is devoid of the heart's delight. For the heart, in a state of health, finds delight only in the remembrance of God Almighty, knowledge of Him, and meeting Him. It delights in other than Him only when it is sick through corrupt habits, just as some people delight in eating clay, and just as some sick persons find sweet things repulsive and bitter things delicious, as it is said:
"And whoever has a sick, bitter mouth / Finds even pure water bitter."
Thus, this is the condition for rejoicing in the blessing of God Almighty. If this is not attained, then there is the second degree. As for the first, it is outside all reckoning. For how great is the difference between one who desires the king for the horse and one who desires the horse for the king! And how great is the difference between one who desires God that He may bestow favors upon him and one who desires the favors of God that he may reach Him through them!

The third principle: Acting in accordance with the joy arising from knowledge of the Benefactor. This action pertains to the heart, the tongue, and the limbs. As for the heart: intending good and wishing it for all creation. As for the tongue: manifesting gratitude to God Almighty through praises that indicate it. As for the limbs: employing the blessings of God Almighty in obeying Him and guarding against using them to aid in disobeying Him. So much so that the gratitude of the eyes is to conceal every fault they see in a Muslim, and the gratitude of the ears is to conceal every fault they hear about him. This enters into the totality of thanking God Almighty for these limbs. Gratitude with the tongue is to manifest contentment with God Almighty, and it is commanded. For the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to a man: "How are you this morning?" The man said: "Well." He repeated the question until on the third time the man said: "Well, I praise God and thank Him." The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "This is what I wanted from you." The early generations would inquire after one another with the intention of eliciting gratitude to God, so that the one thanking would be obedient and the one prompting him to it would be obedient. Their aim was not ostentation by displaying longing. Every servant asked about his condition is between thanking and complaining; if he remains silent, then gratitude is obedience and complaint is disobedience—ugly from the people of religion. And how could complaint to a king not be ugly?

Kings, who hold all things in their hands, to a servant who owns nothing and can do nothing? It is more fitting for the servant, if he cannot endure affliction and divine decree with grace, and weakness leads him to complain, that his complaint be directed to God Almighty. For He is the One who afflicts and has the power to remove affliction. The servant's humility before his Master is glory, while complaining to other than Him is disgrace. Displaying one's lowliness to a servant, who is himself a servant like you, is an ugly disgrace. God Almighty says: "Indeed, those you worship besides God do not possess for you [the power of] provision. So seek provision from God and worship Him and be grateful to Him." And He says: "Indeed, those you invoke besides God are servants like you." Gratitude expressed by the tongue is part of gratitude. It has been narrated that a delegation came to 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, may God have mercy on him. A young man stood to speak, so 'Umar said, "Seniority, seniority!" The young man said, "O Commander of the Faithful, if the matter were by age, there are among the Muslims those older than you." He said, "Speak." The young man said, "We are not a delegation of desire nor a delegation of fear. As for desire, your generosity has already delivered it to us. As for fear, your justice has secured us from it. We have only come to you to give thanks; we thank you with our tongues and depart." These are the foundational meanings of gratitude that encompass the totality of its reality. As for the statement of one who said that gratitude is the acknowledgment of the benefactor's favor in a manner of humility, this looks to the action of the tongue along with some states of the heart. The statement of one who said that gratitude is praising the benefactor by mentioning his kindness looks merely to the action of the tongue. The statement of one who said that gratitude is devotion upon the carpet of witnessing through constant preservation of sanctity gathers most meanings of gratitude, excepting only the action of the tongue. The statement of Hamdun al-Qassar, "Gratitude for a blessing is that you see yourself in gratitude as a parasite," points to the fact that the meaning of recognition is among the meanings of gratitude only. The statement of al-Junayd, "Gratitude is that you do not see yourself as worthy of the blessing," points to a specific state of the heart. These statements express their authors' conditions, hence their answers differ and do not agree. Moreover, the answer of each one may differ in two states, for they speak only from their present, predominant condition, occupied with what concerns them over what does not, or they speak with what they see as suitable to the questioner's condition, limiting themselves to mentioning the amount needed and turning away from what is not needed. Therefore, you should not think that what we have mentioned is a criticism of them, or that if all the meanings we have explained were presented to them, they would deny them. Indeed, no rational person would think so at all, unless there is a dispute regarding the term—whether the name 'gratitude' in linguistic convention encompasses all these meanings or applies to some of them as the primary intent, while the remaining meanings are among its concomitants and necessities. We do not intend in this book to explain linguistic subjects, for that has nothing to do with the knowledge of the path to the Hereafter. And God grants success through His mercy.

(Clarifying the way to remove the veil from gratitude in relation to God Almighty)

Perhaps it occurs to your mind that gratitude is only done for a benefactor who has a share in the gratitude, for we thank kings either with praise to increase their station in hearts and manifest their generosity among people, thereby increasing their fame and prestige; or with service, which is an aid to them for some of their aims; or by presenting ourselves before them in the form of service, which multiplies their retinue and is a cause for increasing their prestige. Thus, they are not thanked except with something of this sort. This is impossible in relation to God Almighty for two reasons: First, God Almighty is transcendent above shares and aims, sanctified from need for service and aid, and from spreading prestige and dignity through praise and extolling, and from multiplying the retinue of servants by presenting oneself before Him bowing and prostrating. So our thanking Him with that in which there is no share resembles our thanking a king who has bestowed favor upon us by sleeping in our houses or prostrating or bowing, since there is no share in it for the king who is absent, having no knowledge of it, and there is no share for God Almighty in all our actions. The second reason is that everything we undertake by our choice is another blessing from God's blessings upon us, for our limbs, our capability, our will, our motive, and all the matters that are the causes of our movement, and the movement itself, are from the creation and favor of God Almighty. So how can we thank one blessing with another? If a king gave us a mount, and we took another mount belonging to him and rode it, or the king gave us another mount, the second would not be gratitude from us for the first. Rather, the second would itself require gratitude just as the first does. Then gratitude for gratitude is only possible through another blessing, leading to gratitude being impossible in relation to God Almighty from these two perspectives. Yet we have no doubt about both matters, and the Sacred Law has come with it. So what is the way to reconcile? Know that this thought occurred to David, peace be upon him.

Likewise, to Moses, peace be upon him, he said: "O Lord, how can I thank You when I am unable to thank You except through a second favor from Your favors?" And in another wording: "And my gratitude to You is another favor from You, obliging me to gratitude toward You." So God Almighty revealed to him: "If you have recognized this, then you have thanked Me." And in another report: "If you have recognized that the favor is from Me, I am pleased with you for that as gratitude."

If you say: "I have understood the question, but my understanding falls short of grasping the meaning of what was revealed to them. For I know the impossibility of thanking God Almighty. However, I do not understand how the knowledge of this impossibility constitutes gratitude, for this knowledge is also a favor from Him. So how did it become gratitude? It is as if the outcome reverts to the idea that whoever has not thanked has indeed thanked, and that accepting the second robe from the king is gratitude for the first robe. My understanding is insufficient to grasp the secret therein. If it is possible to explain this with an example, it is important in itself."

Know then that this knocks on a door of spiritual knowledges, which are higher than the sciences of transaction. Yet we shall point from them to glimpses and say: Here are two perspectives. The first perspective is with the eye of pure monotheism. This perspective will certainly make you know that He is the One who gives thanks, and He is the One thanked; He is the Lover, and He is the Beloved. This is the perspective of one who knows that there is none in existence but Him, and that everything perishes except His Face, and that this is true in every state, eternally and forever. For the "other" is that which is imagined to have subsistence by itself, and such an "other" has no existence; rather, it is impossible for it to exist. For the true existent is that which subsists by itself, and that which has no subsistence by itself has no existence by itself; rather, it subsists through another. Thus it exists through another. If its essence is considered without regard to another, it has no existence whatsoever. The existent is only that which subsists by itself, and that which subsists by itself is that which, were the nonexistence of another conceived, would remain existent. If, along with subsisting by itself, the existence of another subsists through its existence, then it is the Sustainer, and there is no Sustainer except One, and it is inconceivable to be otherwise. Therefore, there is in existence no "other" than the Ever-Living, the Sustainer, who is the One, the Eternal. So when you look from this station, you know that all originates from Him and returns to Him. Thus He is the One who gives thanks, and He is the One thanked; He is the Lover, and He is the Beloved. From here is the perspective of Habib ibn Abi Habib when he recited: "Indeed, We found him patient. An excellent servant! Indeed, he was one repeatedly turning back [to Us]." He said: "How wondrous! He gave and praised," indicating that when He praises His giving, He praises Himself. He is the Praiser and the One praised.

From here is the perspective of Shaykh Abu Sa'id al-Mihani when it was recited before him: "He loves them, and they love Him." He said: "By my life, He loves them, and let Him love them! By right, He loves them, for He only loves Himself," alluding by this that He is the Lover and He is the Beloved. This is a high station that you will not understand except through an example within the scope of your intellect. So it should not be hidden from you that when an author loves his composition, he has loved himself; when a craftsman loves his craft, he has loved himself; when a parent loves his child insofar as he is his child, he has loved himself. And all that exists besides God Almighty is the composition of God Almighty and His craft. So if He loves it, He loves nothing but Himself. And if He does not love Himself, then by right He loves what He loves, and this is what He loves. All of this is the perspective with the eye of monotheism. The Sufis express this state as the annihilation of the self—that is, he annihilated from himself and from other than God, so he saw nothing but God Almighty. Whoever does not understand this denies them and says: "How has he annihilated when his shadow's length is four cubits, and perhaps he eats pounds of bread every day?" Thus the ignorant laugh at them due to their ignorance of the meanings of their speech, and it is necessary for the knowers to be a laughingstock for the ignorant. To this is the allusion in His saying, exalted is He: "Indeed, those who committed crimes used to laugh at those who believed. And when they passed by them, they would exchange derisive glances. And when they returned to their people, they would return jesting. And when they saw them, they would say, 'Indeed, those are truly lost.' But they had not been sent as guardians over them." Then He clarified that the laughter of the knowers at them tomorrow is greater, as He said, exalted is He: "So today those who believed are laughing at the disbelievers, on couches, observing." Likewise, the people of Noah, peace be upon him, used to laugh at him when he was occupied with building the ark. He said: "If you ridicule us, then we will ridicule you just as you ridicule." So this is one of the two perspectives.

The second perspective is that of one who has not attained the station of annihilation from himself. These are of two kinds: a kind who affirmed only the existence of themselves and denied that they have a Lord to worship. These are the inverted blind, and their blindness is in both eyes, for they denied what is truly established—the Sustainer, who subsists by Himself and oversees every soul for what it has earned, and every subsisting thing subsists through Him. They did not limit themselves to this but even affirmed themselves. Had they known, they would have realized that from the standpoint of being themselves, they have no stability and no existence. Their existence is from the standpoint of being brought into existence, not from the standpoint of being existent. There is a difference between the existent and the One who brings into existence.

There is no existence except one Existent and one Originator. Thus the Existent is real, and the Originator is unreal from the perspective of its own essence. The Existent is Self-Subsisting and Self-Sustaining, while the originator is perishable and vanishing. Since everything upon it perishes, nothing remains except the Countenance of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor. The second group are not blind, but they are one-eyed, for they see with one eye the existence of the True Existent and do not deny it. Yet if the other eye were to open from its blindness, they would not perceive through it the annihilation of anything other than the True Existent. Thus they affirm another existent alongside God Almighty, and this is pure polytheism, just as the stance before it was pure denial. If one passes beyond the limit of blindness to dim-sightedness, one perceives a distinction between the two existents, affirming a servant and a Lord. With this measure of affirming distinction and deficiency in the other existent, one enters the precinct of Divine Oneness. Then, if one applies kohl to his insight with what increases its light, his dim-sightedness diminishes. In proportion to the increase in his insight, the deficiency of what he affirmed besides God Almighty becomes apparent to him. If he continues his journey thus, the deficiency will inevitably lead him to effacement, so he becomes effaced from seeing anything besides God, seeing nothing but God, thereby attaining the perfection of Oneness. Wherever one perceives deficiency in the existence of anything besides God Almighty, one enters the beginnings of Oneness. Between these two are countless degrees; thus vary the ranks of the affirmers of Oneness. The revealed Books of God upon the tongues of His messengers are the kohl by which the lights of insight are attained, and the prophets are the appliers of kohl. They came calling to pure Oneness, its translation being the statement "There is no god but God," its meaning that nothing is seen but the One True Reality. Those who reach the perfection of Oneness are the fewest, and the deniers and polytheists are also few, being at the farthest extreme opposite the extreme of Oneness, for the idol-worshippers said, "We worship them only that they may bring us nearer to God in proximity," thus being within the first gates of Oneness, albeit with a weak entry. The intermediate are the majority. Among them are those whose inner sight opens in some states, so the realities of Oneness flash to them, but like a fleeting lightning bolt, it does not remain. Among them are those to whom it flashes and remains for a time, but does not endure, and endurance therein is rare: "For every seeker of the heights are movements, but rare among men is steadfastness."

When God Almighty commanded His Prophet to seek nearness, and it was said to him, "Prostrate and draw near," he said in his prostration: "I seek refuge in Your pardon from Your punishment, and I seek refuge in Your pleasure from Your displeasure, and I seek refuge in You from You. I cannot enumerate praise of You; You are as You have praised Yourself." His statement, "I seek refuge in Your pardon from Your punishment," is speech arising from witnessing only God's acts, as if he saw nothing but God and His acts, so he sought refuge in His act from His act. Then he drew nearer and was annihilated from witnessing the acts, ascending to the sources of the acts, which are the attributes, and said: "I seek refuge in Your pleasure from Your displeasure"—these being two attributes. Then he saw that as a deficiency in Oneness, so he drew nearer and ascended from the station of witnessing the attributes to witnessing the Essence, saying: "And I seek refuge in You from You." This is fleeing from Him to Him, without seeing act or attribute. But he saw himself fleeing from Him to Him, seeking refuge and praising, so he was annihilated from witnessing himself, seeing that as a deficiency, and drew nearer, saying: "I cannot enumerate praise of You; You are as You have praised Yourself." His statement, "I cannot enumerate," is a report of the annihilation of his self and emergence from witnessing it. His statement, "You are as You have praised Yourself," clarifies that He is the One praised and the One upon whom praise is bestowed, that all begins from Him and to Him returns, and that "Everything will perish except His Countenance." Thus, his first station was the ultimate station of the affirmers of Oneness, which is to see nothing but God Almighty and His acts, seeking refuge in one act from another. Consider then to what his ultimate end concluded, for it concluded with the One True Reality until there rose from his sight and witnessing anything besides the True Essence. He would not ascend from one rank to another without seeing the former as distant in comparison to the latter, so he would seek God's forgiveness for the former, seeing it as a deficiency in his journey and a shortcoming in his station. To this is the allusion in his saying: "Indeed, a veil comes over my heart until I seek God's forgiveness seventy times a day and night." This was for ascension through seventy stations, some above others; the first, even though it surpassed the furthest limits of creation, was a deficiency in comparison to the last, so his seeking forgiveness was for that. When Aisha, may God be pleased with her, said, "Has God not forgiven you your past and future sins? What is this weeping in prostration and this intense striving?" He said, "Should I not be a thankful servant?" meaning, "Should I not be a seeker of increase in stations?" For thankfulness is a cause of increase, as God Almighty said: "If you are grateful, I will surely increase you." If we delve into the oceans of unveiling, let us rein in the reins and return to what befits the sciences of spiritual conduct. We say: The prophets...

Upon them be peace, they were sent to call to the truth of perfect divine unity as we have described. However, between them and the attainment of it lies a great distance and formidable obstacles. The entirety of the Sacred Law is but a definition of the path for traversing that distance and overcoming those obstacles. At that point, perception arises from another witnessing and another station. In that station, in addition to that witnessing, gratitude, the grateful one, and the One thanked become manifest. This can only be known by an example. I say: You can understand that if a king sent to a servant who was far from him a mount, a garment, and provisions for the journey, so that by them he might traverse the distance of separation and draw near to the king's presence, then there are two possibilities for the servant. The first is that the king's purpose in the servant reaching his presence is for him to perform some of his important tasks and to have a share in serving him. The second is that the king has no personal interest in the servant, nor any need of him. Rather, his presence adds nothing to his kingdom, for he is incapable of performing a service that would benefit him in any meaningful way, and his absence detracts nothing from his kingdom. Thus, the purpose of bestowing the mount and provisions upon him is so that the servant may attain the blessing of proximity to him and obtain the felicity of his presence, for the servant's own benefit, not for the king to benefit from him or his service. The station of the servants with God, Exalted is He, is the second station, not the first, for the first is impossible for God, Exalted is He, and the second is not impossible. Know then that the servant in the first scenario is not grateful merely by riding and arriving at his presence, unless he performs the service the king desired from him. As for the second scenario, he has no need for service at all. Yet, it is conceivable that he could be either grateful or ungrateful. His gratitude would be by using what his Master has sent to him for what He loves, for His sake, not for his own sake. His ingratitude would be by not using it for that purpose, either by neglecting it or by using it in a way that increases his distance from Him. Whenever the servant wears the garment, rides the steed, and spends the provisions only on the path, he has shown gratitude to his Master, for he has used His favor in what He loves—that is, in what He loves for His servant, not for Himself. If he rides it and turns his back on His presence, moving away from Him, he has been ungrateful for His favor—that is, he has used it in what his Master dislikes for His servant, not for Himself. If he sits and does not ride, neither seeking proximity nor seeking distance, he has also been ungrateful for His favor by neglecting and wasting it, though this is less severe than actively distancing himself. Similarly, God, Glorified is He, created creation, and they, in the beginning of their primordial nature, need to use their appetites to perfect their bodies, yet by them they distance themselves from His presence. Their felicity lies in proximity to Him. So He has prepared for them from His favors that which they can use to attain the degree of proximity. Concerning their distance and proximity, God, Exalted is He, has said: "We have certainly created man in the best of stature; then We return him to the lowest of the low, except for those who believe" (Quran 95:4-6). Therefore, the favors of God, Exalted is He, are instruments by which the servant ascends from the lowest of the low. God, Exalted is He, created them for the sake of the servant so that he may attain by them the felicity of proximity. God, Exalted is He, is independent of him, whether near or far. The servant, regarding these favors, is either to use them in obedience, thus being grateful by conforming to what his Master loves, or to use them in disobedience, thus being ungrateful by plunging into what his Master dislikes and does not approve for him, for God does not approve disbelief and disobedience for His servants. If he neglects them and does not use them in either obedience or disobedience, that too is ingratitude—ingratitude for the favor through waste. Everything created in this world was created as an instrument for the servant so that he may attain through it the felicity of the Hereafter and the attainment of proximity to God, Exalted is He. Thus, every obedient person is, to the extent of his obedience, grateful for God's favor in the means he used for obedience. Every slothful person who abandoned their use, or every disobedient person who used them on the path of distance, is ungrateful, straying outside the love of God, Exalted is He. Disobedience and obedience are both encompassed by the Divine Will, but they are not both encompassed by Divine Love and Dislike. For a willed thing may be beloved, and a willed thing may be disliked. Beyond the clarification of this subtle point lies the secret of Divine Decree, which has been prohibited from being divulged. By this, the first difficulty is resolved—namely, if the One thanked has no personal interest, how can there be gratitude? By this, the second is also resolved, for we intended by gratitude nothing other than the channeling of God's favor in the direction of God's love. When the favor is channeled in the direction of love by God's act, the purpose is achieved. Your action is a gift from God, Exalted is He, and from your perspective as its locus, He has praised you, and His praise is another favor from Him to you. Thus, He is the One who gives and He is the One who praises. One of His acts becomes a cause for the channeling of His second act toward the direction of His love. So to Him belongs gratitude in every circumstance, and you are described as being grateful in the sense that you are the locus of the meaning which gratitude expresses, not in the sense that you are its necessitating cause—just as you are described as being knowing and learned, not in the sense that you are the creator or originator of knowledge, but rather...

In meaning, you are a locus for Him, and He has found through the eternal power in you, so describing you as being grateful affirms a thingness for you. And you are a thing since the Creator of things made you a thing. Yet you are truly nothing if you suppose yourself to be something from your own essence. As for considering the view toward Him who made things into things, you are a thing since He made you a thing. But if the view is cut off from His making, you are nothing in reality. To this He, peace be upon him, alluded when he said: “Work, for everyone is facilitated for what he was created for.” This was when it was said to him, O Messenger of God, “Then why work if things have already been concluded beforehand?” Thus it became clear that creation are the courses of God’s power, exalted is He, and the loci of His acts—even though they themselves are also from His acts—but some of His acts are the locus for others. And His saying “Work,” even though it proceeds upon the tongue of the Messenger, peace be upon him, is an act from His acts, and it is a cause for the creation’s knowing that work is beneficial. And their knowing is an act from the acts of God, exalted is He, and knowledge is a cause for the arising of a decisive motive toward movement and obedience. And the arising of the motive is also from the acts of God, exalted is He, and it is a cause for the movement of the limbs, which are also from the acts of God, exalted is He. But some of His acts are a cause for others—that is, the first is a condition for the second, just as creating the body was a cause for creating the accident, since the accident is not created before it; and creating life is a condition for creating knowledge; and creating knowledge is a condition for creating will; and all are from the acts of God, exalted is He, and some are a cause for others. That is, it is a condition, and the meaning of its being a condition is that nothing is prepared to receive the act of life except a substance; and nothing is prepared to receive knowledge except one possessing life; and nothing is prepared to receive will except one possessing knowledge. Thus some of His acts are a cause for others in this sense—not in the sense that some of His acts bring others into existence, but rather that they prepare the condition for the occurrence of others. And when this is realized, one ascends to the degree of unification that we have mentioned.

If you say: Then why did God, exalted is He, say “Work, otherwise you will be punished, blamed for disobedience,” when nothing is up to us? How can we be blamed when everything belongs to God, exalted is He? Know that this statement from God, exalted is He, is a cause for the attainment of a belief within us, and belief is a cause for the stirring of fear, and the stirring of fear is a cause for abandoning desires and turning away from the abode of delusion, and that is a cause for arriving at the proximity of God. And God, exalted is He, is the Causer of causes and their Arranger. So for whom happiness was decreed in eternity, He facilitates these causes for him until they lead him by their chain to Paradise. And its like is expressed by “everyone is facilitated for what he was created for.” And for whom the good was not decreed by God, he is kept from hearing the speech of God, exalted is He, and the speech of His Messenger, peace be upon him, and the speech of the scholars. So if he does not hear, he does not know; and if he does not know, he does not fear; and if he does not fear, he does not abandon reliance on this world; and if he does not abandon reliance on this world, he remains in the party of Satan—and indeed Hell is their promised place, all together. So when you know this, you will marvel at a people who are led to Paradise by chains. There is no one except that he is led to Paradise by the chains of causes, which is the imposition of knowledge and fear upon him. And there is no forsaken one except that he is led to the Fire by chains, which is the imposition of heedlessness, false security, and delusion upon him. Thus the God-fearing are driven to Paradise by compulsion, and the criminals are dragged to the Fire by compulsion. And there is no compeller except God, the One, the Subduer; and there is no powerful one except the Sovereign, the Compeller. And when the veil is lifted from the eyes of the heedless and they witness the matter as such, they will then hear the call of the caller: “To whom belongs the dominion this Day? To God, the One, the Subduer.” And indeed the dominion belonged to God, the One, the Subduer, every day—not that day in particular—but the heedless do not hear this call except on that Day. So it is news of what is newly revealed to the heedless from the uncovering of states, when the uncovering will not benefit them. So we seek refuge with God, the Forbearing, the Generous, from ignorance and blindness, for it is the root of the causes of perdition.

(Clarification of Distinguishing What God Loves from What He Hates)

Know that the act of thankfulness and the abandonment of ingratitude are not complete except by knowing what God, exalted is He, loves from what He hates. For the meaning of thankfulness is using His blessings, exalted is He, in what He loves, and the meaning of ingratitude is the opposite of that—either by abandoning their use or by using them in what He hates. And for distinguishing what God, exalted is He, loves from what He hates, there are two means of perception: one is hearing, whose basis is the verses and reports. The second is the insight of the heart, which is looking with the eye of consideration. This latter is difficult and, because of that, rare. Therefore, God, exalted is He, sent the messengers and made the path easy for creation through them. And knowing this is built upon knowing all the rulings of the Sacred Law regarding the acts of the servants. So whoever does not become acquainted with the rulings of the Sacred Law in all his actions cannot possibly fulfill the right of thankfulness at all. As for the second, which is looking with the eye of consideration, it is perceiving the wisdom of God, exalted is He, in every existent He created, for He did not create anything in the world except that there is wisdom in it, and beneath the wisdom...

The intended purpose is the beloved, and that wisdom is divided into manifest and hidden. As for the manifest, such as knowing that the wisdom in creating the sun is to achieve through it the distinction between night and day, so that day becomes a livelihood and night a garment, thus facilitating movement during visibility and rest during concealment. This is among the wisdoms of the sun, not all of its wisdoms, for it contains many other subtle wisdoms. Likewise, knowing the wisdom in clouds and the descent of rain, which is for the earth to split with various plants as sustenance for creation and pasture for cattle. The Qur'an encompasses a totality of magnificent wisdoms that the understandings of creation can bear, not the subtle ones they fall short of comprehending, as God Almighty said: "We poured down water in torrents, then We split the earth asunder, and caused to grow therein grain, and grapes" (Qur'an 80:25-28). As for the wisdom in all the celestial bodies, both the wandering planets and the fixed stars, it is hidden, not disclosed to all of creation. The extent that the understanding of creation can bear is that they are an adornment for the heaven so that the eye may delight in gazing upon them, as indicated by His saying, Almighty: "We have adorned the lowest heaven with the adornment of the stars" (Qur'an 37:6). Thus, all parts of the world—its heaven, stars, winds, seas, mountains, minerals, plants, animals, and the limbs of animals—not a single atom among its atoms is devoid of many wisdoms, from one to ten to a thousand to ten thousand. Similarly, the limbs of an animal are divided, except for what is known of their wisdom, such as knowing that the eye is for sight, not for striking; the hand for striking, not for walking; and the foot for walking, not for smelling. As for the internal organs—the intestines, gallbladder, liver, kidney, individual veins, nerves, muscles, and what they contain of cavities, convolutions, intertwinings, deviations, fineness, thickness, and all other attributes—their wisdom is not known by most people. Those who know them know only a small amount in comparison to what is in the knowledge of God Almighty: "You have been given but little knowledge" (Qur'an 17:85). Therefore, whoever uses something in a direction other than the one for which it was created, and not in the manner intended for it, has indeed been ungrateful for the blessing of God Almighty. Thus, whoever strikes another with his hand has been ungrateful for the blessing of the hand, for the hand was created for him to repel with it what would destroy him and to take what benefits him, not to destroy another with it. And whoever looks at a face that is not forbidden has been ungrateful for the blessing of the eye and the blessing of the sun, for sight is accomplished through them, and they were created only to see with them what benefits him in his religion and his worldly life and to guard with them against what harms him in both. He has used them for other than what was intended. This is because the purpose of creating creation and creating the world and its means is for creation to be aided by them in attaining God Almighty, and there is no attainment of Him except through love of Him and intimacy with Him in this world, and turning away from the deception of the world. There is no intimacy except through constant remembrance, and no love except through the knowledge attained through constant reflection. Constant remembrance and reflection are not possible except through the permanence of the body, and the body does not remain except through nourishment, and nourishment is not complete except through the earth, water, and air, and that is not complete except through the creation of the heaven and the earth and the creation of all limbs, external and internal. All of that is for the sake of the body, and the body is the mount of the soul, and what returns to God Almighty is the soul at peace through prolonged worship and knowledge. Therefore, God Almighty said: "I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me. I seek no provision from them" (Qur'an 51:56-57). Thus, whoever uses something in other than obedience to God has been ungrateful for the blessing of God in all the necessary means that enabled him to commit that disobedience. To mention a single example of the hidden wisdoms that are not in the utmost concealment, so that you may reflect upon it and know the way of gratitude and ingratitude for blessings, we say: Among the blessings of God Almighty is the creation of dirhams and dinars, through which the world is sustained. They are two stones with no inherent benefit in their essences, but creation is compelled to them because every person is in need of many tangible things for his food, clothing, and all his needs. He may be incapable of obtaining what he needs while possessing what he can do without, such as one who possesses saffron, for example, while needing a camel to ride, and one who possesses a camel may have no need for it but needs saffron. An exchange between them is necessary, and a valuation of the equivalent is necessary, for the owner of the camel will not give his camel for any amount of saffron, and there is no correlation between saffron and a camel such that one could say to give its equivalent in weight or form. Likewise, one who buys a house with clothes, or a slave with a shoe, or flour with a donkey—these things are not commensurate, so one does not know how much the camel is worth in saffron, making transactions extremely difficult. These disparate, distant tangible things thus required an intermediary.

Between them, He judges with a just ruling, so that from each one his rank and station become known. When the stations are established and the ranks are ordered, then the equivalent is distinguished from the non-equivalent. Thus, Allah the Exalted created dinars and dirhams as arbiters and intermediaries among all forms of wealth, so that properties may be valued by them. It is said: this camel is worth a hundred dinars, and this amount of saffron is worth a hundred. Thus, from the perspective that they are equivalent to one thing, they are equal. Adjustment through the two currencies is possible precisely because there is no inherent desire for their specific forms. If there were desire for their forms, that particular desire might necessitate preference for the one who has that desire, but not for one who has no such desire, and order would not be maintained. Therefore, Allah the Exalted created them to circulate among hands and to be just arbiters between properties, and for another wisdom: to serve as a means to all other things, because they are precious in themselves yet no desire lies in their specific forms, and their relation to all conditions is uniform. Thus, whoever possesses them is as if he possesses everything, unlike one who owns a garment, for he owns only the garment. If he needs food, the owner of the food may not desire the garment, because his desire may be for a mount, for instance. Thus, something is needed which in its form is as if nothing, yet in its meaning is as if all things. A thing’s relation to different matters is equal only when it has no specific form that it confers uniquely—like a mirror that has no color yet reflects every color. Similarly, currency has no inherent desire and is a means to every desire; like a particle that has no meaning in itself yet through it meanings appear in others. This is the second wisdom. In them also lies wisdom too lengthy to mention. So whoever uses them in a manner unbefitting their purpose, indeed opposing the intended aim of their creation, has shown ingratitude for Allah’s blessing in them. Thus, whoever hoards them has wronged them and nullified the wisdom in them, and is like one who imprisons the judge of the Muslims in a prison, preventing him from judging thereby. For by hoarding, he wastes the judgment and the intended purpose is not achieved. Dirhams and dinars were not created for Zayd specifically nor for ‘Amr specifically, since individuals have no desire for their specific forms—they are but stones. Rather, they were created to circulate among hands, so that they may be arbiters among people and a measure for knowing quantities, evaluating the fixed. So Allah the Exalted informed those incapable of reading the divine lines written on the pages of existence in a divine script without letter or sound—which is perceived not with the eye of sight but with the eye of insight—He informed these incapable ones through words they heard from His Messenger (peace be upon him), conveyed to them via letter and sound, the meaning they were unable to grasp. Thus He said: “And those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend it in the way of Allah—give them tidings of a painful punishment.” And whoever makes from dirhams and dinars vessels of gold or silver has shown ingratitude for the blessing and is in a worse state than the hoarder, for this is like one who employs the judge of the land in weaving, tax-collecting, and tasks performed by the lowly among people. Imprisonment is more trivial than that, for pottery, iron, lead, and copper can substitute for gold and silver in containing liquids from spilling; vessels are for preserving liquids, and pottery and iron suffice for the purpose intended for them, but not for the purpose intended for currency. Whoever does not perceive this will perceive it through the divine translation, and it is said to him: “Whoever drinks from a vessel of gold or silver, it is as if he is swallowing the fire of Hell into his belly.” And whoever engages in usurious transactions with dirhams and dinars has shown ingratitude for the blessing and committed wrong, for they were created for other things, not for themselves, since there is no desire in their specific forms. So if one trades in their specific forms, he has taken them as an end contrary to the wisdom of their creation, for seeking currency for other than what it was created for is wrong. He who has a garment but no currency may not be able to buy food or a mount with it, for perhaps food and mounts are not sold for garments. He is excused in selling it for another currency to obtain currency, through which he may attain his aim, for they are means to other things, with no desire in their specific forms. Their position among properties is like the position of particles in speech, as grammarians say: the particle is that which comes for a meaning in something else; and like the position of a mirror among colors. As for one who has currency, if it were permissible for him to sell it for currency and make dealing in currency the ultimate goal of his work, then currency would remain bound with him and assume the status of hoarded wealth. Restricting the judge and the courier who delivers to others is wrong, just as imprisoning him is wrong. Thus, there is no meaning in selling currency for currency except taking currency as an object for hoarding, and that is wrong.

If you say: Why then is it permitted to sell one of the two currencies for the other, and why is it permitted to sell a dirham for its like? Know that...

One of the two currencies contradicts the other in the aim of facilitation, for it may be possible to facilitate with one of them due to its abundance, like dirhams that are dispersed for needs little by little, so prohibiting it disrupts its specific purpose, which is the ease of using it to obtain other things. As for selling a dirham for an identical dirham, it is permissible because no rational person desires it when they are equal, nor does a merchant engage in it, for it is frivolous, akin to placing a dirham on the ground and picking up the same one. We do not fear that rational people would spend their time placing a dirham on the ground and picking up the same one, so we do not prohibit what souls have no inclination toward, unless one is of better quality than the other, which is also inconceivable to occur, since the owner of the good one would not accept its like from the inferior, so the contract would not be valid. If an increase in the inferior is sought, that is something that may be intended, so we rightly prohibit it and rule that its good and bad are equal, because quality and inferiority should be considered in what is intended in its essence, and what has no purpose in its essence should only be considered for subtle additions in its attributes. The one who wronged is the one who struck coins differing in quality and inferiority until they became intended for their essences, while their right is not to be intended. As for selling a dirham for an identical dirham on credit, it is not permitted because only one who is indulgent, intending kindness in a loan, would proceed with this, and it is a virtue that can be dispensed with, so that the form of indulgence remains and he receives praise and reward. In exchange, there is no praise or reward, so it is also wrong because it wastes the particularity of indulgence and brings it into the arena of opposition. Likewise, foods were created to be nourished by or treated with, so they should not be diverted from their purpose, for opening the door of transaction in them necessitates their restriction in hands and delays the eating for which they were intended. God did not create food except to be eaten, and the need for food is intense, so it should pass from the hand of one who has no need to the one in need, and transactions should not be made over food except by one who has no need for it. For whoever has food, why does he not eat it if he is in need, and why does he not make it a commodity for trade? If he makes it a commodity for trade, let him sell it to one who seeks it for a compensation other than food, which he needs. As for one who seeks it for the same food, he also has no need for it, and for this reason, the law has cursed the hoarder and included the strictures we mentioned in the Book of the Etiquettes of Earning. Indeed, the seller of wheat for dates is excused because one does not substitute for the other in purpose, but the seller of a measure of wheat for an identical measure of it is not excused, yet he is frivolous and does not need prohibition because souls do not permit it except when there is disparity in quality, and matching the good with its like from the inferior is not accepted by the owner of the good. As for good for two inferior, it may be intended, but since foods are necessities and the good equals the inferior in the core benefit and differs in aspects of enjoyment, the law disregarded the aim of enjoyment in what is the sustenance. This is the ruling of the law in prohibiting usury, and this has become clear to us after turning away from the art of jurisprudence, so let us attach this to the art of legal rulings, for it is more comprehensive than all we presented in matters of disagreement. By this, the preeminence of Imam al-Shafi'i's school—may God have mercy on him—in specifying foods over measurable items becomes clear, for if plaster were included, then cloth and animals would be more deserving of inclusion. Were it not for salt, the school of Imam Malik—may God have mercy on him—would be the most upright of schools in it, as he specified it for times, but every meaning upheld by the law must be defined by a limit, and defining this was possible with sustenance and possible with what is eaten, so the law saw the definition by the genus of what is eaten as more fitting for all that is essential for survival. The definitions of the law may encompass aspects where the original meaning motivating the ruling is not strong, but the definition occurs thus out of necessity, and if it were not defined, creation would be perplexed in following the essence of the meaning with its variation according to circumstances and individuals, for the exact meaning in its full strength varies with circumstances and individuals, so the limit is necessary. Therefore, God Almighty said: "And whoever transgresses the limits of God has wronged himself." Because the foundations of these meanings do not differ among the laws, but they differ in aspects of definition, as the law of Jesus son of Mary—peace be upon him—defined the prohibition of wine by intoxication, while our law defined it by being of the intoxicating genus, because a little of it leads to much, and what falls within the limits falls within prohibition by the ruling of the genus, just as the original meaning entered through the foundational whole. This is one example of its hidden ruling from the ruling of the two currencies, so gratitude for blessings and ingratitude should be considered by this example. Everything created for a wisdom should be directed toward it, and none knows this except one who has known.

Wisdom—"To whomsoever wisdom is granted, he has been granted abundant good"—yet the jewels of divine judgment do not alight in hearts that are dunghills of desires and playgrounds of devils. Rather, only the possessors of understanding take heed. Therefore, He, exalted is He, said: "Were it not that the devils hover around the hearts of the children of Adam, they would gaze upon the kingdom of the heavens." Once you comprehend this example, apply it to your every movement and stillness, your speech and silence, and every action issuing from you, for it is either gratitude or ingratitude, as it is inconceivable to be free from these two. Some of this is termed in the language of jurisprudence, which the common folk speak of, as "disliked," and some as "perilous," yet all of it is described by the people of hearts as perilous.

I say, for example: if you cleanse yourself with the right hand, you have shown ingratitude for the blessing of the hands, for God created for you two hands and made one stronger than the other, so the stronger, due to its preponderance in most matters, deserves honor and preference.
