To prefer the deficient is a deviation from justice, and God does not command justice then constrain you—He who gave you the hands—to tasks, some noble like taking the Quran, and some base like removing filth. If you take the Quran with the left and remove filth with the right, you have assigned the noble to what is base, thus diminishing its right, wronging it, and deviating from justice. Likewise, if you spit, for instance, toward the direction of prayer or face it while relieving yourself, you have shown ingratitude for the blessing of God, exalted is He, in creating directions and the expanse of the world, for He created directions to be your space in movement and divided them into what He did not ennoble and what He ennobled by placing therein a House, attributing it to Himself to attract your heart toward it, so that your heart may be bound to it, and thereby your body constrained in that direction with composure and dignity when you worship your Lord. Similarly, your actions are divided into what is noble, like acts of obedience, and what is base, like relieving oneself and spitting. If you cast your spittle toward the direction of prayer, you have wronged it and shown ingratitude for the blessing of God, exalted is He, in establishing the qibla, through which the perfection of your worship is achieved.

Likewise, if you put on your shoe beginning with the left, you have wronged, for the shoe is a protection for the foot, so the foot has a share in it, and precedence in shares ought to be given to the more noble—that is justice and fulfillment of wisdom. Its opposite is injustice and ingratitude for the blessing of the shoe and the foot. This, in the view of the knowers, is a major sin, even if the jurist terms it disliked. Indeed, one of them had gathered a measure of wheat and was giving it in charity; when asked about the reason, he said: "I put on my shoes once and began with the left foot by mistake, so I wished to atone for it with charity." Indeed, the jurist cannot magnify the matter in these affairs, for he is constrained by reforming the common folk, whose rank is close to the rank of blessing, and they are immersed in darknesses too vast and immense for such darknesses to appear in comparison. Thus, it is ugly to say that one who drank wine and took the cup with his left hand has transgressed in two aspects: one is the drinking, and the other is taking with the left. And one who sells wine at the time of the call to prayer on Friday—it is ugly to say he betrayed in two aspects: one is selling wine, and the other is selling at the time of the call. And one who relieves himself in the mosque's prayer niche, turning his back to the qibla—it is ugly to mention his lack of etiquette in relieving himself from the aspect that he did not place the qibla to his right. All sins are darknesses, some above others, so some are obscured beside others. A master may punish his servant if he uses his knife without permission, but if he killed with that knife his dearest child, the ruling for using the knife without permission would remain, yet its sting in himself would not. All the etiquettes observed by the prophets and the saints, which we are lenient about in jurisprudence with the common folk, are due to this necessity; otherwise, all these disliked matters are deviations from justice and ingratitude for blessings, and a shortfall from the degree that conveys the servant to the degrees of nearness. Some affect the servant by diminishing nearness and lowering his station, and some remove him entirely from the bounds of nearness to the realm of distance, which is the abode of devils.

Likewise, one who breaks a branch from a tree without an immediate, pressing need or a sound, legitimate purpose has shown ingratitude for the blessing of God, exalted is He, in creating trees and creating the hand. As for the hand, it was not created for frivolity but for obedience and acts that aid in obedience. As for the tree, God, exalted is He, created it and created roots for it, conveyed water to it, and placed within it the power of nourishment and growth so that it may reach the peak of its vigor and His servants benefit from it. To break it before the peak of its vigor, not in a manner that benefits His servants, is contrary to the aim of wisdom and a deviation from justice. If one has a sound, legitimate purpose, then it is permissible, for trees and animals are made as ransom for human purposes, as both are perishable, vanishing. To expend the lower for the preservation of the higher for a time is closer to justice than wasting both.

All together, and to this the verse of God Almighty alludes: "And He has subjected to you whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth, all together from Him." Indeed, if someone were to break that from the dominion of another, he would also be an oppressor, even if he were in need, because each specific tree does not fulfill the needs of all God's servants; rather, it fulfills only one need. And if one person were to appropriate it for himself without any prior claim or specific right, it would be oppression. The one with the specific right is he who obtained the seed, placed it in the earth, channeled water to it, and undertook its care; he is more entitled to it than others, and his claim is thereby established. If that tree grew in barren land without human effort, the right belongs to the one who planted it or to the one who sowed it. Another specific right must then be sought, which is precedence in taking it, for the one who precedes has the particularity of precedence. Justice is that he be the most entitled to it. The poor have expressed this precedence as ownership, but this is purely metaphorical, for there is no ownership except for the King of Kings, to whom belongs whatever is in the heavens and the earth. How can a servant be an owner when he himself does not own his own self, but is rather owned by another? Indeed, creation are the servants of God, and the earth is God's table. He has permitted them to eat from His table according to their need, like a king who sets a table for his servants. If one takes a morsel with his right hand and encloses it within his fingers, and then another servant comes and wants to snatch it from his hand, he cannot be allowed to do so—not because the morsel has become his property by taking it in hand, for the hand and its owner are also owned—but because each specific morsel does not fulfill the need of every servant. Justice in specification occurs when a kind of precedence, specific right, and taking arises—a right specific to the servant—and thus one who cannot establish such a specific right is prevented from contending with him. This is how God's command concerning His servants should be understood. Therefore, we say: Whoever takes from the worldly wealth more than his need, hoards it, and withholds it while among God's servants are those who need it, he is an oppressor and is among those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend it in the way of God. The way of God is obedience to Him, and the provision for creation in His obedience is worldly wealth, for through it their necessities are repelled and their needs are elevated. However, this does not enter into the scope of legal rulings, because the measures of needs are hidden, souls differ in their perception of future poverty, and the ends of lifespans are unknown. To impose this upon the common people would be like imposing dignity, gravity, and silence about unimportant speech upon children; due to their deficiency, they cannot bear it. Thus, we refrain from objecting to them in play and amusement, and our permitting that to them does not indicate that amusement and play are inherently right. Similarly, our permitting the common people to preserve wealth and restrict their spending to the amount of zakah, due to the miserliness ingrained in their nature, does not indicate that it is the ultimate truth. The Qur'an alluded to this when God Almighty said: "If He were to ask you for it and press you, you would withhold." Rather, the unblemished truth and the justice devoid of oppression is that none of God's servants should take from God's wealth except the amount of a traveler's provision, for all God's servants are riders upon the mounts of their bodies to the presence of the Just King. So whoever takes more than that and then withholds it from another rider in need of it is an oppressor, abandoning justice, departing from the intended wisdom, and ungrateful for the favor of God Almighty upon him through the Qur'an, the Messenger, intellect, and all the means by which he knows that whatever exceeds a traveler's provision is a burden upon him in this world and the next. Whoever understands the wisdom of God Almighty in all types of existent things is able to fulfill the duty of gratitude. Exhausting this subject would require volumes, and even then it would only cover a little. We have mentioned this amount only so that the reason for the truthfulness in God Almighty's saying may be known: "And few of My servants are grateful." And Iblis, may God curse him, rejoiced in His saying: "And you will not find most of them grateful." One who does not know the meaning of all this and other matters beyond it—whose principles lifetimes would end before exhausting—does not know the meaning of this verse. As for the explanation of the verse and the meaning of its wording, anyone who knows the language knows it. By this, the difference between meaning and explanation becomes clear to you.

If you say: The essence of this discourse returns to the fact that God Almighty is the Judge in everything, and that He has made some actions of the servants a cause for the perfection of wisdom and its reaching its intended purpose, and He has made some of their actions a preventer of the perfection of wisdom. Thus, every action that conforms to the requirement of wisdom, so that wisdom flows to its purpose, is gratitude; and everything that opposes and prevents the causes from flowing to their intended purpose is ingratitude. All this is understood, but the difficulty remains: The action of the servant, divided into what completes wisdom and what removes it, is also from the action of God Almighty. So where is the servant in between, such that he is grateful at one time and ungrateful at another? Know that the completion of certainty in this is drawn from the current...

A vast ocean of unveiling sciences, to whose principles we have previously alluded with subtle hints. Now we express in brief words its ultimate end and goal, which is understood by one who knows the language of the birds, and denied by one who is incapable of even setting out on the journey, let alone soaring in the realm of the Kingdom like the birds. So we say:

Allah, Mighty and Majestic is He, in His Majesty and Grandeur, has an Attribute from which creation and origination issue forth. That Attribute is too exalted and sublime for the eye of a language-coiner to perceive it, such that he could express it with a phrase indicating the essence of its Majesty and the specific reality of its truth. Thus, in the world, there exists no expression for it due to the loftiness of its station and the lowliness of the rank of language-coiners, whose understanding cannot extend to the beginnings of its radiance. Their sight falls short of its pinnacle, just as the sight of bats falls short of the light of the sun—not due to any obscurity in the sun's light, but due to weakness in the bats' sight.

Therefore, those whose eyes were opened to observe its Majesty were compelled to borrow, from the lowly world of those who articulate languages, a phrase that conveys from the beginnings of its realities something very feeble. So they borrowed for it the name "Power" (al-Qudrah). Due to their borrowing, we ventured to speak and said: Allah, Exalted is He, has an Attribute which is Power, from which creation and origination issue forth.

Then, creation divides in existence into divisions, each with specific attributes. The source of the division of these divisions and their specification with their particular attributes is another Attribute. For it, by a similar necessity as before, the expression "Will" (al-Mashiyyah) was borrowed. It suggests from it a meaning understood by those who articulate languages, which are letters and sounds used for mutual understanding. The inadequacy of the term "Will" to indicate the essence of that Attribute and its reality is like the inadequacy of the term "Power."

Then, the actions issuing from Power divided into that which proceeds to the ultimate end, which is the goal of its wisdom, and that which stops short of the goal. Each had a relation to the attribute of Will, since they refer back to the specificities by which the division and differences are completed. For the relation of that which reaches its goal, the expression "Love" (al-Mahabbah) was borrowed. For the relation of that which stops short of its goal, the expression "Dislike" (al-Karahah) was borrowed. It is said that both are included within the description of Will, but each has another specific characteristic in the relation, which the terms "Love" and "Dislike" suggest as a general meaning for those seeking understanding from words and languages.

Then, His servants—who are also from His creation and origination—divided into those for whom the Eternal Will preceded that He would use them to halt His wisdom short of its goal, and that would be a compulsion upon them by unleashing inclinations and motives upon them; and into those for whom it was pre-eternally decreed that He would use them to conduct His wisdom to its goal in some matters. Thus, each of the two groups had a specific relation to the Will. For the relation of those used to complete wisdom through them, the expression "Pleasure" (al-Rida) was borrowed. For those by whom the means of wisdom were halted short of its goal, the expression "Wrath" (al-Ghadab) was borrowed.

Thus, upon the one upon whom wrath was decreed pre-eternally appeared an action by which wisdom was halted short of its goal, so "Ingratitude" (al-Kufran) was borrowed for him, and that was followed by the punishment of curse and blame as an increase in retribution. And upon the one whom He was pleased with pre-eternally appeared an action by which wisdom, because of it, proceeded to its goal, so the expression "Gratitude" (al-Shukr) was borrowed for him, and it was followed by the robe of praise and commendation as an increase in pleasure, acceptance, and favor.

The result was that He, Exalted is He, bestowed beauty, then praised; and bestowed punishment, then deemed ugly and cast down. Its similitude is that a king cleans his dirty servant from his filth, then clothes him from the finest of his garments. When he completes his adornment, he says, "O beautiful one, how beautiful you are, and how beautiful your garments, and how clean your face!" In reality, He is the Beautifier and the One who praises the beauty. Thus, He is the One praised in every state. It is as if, from the perspective of meaning, He praised none but Himself, while the servant is the target of praise from the perspective of outward appearance and form.

Thus were the matters in pre-eternity, and thus do causes and effects proceed in sequence by the decree of the Lord of lords, the Originator of causes. This was not by chance or inquiry, but by a Will, Wisdom, true Judgment, and decisive Command, for which the term "Decree" (al-Qada') was borrowed. It is said it is like a glance of the eye, or closer, whence the seas of measures flowed by the ruling of that decisive Decree with what pre-eternal determination had ordained. Then, for the ordering of the individual destined things one upon another, the term "Divine Measure" (al-Qadar) was borrowed. Thus, the term "Decree" corresponds to the single, universal Command, and the term "Divine Measure" corresponds to the detailed, endless succession.

It is said that nothing of that is outside of Decree and Divine Measure. It occurred to some servants: "Why did the division necessitate this detail, and how is justice consistent with this disparity and preferential treatment?" Some of them, due to their incapacity, could not bear to observe the essence of this matter and encompass its totality. So they were restrained from what they could not fathom plunging into, by the bridle of prohibition, and it was said to them: "Be still, for..."

For this were you created. He is not questioned about what He does, but they will be questioned. And the niche of some of them was filled with a light, kindled from the light of God, Most High, in the heavens and the earth. And their oil was, at first, pure, so that it would almost give light even if no fire touched it. Then a fire touched it, and it blazed with light upon light. So the regions of the dominion shone before them with the light of their Lord, and they perceived all matters as they truly are. Then it was said to them: "Adorn yourselves with the manners of God, Most High, and be at peace. And when Predestination is mentioned, be silent." For walls have ears, and around you are the weak of vision. So proceed at the pace of your weakest, and do not lift the veil of the sun for the eyes of bats, for that would be a cause of their destruction. Therefore, embody the character traits of God, Most High, and descend from the zenith of your ascent to the heaven of this world, so that the weak may find comfort in you and may kindle from the remnants of your shining lights from behind your veil, just as bats kindle from the remnants of the light of the sun and the stars in the darkness of night. Thus, they live by it a life that their person and state can bear, even if they do not live by it the life of those who move about in the full light of the sun.

And be like those of whom it was said:
"We drank a pure drink in the presence of the Pure,
Thus is the drink of the pure made pure.
We drank and poured upon the earth what remained,
And for the earth from the cup of the generous is a share."

Thus was the beginning of this affair and its end. You will not understand it unless you are worthy of it. And if you are worthy of it, the eye is opened and you see, so you have no need for a guide to lead you. The blind can be led, but only to a limit. When the path narrows and becomes sharper than a sword's edge and finer than a hair, the bird may be able to fly upon it, but it cannot drag a blind man behind it. And when the passage becomes subtle and fine, like water for example, and crossing is only possible by swimming, the one skilled in the art of swimming may be able to cross by himself, but perhaps he cannot pull another behind him. These are matters wherein the act of traversing them, compared to traversing what is the state of the commonality of creation, is like walking on water compared to walking on land. Swimming can be learned, but as for walking on water, it is not acquired by teaching; rather, it is attained by the strength of certainty. Therefore, it was said to the Prophet (peace be upon him), "It is said that Jesus (peace be upon him) walked on water." He (peace be upon him) said, "Had he increased in certainty, he would have walked on air." These are symbols and allusions to the meaning of aversion and love, pleasure and anger, gratitude and ingratitude. It is not fitting for the science of spiritual transaction to exceed this. And God, Most High, has set forth a similitude for this, bringing it near to the understandings of creation, for He knew that He created the jinn and mankind only to worship Him. Thus, their worship is the ultimate wisdom in their regard. Then He informed that He has two servants: He loves one of them, whose name is Gabriel, the Spirit of Holiness, and the Trustworthy, and he is with Him beloved, obeyed, trustworthy, and firmly established. And He detests the other, whose name is Iblis, and he is the accursed, granted respite until the Day of Recompense. Then He attributed guidance to Gabriel, saying, Most High, "Say, 'The Spirit of Holiness has brought it down from your Lord in truth.'" And He, Most High, said, "He sends down the Spirit from His command upon whom He wills of His servants." And He attributed misguidance to Iblis, saying, Most High, "To lead astray from His path." And misguidance is preventing the servants from reaching the ultimate wisdom. So see how He attributed it to the servant upon whom He is angry. And guidance is His conveying them to the ultimate end, so see how He attributed it to the servant whom He loved.

You have a customary example for this: If a king needed someone to serve him drink and someone to perform cupping and clean the courtyard of his house from filth, and he had two servants, he would not appoint for the cupping and cleaning except the ugliest and basest of them. And he would not entrust the carrying of the drink and perfume except to the best, most perfect, and most beloved of them to him. And you should not say, "This is my doing, and was his action not without my doing?" For you have erred by attributing that to yourself. Rather, it is He who directed your motive for specifying the detested action with the detested person and the beloved action with the beloved person, in completion of justice. For His justice is sometimes completed through matters in which you have no part, and sometimes it is completed within you, for you too are from His actions. Thus, your motive, your power, your knowledge, your action, and all the causes of your movements in expression are His action, which He arranged with justice, an arrangement from which balanced actions proceed. However, you see only yourself, so you imagine that what appears upon you in the world of testimony has no cause from the world of the unseen and the dominion. Therefore, you attribute it to yourself. You are but like a child who looks at night at the play of the puppeteer, who brings out forms from behind a veil that dance, cry out, stand, and sit. They are composed of rags that do not move by themselves; rather, they are moved by fine, hair-like strings that do not appear in the darkness of the night, and their ends are in the hand of the puppeteer, who is concealed from the sight of the children. So they rejoice and marvel, thinking that those forms...

The foolish dance and play, rising and sitting, while the wise know that this is movement, yet not movement in itself. However, they may not know its detailed nature, and even one who knows some of its details does not know it as the illusionist knows, who has command over it and holds the strings in his hand. Similarly, the children of this world—indeed, all creation are like children compared to the learned—look upon these figures and suppose they are the ones moving, attributing the motion to them. The learned know they are being moved, yet they do not know the manner of the moving, and they are the majority, save for the knowers, the learned, and the firmly rooted. For they have perceived with the eyes of their insight fine, spider-web threads—nay, far finer—suspended from the heavens, their ends attached to the persons of the people of earth. Those threads are not perceived by these outward eyes due to their fineness. Then they witnessed the heads of those threads in their points of suspension, by which they are hung, and they witnessed for those points of suspension handles that are in the hands of the angels who move the heavens. They also witnessed the angels of the heavens directed toward the bearers of the Throne, awaiting from them what descends upon them of command from the presence of Lordship, so that they do not disobey God in what He commands them and they do as they are ordered. These visions are alluded to in the Qur’an, where it is said: "And in the heaven is your provision and what you are promised." (51:22) And it alludes to the waiting of the angels of the heavens for what descends to them of decree and command, as it is said: "He created seven heavens, and of the earth the like thereof. The command descends between them, that you may know that God has power over all things and that God encompasses all things in knowledge." (65:12) These are matters whose interpretation none knows save God and those firmly rooted in knowledge. Ibn ‘Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, alluded to the exclusive possession by those firmly rooted in knowledge of sciences that the understandings of creation cannot bear when he recited the words of the Exalted: "The command descends between them," and said, "If I mentioned what I know of the meaning of this verse, you would stone me," and in another wording, "you would say he is an unbeliever." Let us confine ourselves to this measure, for the reins of speech have slipped from the grasp of choice and have mingled with the science of spiritual transaction what is not of it. Let us return to the purposes of gratitude.

We say: If the reality of gratitude reverts to the servant being an instrument in the completion of God’s wisdom, then the most grateful of servants are the most beloved to God and the closest to Him. The closest to God are the angels, and they too have an order; there is not one among them but that he has a known station. The highest of them in rank of proximity is an angel named Israfil, peace be upon him. The loftiness of their degree is because they are in themselves noble and righteous, and God has rectified the prophets, peace be upon them, through them. They are the noblest creation on the face of the earth. Next to their degree is the degree of the prophets, for they are in themselves excellent, and God has guided the rest of creation through them and completed His wisdom through them. The highest of them in rank is our Prophet, upon whom be peace, for through him God perfected the religion and sealed the prophets. Next to them are the learned who are the heirs of the prophets, for they are in themselves righteous, and God has rectified the rest of creation through them. The degree of each of them is according to what he has rectified of himself and of others. Then next to them are the just rulers, for they have rectified the worldly affairs of creation as the learned have rectified their religion. Due to the combination of religion, kingship, and authority for our Prophet Muhammad, upon whom be peace, he is superior to the rest of the prophets, for God perfected through him the rectification of their religion and their world, and the sword and kingship were not for other prophets. Then next to the learned and the rulers are the righteous who have rectified only their religion and their own souls, so the wisdom of God was not completed through them, but it is in them. Apart from these are the rabble and the common herd.

Know that the ruler is the mainstay of religion; he should not be belittled even if he is oppressive and sinful. ‘Amr ibn al-‘As, may God have mercy on him, said: "A tyrannical imam is better than lasting sedition." And the Prophet, upon whom be peace, said: "There will come upon you rulers whom you will recognize and disapprove of, and they will cause corruption, yet God will bring about more good through them. If they do good, they have the reward and upon you is gratitude; and if they do evil, upon them is the burden and upon you is patience." Sahl said: "Whoever rejects his imam, the ruler, is a heretic; and whom the ruler calls and does not answer is an innovator; and who comes to him without being summoned is ignorant." He was asked, "Who are the best of people?" He said, "The ruler." It was said, "We used to think the worst of people was the ruler." He said, "Gently! Verily, God has for him every day two glances: a glance at the safety of the Muslims’ wealth and a glance at the safety of their bodies. Then He looks into his record and forgives him all his sin." And he used to say, "The black wooden beams hung at their doors are better than seventy preachers preaching."

(The Second Pillar of the Pillars of Gratitude: That Upon Which Gratitude is Rendered)
It is the blessing. Let us mention therein the reality of blessing, its divisions, its degrees, its kinds, and its aggregates in what is specific and general, for enumerating the blessings of God upon His servants is beyond the capacity of humankind, as He said...

Exalted is He: "And if you should count the favors of Allah, you could not enumerate them." Therefore, we shall first present comprehensive principles that serve as foundational laws for recognizing blessings, and then we will devote ourselves to enumerating them individually. And Allah is the Granter of success to what is correct.
                        (Clarifying the True Nature of Blessings and Their Categories)

Know that every good, pleasure, and happiness—indeed, every object of desire and pursuit—is termed a blessing. However, the blessing in its true reality is the happiness of the Hereafter. To call anything else a blessing or happiness is either an error or a metaphorical usage, like calling worldly happiness that does not aid in attaining the Hereafter a blessing, for that is pure error. The term 'blessing' may be applied to a thing truthfully, but its application to the happiness of the Hereafter is the most truthful. Thus, every cause that leads to and assists in attaining the happiness of the Hereafter, whether through a single means or multiple intermediaries, its designation as a blessing is correct and true, because it culminates in the true blessing. We shall explain the causes, aids, and pleasures termed blessings through classifications.

The First Classification: All matters, in relation to us, are divided into: 1) That which is beneficial in both this world and the Hereafter, such as knowledge and good character; 2) That which is harmful in both, such as ignorance and bad character; 3) That which is beneficial in the immediate situation but harmful in the ultimate outcome, such as indulging in following desires; 4) That which is harmful and painful in the immediate situation but beneficial in the ultimate outcome, such as suppressing desires and opposing the lower self. That which is beneficial in both the immediate and ultimate sense is truly a blessing, like knowledge and good character. That which is harmful in both is truly a calamity, being their opposite. That which is beneficial in the immediate situation but harmful in the ultimate outcome is, in the sight of the insightful, a pure calamity, though the ignorant deem it a blessing. Its example is a hungry person who finds honey containing poison; if ignorant, he considers it a blessing, but if he knows, he understands it is a calamity that has befallen him. That which is harmful in the immediate situation but beneficial in the ultimate outcome is a blessing in the sight of the wise, but a calamity to the ignorant. Its example is bitter-tasting medicine in the moment, yet it cures diseases and ailments and brings health and well-being. An ignorant child, if compelled to drink it, considers it a calamity, while the wise person considers it a blessing and feels indebted to whoever guides him to it, brings it near, and prepares its means. Therefore, a mother prevents her child from cupping, while the father calls him to it. For the father, due to his perfect intellect, perceives the consequence, while the mother, due to her excessive love and deficiency, focuses on the immediate situation. The child, due to his ignorance, feels indebted to his mother rather than his father, feels comfort with her and her compassion, and considers the father an enemy. If he were wise, he would know that the mother is a hidden enemy in the guise of a friend, for her preventing him from cupping leads him to diseases and pains more severe than cupping. However, an ignorant friend is worse than a wise enemy. Every person is a friend to himself, but he is an ignorant friend, and thus he does to himself what even an enemy would not do.

A Second Classification: Know that all worldly causes are mixed, their good blended with their evil, so their good is seldom pure, such as wealth, family, children, relatives, status, and all other means. However, they are divided into: 1) That whose benefit outweighs its harm, like a sufficient amount of wealth, status, and other means; 2) That whose harm outweighs its benefit for most people, like abundant wealth and extensive status; 3) That whose harm and benefit are equivalent. These matters differ according to individuals. For one righteous person may benefit from lawful wealth, even if abundant, by spending it in the way of Allah and directing it to good deeds; with such divine facilitation, it is a blessing for him. Another person may be harmed even by a little, constantly belittling it, complaining to his Lord, and seeking increase in it; with such divine abandonment, it is a calamity for him.

A Third Classification: Know that, from another perspective, good things are divided into: 1) That which is sought for its own sake, not for something else; 2) That which is sought for the sake of something else; 3) That which is sought for both its own sake and for something else. The first is what is sought for its own sake, not for something else, like the pleasure of gazing upon the Countenance of Allah, the Exalted, and the happiness of meeting Him—in sum, the everlasting happiness of the Hereafter. It is not sought to attain another intended goal beyond it; rather, it is sought for its own essence. The second is what is intended for something else, with no purpose in its essence at all, like dirhams and dinars. If needs were not fulfilled by them, they would be equivalent to pebbles. But because they are a means to pleasures, quickly delivering to them, they become beloved in themselves to the ignorant, so they hoard and treasure them, trade in usury over them, and think they are the intended goal. Their example is like one who loves a person, and because of him loves the messenger who brings them together, then forgets, in his love for the messenger, the love for the original person, turns away from him for his entire life, and remains preoccupied with tending to, observing, and checking on the messenger. This is the height of ignorance and misguidance. The third is what is sought for its own sake and for something else, like health and well-being. They are sought so that one may, because of them, be capable of the remembrance and reflection that lead to meeting Allah, the Exalted, or to attain through them...

To the attainment of worldly pleasures and the pursuit of their essence, for even if a person is independent of a thing for which a man's well-being is sought, he still desires the man's well-being insofar as it is well-being. Therefore, that which is chosen for its own sake alone is goodness and blessing in reality. That which is chosen for its own sake and for the sake of something else is also a blessing, but lesser than the first. As for that which is chosen only for the sake of something else, like the two currencies (gold and silver), they are not described in themselves, as they are substances, as being a blessing. Rather, from the perspective that they are means, they become a blessing for one who intends a matter he cannot attain except through them. If his objective were knowledge and worship, and he possessed the sufficiency which is a necessity for his life, gold and clay would be equal to him; their existence and non-existence would be of one level to him. Indeed, perhaps their existence might preoccupy him from reflection and worship, so they would be an affliction for him and not a blessing.

A fourth division: Know that goods, from another consideration, are divided into the beneficial, the pleasurable, and the beautiful. The pleasurable is that whose comfort is perceived immediately. The beneficial is that which yields benefit in the ultimate end. The beautiful is that which is deemed good in all circumstances. Evils are also divided into the harmful, the ugly, and the painful. Each of these two categories has two types: absolute and conditional. The absolute is that in which the three attributes are combined. In good, such as knowledge and wisdom, for they are beneficial, beautiful, and pleasurable to the people of knowledge and wisdom. In evil, such as ignorance, for it is harmful, ugly, and painful. The ignorant one only feels the pain of his ignorance when he knows he is ignorant, which is by seeing others as knowledgeable and seeing himself as ignorant, thus perceiving the pain of deficiency. Then a desire for the pleasurable knowledge arises within him. Yet, envy, pride, and bodily appetites may prevent him from learning, so two opposites pull at him, and his pain intensifies. For if he abandons learning, he suffers from ignorance and perceives deficiency. If he occupies himself with learning, he suffers from abandoning appetites or from abandoning pride and the humility of learning. Such a person remains inevitably in constant torment. The second type is the conditional, which combines some of these attributes but not others. Sometimes a thing is beneficial yet painful, like amputating a gangrenous finger or removing a tumor from the body. Sometimes a thing is beneficial yet ugly, like foolishness, for relative to some circumstances it is beneficial. It has been said, "He who has no intellect rests," for he is not concerned with consequences and thus finds rest in the present until the time of his destruction arrives. Sometimes a thing is beneficial from one aspect and harmful from another, like throwing wealth into the sea when fearing drowning, for it is harmful to the wealth but beneficial to the soul in its salvation. The beneficial is of two kinds: essential, like faith and good character in attaining the happiness of the Hereafter—and I mean by these knowledge and action, for nothing whatsoever can take their place—and non-essential, like oxymel for calming yellow bile, for it may also be possible to calm it with something that can take its place.

A fifth division: Know that "blessing" is expressed as every pleasurable thing. Pleasures, relative to man in terms of his exclusive possession of them or his sharing them with others, are of three types: intellectual, bodily shared with some animals, and bodily shared with all animals. As for the intellectual, such as the pleasure of knowledge and wisdom, for the ear, sight, smell, taste, the belly, and the private parts do not find pleasure in them. Only the heart finds pleasure in them due to a quality specific to it expressed as intellect. These are the least prevalent of pleasures and the most noble. As for their scarcity, it is because only a knowledgeable person finds pleasure in knowledge, and only a wise person finds pleasure in wisdom. How few are the people of knowledge and wisdom, and how many are those who merely bear their name and imitate their outward forms. As for their nobility, it is because they are inherent and never vanish, neither in this world nor in the Hereafter, and are perpetual without causing weariness. Food brings satiety, then weariness; the appetite for intercourse is spent, then becomes burdensome. Knowledge and wisdom can never be conceived to cause weariness or become burdensome. He who is capable of the noble, everlasting eternal, yet is content with the base, perishable in the nearest of times, is afflicted in his intellect, deprived due to his wretchedness and misfortune. The least of it is that knowledge and intellect do not need assistants and guards, unlike wealth, for knowledge guards you while you guard wealth. Knowledge increases through spending, while wealth decreases through spending. Wealth can be stolen, and authority can be removed, but knowledge cannot be reached by the hands of thieves for taking, nor by the hands of rulers for removal. Thus, its possessor is in a spirit of security forever, while the possessor of wealth and status is in the distress of fear forever. Furthermore, knowledge is beneficial, pleasurable, and beautiful in every state forever. Wealth, at times, pulls toward destruction and at times pulls toward salvation. Therefore, God Almighty censured wealth in the Quran in several places, though He called it good in other places. As for the failure of most of creation to perceive the pleasure of knowledge, it is either due to lack of taste, for he who has not tasted does not know and does not yearn, since...

Longing follows taste. As for those who fail to perceive it, it is either due to the corruption of their temperaments and the sickness of their hearts from following base desires, like a sick person who cannot perceive the sweetness of honey and finds it bitter; or due to a deficiency in their innate perception, for the quality by which knowledge is relished has not yet been created within them, like an infant who cannot perceive the delight of honey and fat birds and finds pleasure only in milk. This does not indicate that these things are not delightful, nor does the infant's enjoyment of milk prove it to be the most delightful of things. Thus, those deficient in perceiving the delight of knowledge and wisdom are of three kinds: one whose inner self has not yet come to life, like a child; one who died after having lived, by following base desires; and one who became sick due to following base desires. His statement, exalted is He, "in their hearts is a disease" (Qur'an 2:10) alludes to the sickness of intellects. And His statement, mighty and majestic, "that he may warn whoever is alive" (Qur'an 36:70) alludes to one who has not attained an inner life. Every being physically alive but dead in heart is among the dead in the sight of God, even if considered among the living by the ignorant. For this reason, the martyrs are alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing, even though they are dead in their bodies.

The second kind is a delight in which man shares with some animals, such as the delight of leadership, domination, and mastery. This exists in the lion, the tiger, and some animals. The third is what he shares with all other animals, such as the delight of the belly and the private parts. This is the most prevalent and the basest of them, which is why every class partakes in it, even worms and insects. Whoever transcends this rank becomes attached to the delight of domination, which is the most tenacious for the heedless. If he transcends that, he ascends to the third, and the delight that predominates over him becomes the delight of knowledge and wisdom, especially the delight of knowing God, exalted is He, and knowing His attributes and His acts. This is the rank of the truthful ones (al-siddiqin), and its perfection is not attained except by the expulsion of the love of leadership from the heart. The last thing to leave the heads of the truthful ones is the love of leadership. As for the greed of the belly and private parts, its breaking is something the righteous can achieve, but the desire for leadership, none can break except the truthful ones. As for suppressing it completely so that one does not feel it at all times and in varying states, this seems to be beyond human capability. Indeed, the delight of knowing God, exalted is He, overpowers in states where one does not feel the delight of leadership and domination, but this does not last a lifetime; rather, periods of lassitude befall it, and one returns to human attributes, so they exist but are subdued, unable to compel the soul to deviate from justice.

At this point, hearts are divided into four categories: a heart that loves nothing but God, exalted is He, and finds rest only in increasing knowledge of Him and contemplation of Him; a heart that knows not the delight of knowledge nor the meaning of intimacy with God, its delight being only in status, leadership, wealth, and other bodily desires; a heart whose predominant state is intimacy with God, glorified is He, and delight in knowing Him and contemplating Him, though it may occasionally revert to human attributes; and a heart whose predominant state is delight in human attributes, though it may occasionally experience delight in knowledge and gnosis. As for the first, if it is possible in existence, it is extremely rare. The second, the world is teeming with it. The third and fourth exist, but are exceedingly scarce. It is inconceivable for this to be rare and anomalous, yet despite its rarity, it varies in degree of scarcity and abundance. Its abundance occurs only in eras close to the eras of the prophets, peace be upon them. The interval continues to lengthen, and such hearts become fewer until the Hour draws near and God accomplishes His decree. This must be rare because it is the inception of the kingdom of the Hereafter, and sovereignty is precious, and sovereigns are not numerous. Just as the preeminent in sovereignty and beauty are but rare, and most people are beneath them, so it is with the sovereignty of the Hereafter. For this world is a mirror of the Hereafter; it is an expression of the world of witness, and the Hereafter is an expression of the world of the unseen. The world of witness follows the world of the unseen, just as the image in the mirror follows the image of the viewer. The image in the mirror, though secondary in the order of existence, is primary in relation to your vision, for you do not see yourself, but you see your image in the mirror first, and thereby know your image which is inherent to you secondarily, by way of similitude. Thus, the heart that is secondary in existence is primary in relation to knowledge, and the heart that is later is earlier. This is a kind of inversion, but inversion and reversal are necessities of this world. Likewise, the world of dominion and witness is a similitude of the world of the unseen and the sovereign realm. Among people are those for whom reflective consideration is made easy, so he looks at nothing in the world of dominion without interpreting it to the world of the sovereign realm; his interpretation is called a lesson, and the Truth has commanded it.

He said: "So take heed, O you of insight." Yet among them are those whose inner vision is blinded and do not take heed, so they are confined in the realm of sovereignty and the visible world, and the gates of Hell will be opened to their confinement. This confinement is filled with a fire whose nature is to assail the hearts, save that between it and the perception of its pain is a veil. When that veil is lifted by death, he perceives it. Concerning this, God Almighty manifested the truth upon the tongues of a people whom He caused to speak the truth, and they said: Paradise and Hell are created, but Hellfire is perceived once by a perception called the knowledge of certainty, and once by another perception called the vision of certainty. The vision of certainty occurs only in the Hereafter, while the knowledge of certainty may occur in this world, but only for those who have received their share of the light of certainty. Therefore, God Almighty said: "Nay, if you knew with the knowledge of certainty, you would surely see Hellfire" — that is, in this world — "Then you would surely see it with the vision of certainty" — that is, in the Hereafter. Thus, it has become clear that the sound heart for the sovereignty of the Hereafter can only be noble, just as the sound person is for the sovereignty of this world.

Know that blessings are divided into those which are an end sought for itself and those which are sought for the sake of the end. As for the end, it is the happiness of the Hereafter, and its essence reverts to four matters: everlasting life without perishing, joy without grief, knowledge without ignorance accompanying it, and wealth without poverty thereafter. This is the true blessing. Therefore, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: "There is no life except the life of the Hereafter." He said this during hardship to console the soul, and that was at the time of digging the trench in severe distress. And he said it once during joy to prevent the soul from inclining to the joys of this world, and that was when people thronged around him during the Farewell Pilgrimage. A man said: "O God, I ask You for the perfection of blessing." The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: "Do you know what the perfection of blessing is?" He said: "No." He said: "The perfection of blessing is entry into Paradise." As for the means, they are divided into the nearest and most specific, such as the virtues of the soul; and what follows it in proximity, such as the virtues of the body, which is the second; and what follows that in proximity and extends beyond the body, such as the causes surrounding the body like wealth, family, and tribe; and what combines these external causes with those attained by the soul, such as divine facilitation and guidance. They are, therefore, four types: The first type, which is the most specific, is the spiritual virtues, and their essence, despite the branching of their aspects, reverts to faith and good character. Faith is divided into the knowledge of unveiling, which is knowledge of God Almighty, His attributes, His angels, and His messengers; and the sciences of conduct. Good character is divided into two parts: abandoning the demands of desires and anger, which is called chastity; and observing justice in refraining from the demands of desires and in proceeding, such that one does not abstain entirely nor proceed however one wishes, but rather his proceeding and holding back are by the just balance that God Almighty revealed upon the tongue of His Messenger, peace be upon him, when God Almighty said: "That you do not transgress in the balance, and establish weight in justice and do not make deficient the balance." Thus, whoever castrates himself to remove the desire for marriage, or forsakes marriage despite capability and safety from harm, or forsakes eating until he becomes too weak for worship, remembrance, and reflection, has indeed made deficient the balance. And whoever plunges into the desires of the belly and private parts has transgressed in the balance. Justice is only that his weighing and estimation be free from transgression and deficiency, so that the two scales of the balance are balanced by it. Therefore, the specific virtues of the soul that draw near to God Almighty are four: the knowledge of unveiling, the knowledge of conduct, chastity, and justice. This is not fully realized in most cases except through the second type, which is the bodily virtues, and they are four: health, strength, beauty, and long life. These four matters are not made available except through the third type, which are the external blessings surrounding the body, and they are four: wealth, family, status, and noble lineage. And one benefits from none of these external and bodily causes except through the fourth type, which are the causes that combine them with what corresponds to the internal spiritual virtues, and they are four: God's guidance, His direction, His correction, and His support. Thus, the total of these blessings is sixteen when we divide them into four and divide each of the four into four. This totality requires some parts for others, whether out of essential need or beneficial need. As for the essential need, it is like the need of the happiness of the Hereafter for faith and good character, for there is absolutely no way to attain the happiness of the Hereafter except through them. Man has only what he strives for, and no one has in the Hereafter except what he provisioned from this world. Likewise, the need of the spiritual virtues, which acquire these sciences and refine character, for the health of the body is essential. As for the beneficial need in general, it is like the need of these...

The inner blessings of the soul and body, as well as the external blessings such as wealth, honor, and family—if these were lacking, deficiency might encroach upon some of the internal blessings.

If you ask: What is the need for the path of the Hereafter for external blessings like wealth, family, status, and kinship? Know that these causes function like wings that carry one to the goal and tools that facilitate the objective. As for wealth, a poor person seeking knowledge and perfection without sufficiency is like one rushing into battle without weapons, or a falcon attempting to hunt without wings. Thus, the Prophet ﷺ said: "Excellent is righteous wealth for a righteous man," and he ﷺ said: "Wealth is an excellent aid for God-consciousness." How could it not be so? For one deprived of wealth becomes consumed in seeking sustenance, arranging clothing, shelter, and life's necessities, then exposed to various harms that distract from remembrance and reflection—harms only repelled by the weapon of wealth. Moreover, such a one is deprived of the virtues of pilgrimage, almsgiving, charity, and spreading good deeds.

A sage was asked: "What is bliss?" He replied: "Wealth, for I have seen the poor have no life." He was asked: "Tell us more." He said: "Security, for I have seen the fearful have no life." He was asked: "Tell us more." He said: "Health, for I have seen the sick have no life." He was asked: "Tell us more." He said: "Youth, for I have seen the elderly have no life." What he mentioned alludes to worldly bliss, but insofar as it aids the Hereafter, it is a blessing. Thus, the Prophet ﷺ said: "Whoever wakes up secure in his home, healthy in his body, with his daily provision, it is as if the entire world has been gathered for him."

As for a righteous spouse and children, the need for them is evident, as the Prophet ﷺ said: "An excellent aid to religion is a righteous wife," and regarding children, he ﷺ said: "When a person dies, his deeds cease except for three: a righteous child who prays for him." We have mentioned the benefits of family and children in the Book of Marriage.

As for relatives, the more children and kin a man has, they become like eyes and hands for him, facilitating through them worldly matters important for his religion—matters that, if he were alone, would occupy him greatly. Anything that frees your heart from worldly necessities aids you in religion and is thus a blessing.

As for honor and status, through them a person repels humiliation and oppression from himself, and no Muslim can do without them, for he is never free from an enemy who harms him or an oppressor who disrupts his knowledge, work, and peace, occupying his heart—and his heart is his capital. These distractions are only repelled by honor and status. Thus, it is said: "Religion and sovereignty are twins." God Almighty said: "If God did not repel some people by means of others, the earth would be corrupted." Status means nothing but mastery over hearts, just as wealth means nothing but mastery over coins. Whoever masters coins, the possessors of hearts are subservient to repel harm from him. Just as one needs a roof to repel rain, a garment to repel cold, and a dog to repel wolves from his flock, so too does one need someone to repel evil from himself through them. With this intent, the prophets—who had no kingdom or dominion—would observe rulers and seek status with them, as do religious scholars, not with the aim of taking from their treasuries or seeking abundance and excess in this world by following them. Do not think that God's blessing upon the Prophet ﷺ when He granted him victory, perfected his religion, made him prevail over all his enemies, and established love for him in hearts—so that his honor and status expanded—was less than His blessing upon him when he was harmed and beaten until he was compelled to flee and emigrate.

If you ask: Is the nobility of kinship and the honor of family among the blessings or not? I say yes, and thus the Prophet ﷺ said: "The leaders are from Quraysh," and for this reason, the Prophet ﷺ was of the noblest lineage among the descendants of Adam, peace be upon him. He ﷺ said: "Choose suitable matches for your offspring," and he ﷺ said: "Beware of the green growth on dung heaps." It was asked: "What is the green growth on dung heaps?" He said: "A beautiful woman from a corrupt lineage." This too is among the blessings, and I do not mean by it affiliation with oppressors and worldly people, but rather affiliation with the tree of prophethood, with the leaders of scholars, and with the righteous and pious distinguished in knowledge and action.

If you ask: What is the meaning of bodily virtues? I say there is no obscurity in the intense need for health, strength, and long life, for knowledge and action are only perfected through them. Thus, the Prophet ﷺ said: "The greatest happiness is a long life spent in obedience to God Almighty." Among these, beauty is considered minor, and it is said: It suffices that the body is free from diseases that distract from pursuing good deeds. By my life, beauty is of little benefit, but it is also among the good things. As for this world, its benefit therein is evident; as for the Hereafter, it is from two aspects: First, the ugly is blameworthy, and natural dispositions recoil from it, and needs...

The comely countenance is nearer to acceptance, and its esteem in hearts is broader; thus from this aspect, it is like a wing that reaches as far as wealth and status, since it is a form of power. For the fair-faced is able to accomplish needs that the ill-favored cannot, and every aid in fulfilling worldly needs is an aid to the Hereafter through it.

Secondly, beauty for the most part indicates virtue of the soul, because when the light of the soul shines most completely, it is conveyed to the body. Appearance and inner character often correspond, which is why practitioners of physiognomy relied on bodily forms to know the soul's noble traits, saying the face and eye are the mirror of the inner self. Therefore, the effects of anger, joy, and grief appear in it. Hence it is said: "An open countenance is a sign of what is within the soul," and it is said: "There is nothing ugly on earth but that its most beautiful part is its face." Al-Ma'mun once reviewed an army, and an ugly man was presented to him. He questioned him and found him to be inarticulate, so he struck his name from the register, saying: "When the spirit shines upon the outward, it is comeliness; or upon the inward, it is eloquence. This one has neither outward nor inward."

It is said: "Seek good from the radiant of face." And 'Umar, may God be pleased with him, said: "When you send an envoy, seek one with a handsome face and a good name." Jurists said: "When the ranks of worshippers are equal, the fairest of face is most deserving of leading the prayer." And God the Exalted, bestowing favor thereby, said: "And He increased him in knowledge and stature." We do not mean by beauty what stirs desire, for that is femininity; rather, we mean tallness with uprightness, moderation in flesh, proportionality of limbs, and symmetry in the face's creation such that temperaments do not recoil from looking upon it.

If you say: "You have included wealth, status, lineage, family, and children within the scope of blessings, yet God the Exalted has censured wealth and status, as did the Messenger and the scholars. God said: 'Indeed, among your wives and your children are enemies to you, so beware of them,' and He said: 'Your wealth and your children are but a trial.' And 'Ali, may God honor his face, said in censuring lineage: 'People are the children of what they excel in, and a person's worth is what he excels at.' It is said: 'A man is by himself, not by his father.' So what is the meaning of them being blessings while they are censured by the Law?"

Know that whoever takes knowledge from transmitted, interpreted expressions and generalities requiring specification, misguidance is more likely for him unless he is guided by God's light to grasp the sciences as they truly are, then applies the transmission in accordance with what has become clear to him—through interpretation at times and specification at others. These are blessings that assist in the matter of the Hereafter; there is no way to deny them except that within them are trials and dangers. The example of wealth is like a snake containing both beneficial antidote and harmful poison. If it is obtained by the charmer who knows how to guard against its poison and extract its beneficial antidote, it is a blessing. But if it is obtained by the ignorant commoner, it is a calamity and ruin for him. It is like the sea beneath which are varieties of jewels and pearls. Whoever attains the sea, if he knows swimming, diving, and how to guard against the sea's perils, has attained its blessings. But if he plunges into it ignorant of that, he is destroyed.

For this reason, God the Exalted praised wealth and called it good, and the Messenger praised it, saying: "How excellent an aid toward God-consciousness is wealth." Likewise, He praised status and honor, for God bestowed upon His Messenger by making him prevail over all religion and endearing him to the hearts of creation—which is the meaning of status. However, what is transmitted in praise of them is little, and what is transmitted in censure of wealth and status is much. And where ostentation is censured, it is censure of status, for ostentation aims to attract hearts, and the meaning of status is mastery over hearts.

This is abundant and that is scarce because most people are ignorant of the method of charming the snake of wealth and diving into the sea of status, so warning them is obligatory, for they are destroyed by the poison of wealth before reaching its antidote, and the crocodile of the sea of status destroys them before discovering its jewels. If they were inherently blameworthy for everyone, it would be inconceivable for kingship to be joined to prophethood as it was for our Messenger, or for wealth to be joined to it as it was for Solomon, peace be upon him. All people are children, and wealths are snakes; the prophets and the knowers are charmers. What harms the child may not harm the charmer. Indeed, if a charmer had a child whose continued existence and rectitude he desired, and he found a snake, knowing that if he took it for its antidote, his child would imitate him and take the snake upon seeing it to play with it and thus perish, he would have an interest in the antidote and an interest in protecting the child. It is incumbent upon him to weigh his interest in the antidote against his interest in protecting the child. If he is able to abstain from the antidote without suffering great harm, and if he took it, his child would take it...

The child, and the harm is magnified by their destruction, so it is incumbent upon him to flee from the serpent when he sees it, and to instruct the child to flee, and to make its form ugly in his sight, and to inform him that within it is a lethal poison from which none are saved. And he must not relate to him at all the benefit of the antidote contained within it, for that might entice him to approach it without complete knowledge. Likewise, the diver, if he knows that were he to dive into the sea within sight of his child, the child would follow him and perish, it is incumbent upon him to warn the child away from the seashore and the riverbank. If the child is not deterred by mere warning whenever he sees his father lingering around the shore, then it is incumbent upon him to distance himself from the shore with the child and not to approach it in his presence. Similarly, the community within the care of the Prophets, peace be upon them, are like foolish children. For this reason He, peace be upon him, said: "I am to you only like a father to his child." And He, peace be upon him, said: "You are but plunging into the Fire like moths, and I am seizing you by your garments." Their greatest share is in preserving their children from destruction, for they were not sent except for that. They have no share in wealth except to the measure of sustenance. Thus, they restricted themselves to the measure of sustenance, and what remained beyond that they did not hoard but spent it, for in spending is the antidote and in hoarding is the poison. If the door of acquiring wealth were opened for people and they were inclined to it, they would lean towards the poison of hoarding and turn away from the antidote of spending. Therefore, wealth was made repugnant, and the meaning is the repugnance of hoarding it and being greedy for it, for amassing it and indulging in its pleasures, which necessitates leaning towards this world and its delights. As for taking it to the measure of sufficiency and directing the surplus to good works, that is not blameworthy. It is the right of every traveler to carry only the measure of his provision for the journey, if he resolves firmly to confine himself to what he carries. However, if his soul is generous in feeding others and expanding the provision for his companions, then there is no harm in acquiring more. His saying, peace and blessings be upon him: "Let the provision of any one of you from this world be like the provision of a rider," means for yourselves specifically. Indeed, among those who narrated this hadith and acted upon it were those who would take one hundred thousand dirhams in one place and distribute them in another, not keeping a single grain from it. And when the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, mentioned that the wealthy enter Paradise with difficulty, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, may God be pleased with him, sought his permission to give away all that he owned. He permitted him, and Gabriel, peace be upon him, descended and said: "Command him to feed the poor, clothe the naked, and host the guest." So, worldly blessings are mixed; their remedy is blended with their malady, their hope with their fear, and their benefit with their harm. Whoever trusts in his insight and the perfection of his knowledge, for him is to draw near to them, warding off their malady and extracting their remedy. But whoever does not trust in them, then distance, distance, and flight, flight from the places of danger. Nothing equals safety for these people, and they are all of creation except whom God, the Exalted, protects and guides to the path.

If you say: What then is the meaning of the preponderant, facilitating blessings that lead to guidance, right conduct, support, and rectification? Know that none can dispense with facilitation. It is an expression for the composition and joining between the will of the servant and the decree and destiny of God. This encompasses good and evil, what constitutes happiness and what constitutes misery. But custom has restricted the name 'facilitation' to that part of God's decree and destiny which conforms to happiness, just as 'deviation' is an expression for inclining, but is specified for one who inclines to falsehood over truth, and likewise 'apostasy.' The need for facilitation is evident, and for this reason it is said:
"If there is no aid from God for a youth, then the most his striving gathers is against him."

As for guidance, there is no way for anyone to seek happiness except through it, for a person's inclination may lean towards what contains the rectification of his Hereafter. But if he does not know what contains the rectification of his Hereafter, to the point that he considers corruption to be rectification, then how can mere will benefit him? There is no benefit in will, capability, and means except after guidance. For this reason, God, the Exalted, said: "Our Lord is He who gave everything its creation, then guided." And He, the Exalted, said: "And were it not for the favor of God upon you and His mercy, not one of you would ever have been pure, but God purifies whom He wills." And He, peace be upon him, said: "No one will enter Paradise except by the mercy of God, the Exalted," meaning by His guidance. It was said: "Not even you, O Messenger of God?" He said: "Not even I." Guidance has three stations: The first is knowledge of the path of good and evil, alluded to in His saying, the Exalted: "And We have shown him the two ways." God, the Exalted, has bestowed this upon all His servants, some of it through intellect and some of it upon the tongues of the messengers. For this reason He, the Exalted, said: "And as for Thamud, We guided them, but they preferred blindness over guidance." So the means of guidance are the Book, the messengers, and the insights of the intellects. They are offered, and none are prevented from them except...

Envy, arrogance, and love of this world are among the causes that blind the hearts, even if they do not blind the eyes. God Almighty has said: "Indeed, it is not the eyes that are blind, but blind are the hearts within the breasts." Among the blinding veils are familiarity and habit, and the love of adhering to them. This is expressed in His saying: "Indeed, we found our forefathers following a creed." Regarding arrogance and envy, it is expressed in His saying: "And they said, 'Why was this Qur'an not sent down upon a great man from one of the two cities?'" and His saying: "Shall we follow a single human being from among us?" These are the veils that prevented guidance, and the second guidance lies beyond this general guidance. It is that which God Almighty grants the servant state after state, and it is the fruit of spiritual struggle, as He said: "And those who strive in Our cause – We will surely guide them to Our paths." This is what is meant by His saying: "And those who are guided, He increases them in guidance." The third guidance lies beyond the second; it is the light that shines in the realm of prophethood and sainthood after the perfection of spiritual struggle within it. One is guided by it except for that which cannot be attained by the intellect, which is the basis for religious obligation and the possibility of learning sciences, which is the absolute desire, and everything else is a veil and preliminary for it. It is that which God Almighty honored by specifying its attribution to Him, even though all guidance is from Him, as He said: "Say, 'Indeed, the guidance of God is the [true] guidance.'" It is called life in His saying: "Or is one who was dead and We gave him life and made for him light by which to walk among the people like one in darkness?" And the meaning of His saying: "So is one whose breast God has expanded to Islam, so that he is upon a light from his Lord [like one whose heart is constrained]?" As for *rushd* (right judgment), we mean by it the divine care that assists a person when he turns toward his objectives, so it guides him to what is good for him and averts him from what corrupts him, and this is from the inward, as He said: "And We had certainly given Abraham his sound judgment before, and We were of him Knowing." Thus, *rushd* is an expression for a motivating guidance toward the direction of happiness, moving one toward it. For a child, when he reaches maturity and is knowledgeable about safeguarding wealth, methods of trade, and increasing it, but despite that he squanders and does not desire to increase it, he is not called *rashid* (judicious), not for lacking guidance, but because his guidance is insufficient to move his innate drive. How many a person proceeds with what he knows harms him; he has been given guidance and is distinguished by it from the ignorant one who does not know it harms him, but he has not been given *rushd*. Thus, *rushd*, by this consideration, is more complete than mere guidance to the aspects of actions, and it is a great blessing. As for *tasdid* (setting aright), it is the directing of one's movements toward the aim and facilitating them for him, so that he proceeds firmly toward correctness in the shortest time. For guidance alone is not sufficient; rather, there must be a guidance that motivates the innate drive, and that is *rushd*. And *rushd* is not sufficient; rather, there must be facilitation of movements with the assistance of the limbs and instruments, so that what the innate drive was aroused for is accomplished. Thus, guidance is pure instruction; *rushd* is the awakening of the innate drive so it stirs and moves; and *tasdid* is aid and support by moving the limbs toward correctness. As for *ta'yid* (divine support), it is as if it gathers all; it is an expression for strengthening his affair with insight from within, and strengthening his grasp and the assistance of means from without. This is what is meant by His saying, Mighty and Majestic: "When I supported you with the Holy Spirit." Close to it is *'ismah* (divine protection), which is an expression for a divine presence that flows in the inward, by which a person is strengthened to pursue good and avoid evil, becoming as if prevented by an unseen inward barrier. This is what is meant by His saying: "And she certainly determined [to seduce] him, and he would have inclined to her had he not seen the proof of his Lord." These are the aggregates of blessings, and they will not be established except by what God grants of pure, penetrating understanding, attentive hearing, a vigilant, humble, and observant heart, a sincere teacher, wealth that is surplus beyond what falls short of necessities due to its scantness, yet is not so abundant as to distract from religion, and honor that protects one from the folly of fools and the injustice of enemies. Each one of these sixteen causes requires causes, and those causes require causes, until they ultimately end with the Last, the Guide of the perplexed and the Refuge of the desperate, and that is the Lord of lords and the Causer of causes. Since these causes are lengthy and a book such as this cannot bear their exhaustive treatment, we shall mention from them a model, so that the meaning of His saying may be known: "And if you should count the favors of God, you could not enumerate them." And with God is success.

(Clarifying the aspect of the model in the multitude of God's blessings, their sequence, and their being beyond enumeration and counting)

Know that we have gathered the blessings into sixteen kinds, and we have made bodily health a blessing among the blessings occurring in the later rank. This single blessing, if we wished to exhaustively trace its causes...

Through which this blessing is perfected, we have no power over it, but eating is one of the causes of health. So let us mention a selection from the totality of causes by which the blessing of eating is perfected. It is not hidden that eating is an action, and every action of this type is a movement, and every movement necessarily requires a moving body which is its instrument, and necessarily requires a capability for movement, and necessarily requires a will for movement, and necessarily requires knowledge of what is intended and perception of it. And eating necessarily requires something to be eaten, and the thing eaten necessarily requires an origin from which it is obtained, and necessarily requires a maker who prepares it. So let us mention the causes of perception, then the causes of wills, then the causes of capability, then the causes of the thing eaten, by way of indication, not by way of exhaustive detail.

(The First Part: On God Most High's Blessings in Creating the Causes of Perception)

Know that God Most High created plants, which are more perfect in existence than stone, clay, iron, copper, and all other minerals which do not grow and are not nourished. For the plant was created with a power by which it draws nourishment to itself from the direction of its root and its roots which are in the earth, and they are its instruments. Through them it draws nourishment; they are the delicate roots you see in every leaf, then their bases thicken, then they branch out, and they continue to become finer and branch out into hair-like roots spreading through the parts of the leaf until they disappear from sight. However, the plant, with all this, is deficient. For if it lacks nourishment brought to it and touching its root, it dries and withers, and it cannot seek nourishment from another location. For seeking only occurs with knowledge of what is sought and by moving towards it, and the plant is incapable of that. So from God Most High's blessing upon you is that He created for you the instruments of sensation and the instrument of movement for seeking nourishment. So look at the arrangement of God Most High's wisdom in creating the five senses, which are the instrument of perception. The first of them is the sense of touch. It was created for you so that if a burning fire or a cutting sword touches you, you feel it and flee from it. This is the first sense created for an animal, and no animal is conceivable except that it has this sense, for if it does not feel at all, it is not an animal. The lowest degree of sensation is to feel what does not adhere to and touch it, for sensation of what is distant from it is undoubtedly a more complete sensation. This sense exists for every animal, even the worm in the mud, for if a needle is stuck into it, it contracts to flee, unlike the plant, for the plant is cut and does not contract, as it does not feel the cutting. Yet, if only this sense were created for you, you would be deficient like the worm, unable to seek nourishment from where it is distant from you. Rather, only what touches you, you feel and draw to yourself. So you were in need of a sense by which you perceive what is distant from you. Thus He created for you smell, except that you perceive with it the scent but do not know from which direction it came. So you would need to wander much from various sides; perhaps you would stumble upon the nourishment whose scent you smelled, and perhaps you would not, so you would be in the utmost deficiency if only this were created for you. So He created for you sight, to perceive with it what is distant from you and perceive its direction, so you aim for that specific direction. Except that if only this were created for you, you would be deficient, for you would not perceive with it what is behind walls and veils. You would see nourishment with no veil between you and it, and you would see an enemy with no veil between you and him. But what has a veil between you and it, you would not see, and the veil might not be lifted except when the enemy is near, so you would be unable to flee. So He created for you hearing, so that you perceive with it sounds from behind walls and veils upon the occurrence of movements, because you perceive with sight only something present, but the absent you cannot know except through speech composed of letters and sounds perceived by the sense of hearing. So your need for it was great, and He created that for you, and you were distinguished by understanding speech from all other animals. Yet all that would not suffice you if the sense of taste were not created for you, for when nourishment reaches you, you would not perceive that it is agreeable or disagreeable to you, so you would eat it and perish, like a tree into whose root every liquid is poured, and it has no taste, so it draws it, and perhaps that becomes the cause of its drying up. Then, all that would not suffice you if another perception, called the common sense, were not created in the forefront of your brain, to which these five sensed things are conveyed and in which they gather. Were it not for it, the matter would be prolonged for you.
