For if you ate something yellow, for example, and found it bitter and disagreeable to you, so you left it, then if you saw it again, you would not know it is bitter and harmful unless you tasted it a second time, were it not for the common sense. For the eye sees the yellowness but does not perceive the bitterness, so how would you abstain? And taste perceives the bitterness but does not perceive the yellowness. So a judge is necessary, before whom the yellowness and the bitterness gather together, so that when you desire the yellowness, it judges that it is bitter, and thus you abstain from consuming it a second time. All this you share with the animals, for the sheep has all these senses. So if you had only this, you would be deficient, for the beast is tricked, so it is captured and does not know how to repel the trick.

Concerning the soul and how it may free itself when bound—it may even cast itself into a well without realizing that this will destroy it. For this reason, a beast may eat what it finds pleasing in the moment, only to be harmed thereafter, falling ill and dying, since it possesses only sensation of the present, while perception of consequences it lacks. But God, exalted be He, has distinguished and honored you with another attribute, nobler than all others: the intellect. Through it you perceive the harm and benefit of foods in both the immediate and the ultimate sense; through it you grasp how to cook and combine foods and prepare their means, thus benefiting through your intellect in eating, which is the cause of your health. This is among the finest benefits of the intellect and the least of its judgments—indeed, the greatest wisdom within it is the knowledge of God, exalted be He, knowledge of His acts, and knowledge of the wisdom in His creation. At that point, the benefit of the five senses in your regard is transformed, and the five senses become like spies and informants assigned to the regions of a kingdom, each entrusted with a specific matter: one with reports of colors, another with reports of sounds, another with reports of scents, another with reports of tastes, and another with reports of heat and cold, roughness and smoothness, softness and hardness, and the like. These spies and informants seize reports from the far reaches of the kingdom and deliver them to the common sense, which sits at the forefront of the brain like a keeper of records and dispatches at the king’s gate, gathering the reports and dispatches arriving from the regions of the world. It receives them sealed and passes them on, for it has no capacity except to receive, gather, and preserve them. As for knowing the realities within, it cannot. But when it encounters the discerning heart, which is the commander and king, it delivers the sealed reports to him. The king then examines them, uncovers from them the secrets of the kingdom, and rules within them with wondrous judgments that cannot be exhaustively detailed in this place. According to what becomes apparent to him of judgments and interests, he mobilizes the soldiers—which are the limbs—sometimes in pursuit, sometimes in flight, and sometimes in executing the plans that occur to him. This is the manner of God’s favor upon you in perceptions. Do not suppose that we have exhausted them, for the outward senses are but a portion of perceptions, and sight is one among the senses. The eye is a single instrument for it, yet the eye is composed of ten distinct layers: some are moistures, some are membranes—some membranes like a spider’s web, some like the chorion—and some of those moistures like egg white, some like jelly. Each of these ten layers has a quality, form, shape, configuration, accident, curvature, and composition. If a single layer among the ten or a single quality among the qualities of each layer were disturbed, sight would be impaired, and all physicians and oculists would be powerless regarding it. This is concerning one sense; judge by it the sense of hearing and the rest of the senses. Indeed, it is impossible to exhaust the judgment of God, exalted be He, and the varieties of His favor in the structure of sight and its layers, even in many volumes, while its entirety does not exceed a small walnut. So what is your thought concerning the entire body and its other members and wonders? These are but hints to the favors of God, exalted be He, in creating perceptions.

(The Second Aspect: On the Varieties of Favors in Creating Desires)

Know that if He had created sight for you so that you might perceive nourishment from a distance, but had not created in you an inclination in nature, a longing for it, and an appetite that urges you to movement, then the faculty would be idle. How many a sick person sees food, which is the most beneficial thing for him, yet his appetite has vanished, so he does not partake of it, and thus sight and perception remain idle in his regard. Therefore, it was necessary that you have an inclination toward what agrees with you, called appetite, and an aversion to what disagrees with you, called dislike, so that you might seek through appetite and flee through dislike. So God, exalted be He, created within you an appetite for food, subjected you to it, and entrusted it to you like a creditor who compels you to partake until you eat and are nourished, and thus survive through nourishment. This is something you share with animals, but not with plants. Then, this appetite, if it did not subside once the needed amount is taken, would lead to excess and destroy you. So God created for you dislike upon satiety, so that you might cease eating through it—unlike crops, which continually draw water if it flows at their base until they spoil, requiring a human to measure their nourishment according to need, watering them at one time and cutting off water at another. And just as He created this appetite in you so that you might eat and thereby your body endures, He created in you the appetite for intercourse so that you might engage in it and thereby your progeny endures. If we were to recount to you the wonders of God’s craftsmanship in creating the womb, creating menstrual blood, composing the fetus from semen and menstrual blood, the manner of creating the testicles and the vessels leading to them from the spine, which is the resting place of the sperm, the manner of the flow of the woman’s fluid from the chest by means of vessels, and the manner of the division of the concave uterus into molds into which the sperm falls...

Some of them take on male forms and fall into others taking on female forms, and the manner of managing them through the stages of their creation—as a clinging clot, then a lump of flesh, then bones, flesh, and blood—and the division of their parts into head, hand, leg, belly, back, and other limbs, would alone fill you with utter wonder at the varieties of God’s blessings upon you at the beginning of your creation, let alone what you see now. But we only intend to address God’s blessings in eating alone, so as not to prolong the discourse. Thus, the appetite for food is one type of desire, yet that alone does not suffice you, for destructive forces assail you from all sides. Had He not created anger within you, by which you repel all that opposes and displeases you, you would remain vulnerable to afflictions, and all you have acquired of nourishment would be taken from you, for everyone desires what is in your hands. You therefore need an impetus to repel and combat it, which is the impetus of anger, by which you repel all that opposes and displeases you. Yet even this does not suffice, for appetite and anger only urge toward what harms or benefits in the immediate present; as for the ultimate outcome, these desires are insufficient therein. So God created for you another desire, subservient to the direction of the intellect that discerns consequences, just as He created appetite and anger subservient to the perception of the senses that perceive the present state. Thus, you benefit by the intellect, for mere knowledge that this appetite, for example, harms you does not suffice to guard against it unless you have an inclination to act according to that knowledge. This desire is uniquely granted to you apart from beasts, as an honor to the children of Adam, just as you are uniquely granted knowledge of consequences. We have named this desire the religious impetus and elaborated on it in the Book of Patience more fully than here.

(Third Aspect: On God’s Blessings in Creating the Capacity and Instruments of Movement)

Know that sensation only yields perception, and desire has no meaning except inclination toward pursuit or avoidance. This is insufficient unless you possess the instruments of pursuit and avoidance. How many a sick person longs for something distant, perceiving it, yet cannot walk to it due to loss of a leg, or cannot take it due to loss of a hand or paralysis and numbness therein. Thus, instruments of movement and a capacity within those instruments for motion are necessary, so that their movement follows appetite in pursuit and aversion in avoidance. For this, God created for you limbs whose outward appearance you observe but whose secrets you do not know. Among them are those for pursuit and avoidance, such as legs for humans, wings for birds, and limbs for beasts; and among them are those for defense, such as weapons for humans and horns for animals. In this, animals differ greatly: some have many enemies and distant sustenance, needing swift movement, so He created wings for them to fly swiftly; some have four limbs, some two legs, some crawl. Mentioning this would be lengthy, so let us mention only the limbs by which eating is completed, that others may be inferred therefrom.

We say: Your sight of food from afar and your movement toward it do not suffice unless you are able to take it, so you needed a grasping instrument. Thus, God bestowed upon you the creation of two hands, long and extended toward things, containing many joints to move in directions, extending and bending toward you, unlike a fixed plank. Then He made the end of the hand broad by creating the palm, and divided the end of the palm into five parts, which are the fingers, arranging them in two rows so that the thumb is on one side and rotates around the remaining four. Had they been joined or stacked, your purpose would not be fully achieved. He positioned them such that if you spread them, they become a scoop for you; if you close them, they become a ladle; if you gather them, they become an instrument for striking; if you open then close them, they become an instrument for grasping. Then He created nails for them and supported the fingertips with them, so they do not fray and so you can pick up delicate things that fingers cannot contain, taking them with the tips of your nails.

Now suppose you take food with your hands—how does this suffice unless it reaches the stomach, which is internal? There must be a vestibule from the exterior to it, so that food may enter through it. Thus, He made the mouth a passage to the stomach, with many wisdoms besides being a passage for food to the stomach. Then, if you place food in the mouth as a single piece, swallowing is not easy, so you need a mill to grind the food. Thus, He created for you two jaws from bones and set in them teeth, aligning the upper molars with the lower to grind the food. Food sometimes needs breaking, sometimes cutting, then grinding thereafter. So He divided the teeth into broad grinders like molars and sharp cutters like incisors.

And to what is suitable for crushing, like the canines, then He made the joint of the jaws loose so that the lower jaw advances and recedes, rotating upon the upper jaw like the rotation of a millstone. Were it not for that, it would only be possible for one to strike against the other, like the clapping of hands, for example, and with that, grinding would not be accomplished. So He made the lower jaw move with a circular motion and the upper jaw fixed, not moving. So look at the wondrous craftsmanship of God, exalted is He, for every millstone made by creation has its lower stone fixed and its upper stone rotating, except this millstone which God, exalted is He, made, for its lower part rotates upon its upper part. Glory be to Him, how magnificent is His affair, how mighty His dominion, how perfect His proof, and how vast His favor.

Then consider, if you placed the food in the cavity of the mouth, how would the food move to beneath the teeth, or how would the teeth draw it to themselves, and how could the hand maneuver inside the mouth? So look how God has bestowed favor upon you by creating the tongue, for it circulates in the sides of the mouth and returns the food from the center to the teeth as needed, like a shovel that returns food to the millstone. This is besides its benefit for taste and the wonders of the power of speech and judgment, which we do not elaborate in mentioning.

Then consider, if you cut and ground the food while it is dry, you would not be able to swallow it except by it slipping into the throat with some moisture. So look how God, exalted is He, created beneath the tongue a spring from which saliva flows and pours forth according to need, until the food is kneaded with it. So look how He subjugated it for this matter, for you see the food from a distance, then the jaws stir for service and the saliva pours forth until your cheeks water, and the food is still far from you.

Then, this ground and kneaded food—who conveys it to the stomach while it is in the mouth? You cannot push it with your hand, nor is there a hand in the stomach to extend and pull the food. So look how God, exalted is He, prepared the esophagus and the larynx and placed upon its head layers that open to take the food, then constrict so that the food turns over by its pressure and falls into the stomach through the passage of the esophagus.

When the food reaches the stomach, being bread and cut fruit, it is not suitable to become flesh, bone, and blood in this state. Rather, it must be cooked completely until its parts become homogeneous. So God, exalted is He, created the stomach in the form of a cooking pot. The food falls into it, and it contains it, and the doors close upon it. It remains residing within until digestion and ripening are complete through the heat that surrounds the stomach from the internal organs, for on its right side is the liver, on its left the spleen, in front the chest, and behind the flesh of the back. The heat reaches it from the heating of these organs from the sides until the food is cooked and becomes a fluid, homogeneous substance suitable for permeating the cavities of the veins. At that time, it resembles barley water in the homogeneity of its parts and its state, yet it is still not suitable for nourishment.

So God, exalted is He, created between it and the liver passages from the veins and made for it many openings so that the food pours into them and ends at the liver. The liver is a compound from the clay of blood, as if it were blood, and in it are many hair-like veins spread throughout the parts of the liver. The thin, permeating food pours into them and spreads through its parts until the power of the liver takes control of it and dyes it with the color of blood. It settles there until it attains another ripening and acquires the form of pure blood suitable for nourishing the organs, except that the heat of the liver is what ripens this blood.

From this blood, two residues are generated, as is generated in all that is cooked: one resembling the dregs and sediment, which is the black bile, and the other resembling the froth, which is the yellow bile. If the two residues were not separated from it, the temperament of the organs would spoil. So God, exalted is He, created the gallbladder and the spleen and gave each of them a neck extended to the liver, entering into its cavity. The gallbladder draws the bilious residue, and the spleen draws the black, sedimented residue, leaving the blood pure, containing nothing but increased thinness and moisture due to its wateriness. Were it not for that, it would not spread in those hair-like veins nor emerge from them ascending to the organs.

So God, glorified is He, created the two kidneys and brought out from each of them a long neck to the liver. Among the wonders of God's wisdom, exalted is He, is that their neck is not inside the cavity of the liver but connected to the veins rising from the hump of the liver—among the wonders of God's wisdom, exalted is He, is that their neck is not inside the cavity of the liver but connected to the veins rising from the hump of the liver—so that it draws what is adjacent to it after rising from the fine veins in the liver, for if it drew before that, it would be thick and would not exit the veins. When the wateriness is separated from it, the blood has become pure from...

The three waste products are purified from all that corrupts nourishment. Then God, exalted be He, caused veins to emerge from the liver, then divided them after their emergence into sections and branches, each section with its branches, and that spread throughout the entire body, from the crown of the head to the foot, outwardly and inwardly. Pure blood flows therein and reaches all the limbs, until the divided veins become hair-like, like the veins of leaves and trees, such that they cannot be perceived by sight. Nourishment reaches from them by seepage to all the limbs. If an affliction befalls the gallbladder so that it does not attract the bilious waste, the blood becomes corrupt and from it arise bilious diseases such as jaundice, pustules, and erysipelas. If an affliction befalls the spleen so that it does not attract the melancholic humor, melancholic diseases occur, such as vitiligo, leprosy, melancholy, and others. If the watery [waste] is not driven toward the kidneys, dropsy and other [ailments] arise from it.

Then observe the wisdom of the Wise Creator, how He arranged benefits upon these three base waste products. As for the gallbladder, it attracts with one of its necks and casts out with the other neck into the intestines, so that a slippery moisture is obtained for it in the food residue, and a pungency occurs in the intestines which moves them for expulsion, so they contract until the residue is expelled and slips out, and its bile is for that purpose. As for the spleen, it transforms that waste with a transformation by which acidity and astringency are produced within it, then it sends from it something each day to the mouth of the stomach, which stirs the appetite with its acidity, alerts it, and arouses it, and it expels the remainder with the residue. As for the kidney, it is nourished by the blood within that watery [waste] and sends the remainder to the bladder.

Let us confine ourselves to this extent in clarifying the blessings of God, exalted be He, in the means He prepared for eating. If we were to mention how the liver needs the heart and the brain, and how each one of these principal organs needs its companion, and the manner of the branching of the pulsating veins from the heart to the rest of the body, and through them sensation reaches, and the manner of the branching of the quiescent veins from the liver to the rest of the body, and through them nourishment reaches, and then the manner of the composition of the limbs and the number of their bones, muscles, veins, tendons, ligaments, cartilages, and humors, the discourse would be prolonged. All of that is needed for eating and for other matters besides. Indeed, in the human being are thousands of muscles, veins, and nerves, differing in smallness and largeness, fineness and coarseness, and abundance and paucity of division. There is not a single one of them except that within it is one wisdom, or two, or three, or four, up to ten and more. All of that is a blessing from God, exalted be He, upon you. If from among them a moving vein were to become still, or a still vein were to move, you would perish, O wretched one. So look at the blessing of God, exalted be He, upon you—or will you not thereby be strengthened for gratitude? For you know of the blessing of God, glorified be He, only eating, and it is the basest of them. Then you know of it only that you hunger, so you eat. The donkey also knows that it hungers so it eats, tires so it sleeps, desires so it copulates, is roused so it rises, and gallops. If you know of yourself only what the donkey knows, how will you fulfill gratitude for God's blessing upon you? This to which we have alluded with brevity is but a drop from one sea of the seas of God's blessings. So extrapolate generally what we have omitted from the totality of what we have known, for fear of prolixity. And the totality of what we have known and what all creation has known, in comparison to what they have not known of the blessings of God, exalted be He, is less than a drop from a sea. Yet, whoever knows something of this perceives a whiff of the meanings of His saying, exalted be He: "And if you should count the favors of God, you could not enumerate them."

Then observe how God, exalted be He, linked the soundness of these limbs and the soundness of their benefits, perceptions, and powers to a subtle vapor that ascends from the four humors and has its resting place in the heart, and courses through the entire body by means of the pulsating veins. It does not reach any part of the body's parts except that it occasions within those parts what is needed of sensory and perceptive power, power of movement, and others—like a lamp that is carried to the corners of a house; no part is reached except that light is obtained for the parts of the house because of its arrival, by the creation and invention of God, exalted be He, but He made the lamp a cause for it by His wisdom. This subtle vapor is what the physicians call the spirit (rūḥ). Its place is the heart. Its likeness is the fiery substance of the lamp. The heart is like the lamp-holder. The black blood within the interior of the heart is like the wick. Nourishment is like the oil. The apparent life in the rest of the body's limbs because of it is like the light of the lamp for the entirety of the house. And just as the lamp is extinguished if its oil is cut off, so too the lamp of the spirit is extinguished whenever its nourishment is cut off. And just as the wick may burn and become ash such that it does not accept oil, so the lamp is extinguished despite an abundance of oil. Likewise, the blood upon which this vapor depends...

The heart may burn with excessive heat of the heart and be extinguished while nourishment is present, for it does not accept the nourishment by which the spirit remains, just as ashes do not accept oil in a way that fire clings to it. And just as a lamp is sometimes extinguished due to an internal cause, as we have mentioned, and sometimes due to an external cause, like a violent wind, so too the spirit is sometimes extinguished due to an internal cause and sometimes due to an external cause, which is killing. And just as the extinguishing of a lamp—by the depletion of oil, the corruption of the wick, a violent wind, or a person putting it out—occurs only by causes decreed in God’s knowledge, arranged, and all of that is by divine measure, so too is the extinguishing of the spirit. And just as the extinguishing of the lamp is the end of its time of existence, making that its appointed term which was decreed for it in the Mother of the Book, so too is the extinguishing of the spirit. And just as when the lamp is extinguished, the entire house becomes dark, so when the spirit is extinguished, the entire body becomes dark and the lights it used to derive from the spirit depart from it—these being the lights of sensations, power, volitions, and all else gathered by the meaning of the word “life.” This, too, is a concise symbol pointing to another realm among the realms of God’s blessings and the wonders of His creation and wisdom, so that one may know that “if the sea were ink for the words of my Lord, the sea would be exhausted before the words of my Lord were exhausted,” glorified and exalted is He. So woe to him who disbelieves in God, woe and perdition to him who disbelieves in His blessings, perdition.

If you say: You have described the spirit and likened it, yet the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), when asked about the spirit, did not add more than saying, “Say, ‘The spirit is from the command of my Lord,’” and did not describe it to them in this manner. Know that this is an oversight regarding the homonymy present in the term “spirit,” for “spirit” is applied to many meanings, which we shall not prolong in enumerating. We have only described, among them, a subtle body that physicians call “spirit,” and they have known its attributes, existence, how it flows through the limbs, and how sensation and faculties occur in the limbs through it—so much so that when some limb becomes numb, they know that is due to a blockage occurring in the passage of this spirit. Thus, they do not treat the site of numbness but rather the origins of the nerves and the locations of the blockage within them, treating them with what opens the blockage. For this subtle body, due to its fineness, permeates the network of nerves, and through it is conveyed from the heart to all the limbs. What physicians’ knowledge ascends to concerning it is an easy, lowly matter. As for the spirit that is the origin, which when corrupted corrupts the entire body for it, that is a secret among the secrets of God, exalted is He. We have not described it, nor is there permission to describe it, except by saying it is a divine command, as He, exalted is He, said: “Say, ‘The spirit is from the command of my Lord.’” Divine commands cannot be comprehended by intellects; rather, the intellects of most creation are bewildered by them. As for fancies and delusions, they are necessarily deficient in grasping them, just as sight is deficient in perceiving sounds. Intellects bound by substance and accident, confined within their narrow confines, tremble at mentioning the principles of describing it. Nothing of its description is grasped by the intellect, but rather by another light, higher and nobler than intellect, which shines in the realm of prophethood and saintliness. Its relation to intellect is like the relation of intellect to fancy and imagination. God has created creation in stages. Just as a child perceives sensible things but does not perceive intelligible things because that is a stage he has not yet reached, so too does the mature person perceive intelligible things but does not perceive what is beyond them because that is a stage he has not yet reached. Indeed, it is a noble station, a sweet drink, and a high rank wherein one gazes upon the gardens of Truth with the light of faith and certainty. That drink is too precious to be a common path for every comer; rather, only one after another is granted insight into it. For the Presence of Truth there is a forecourt, and at the forefront of the forecourt there is a spacious field and arena. At the beginning of the arena is a threshold that is the abode of that divine command. Whoever has no pass to this threshold, nor a witnessing from the guardian of the threshold, finds it impossible to reach the arena, let alone attain what lies beyond it of lofty visions. Therefore, it is said: “Whoever does not know himself does not know his Lord.” How could this be found in the storehouse of physicians? And from where would a physician observe it? Rather, the meaning called “spirit” by the physician, in relation to this divine command, is like the ball moved by the king’s scepter in relation to the king. So whoever knows the medical spirit and thinks he has grasped the divine command is like one who sees the ball moved by the king’s scepter and thinks he has seen the king, and there is no doubt that his error is grave, and this error is far graver. And since the intellects by which obligation is established and by which worldly interests are perceived are intellects deficient in contemplating the essence of this matter, God did not permit His Messenger (peace be upon him) to speak about it; rather, He commanded him to speak to people according to their intellects. God did not mention anything of the reality of this matter in His Book, but He mentioned its relation.

His action is mentioned, though His essence is not. As for His attribution, it is in His saying, exalted is He: "From the command of my Lord." As for His action, it is mentioned in His saying, exalted is He: "O soul at peace, return to your Lord, well-pleased and well-pleasing. Enter among My servants, and enter My Paradise." Let us now return to the purpose, for the intent is to mention the blessings of God, exalted is He, in eating. We have already mentioned some of God's blessings, exalted is He, in the instruments of eating.

(The Fourth Aspect: Concerning the blessings of God, exalted is He, in the sources from which foods are obtained and become suitable for man to subsequently prepare through his craft.)

Know that foods are many, and God, exalted is He, has created in them countless wonders and successive, endless causes. To mention this for every food would be lengthy, for foods are either medicines, or fruits, or nourishments. Let us take the nourishments, for they are the foundation, and from their totality, let us take a single grain of wheat, leaving aside all other nourishments. We say: If you found a grain or grains and ate them, they would perish and you would remain hungry. How greatly you would need that grain to grow in itself, increase, and multiply until it suffices for your complete need. So God, exalted is He, created within the grain of wheat powers by which it is nourished, just as He created within you. For the plant only differs from you in sensation and movement; it does not differ from you in nourishment, for it is nourished by water and draws it into its interior via roots, just as you are nourished and draw sustenance. We will not elaborate on describing the plant's instruments for drawing nourishment to itself, but will allude to its nourishment. We say: Just as wood and earth do not nourish you, but you require specific food, so too the grain is not nourished by everything; rather, it requires something specific. This is evidenced by the fact that if you left it in a house, it would not increase, for only air surrounds it, and mere air is not suitable for its nourishment. If you left it in water, it would not increase. If you left it in earth with no water, it would not increase. Rather, it must be in earth containing water, so that its water mixes with the earth and becomes mud. To this is the allusion in His saying, exalted is He: "Then let man look at his food: We poured down water in abundance, then We split the earth wide open, and caused to grow therein grain, and vines, and herbs, and olives, and palms." Then water and earth alone are not sufficient, for if it were left in damp, solid, compacted earth, it would not sprout due to the lack of air. Thus, it needs to be placed in loose, crumbly earth into which air can penetrate. Then, the air does not move to it by itself, so it needs a wind to move the air and strike it with force and violence upon the earth so that it penetrates it. To this is the allusion in His saying, exalted is He: "And We send the fertilizing winds." Their fertilization lies in effecting the coupling between air, water, and earth. Yet all of that would not benefit you if it were in extreme cold and harsh winter, so you need the heat of spring and summer. Thus, the need of its nourishment for these four [elements] has become clear. Consider what each one requires. Water needs to flow to the land of cultivation from seas, springs, rivers, and streams. Consider how God created the seas, made springs gush forth, and caused rivers to flow from them. Then the land may be elevated, and the waters do not rise to it. Consider how God, exalted is He, created the clouds and how He subjected the winds to drive them, by His leave, to the regions of the earth—clouds heavy and laden with water. Then consider how He sends it down pouring upon the lands in the time of spring and autumn according to need. Consider how He created the mountains as reservoirs for water, from which springs gush forth gradually. Had they emerged all at once, the lands would have flooded, and crops and livestock perished. The blessings of God in the mountains, clouds, seas, and rains cannot be enumerated. As for heat, it does not arise between water and earth, for both are cold. Consider how He subjugated the sun and how He created it, despite its distance from the earth, to heat the earth at one time and not another, so that cold occurs when cold is needed and heat when heat is needed. This is one of the wisdoms of the sun, and the wisdoms in it are too numerous to count. Then, when the plant rises above the earth, the fruits require firmness and solidity to form, so they need moisture to ripen them. Consider how He created the moon and made among its specific properties moistening, just as He made among the specific properties of the sun heating. Thus, it ripens the fruits and colors them by the decree of the Creator, the Wise. For this reason, if trees were in a shade that prevented the rising of the sun, moon, and other celestial bodies upon them, they would be corrupt and deficient. Indeed, a small tree becomes corrupt if a large tree shades it. You may recognize the moistening of the moon by exposing your head to it at night; moisture, expressed as a cold, will overcome your head. Just as it moistens your head, it also moistens the fruit. We shall not prolong discussion of what cannot be fully encompassed, but say: Every celestial body in the sky...

Indeed, He has subjugated each kind for a benefit, just as the sun is subjugated for heating and the moon for moistening, so not one of them is devoid of numerous wisdoms which human strength cannot enumerate. Were it not so, their creation would have been in vain and futile, and the saying of the Exalted would not hold true: "Our Lord, You have not created this in vain" (Qur'an 3:191), and His Mighty and Majestic saying: "We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them in play" (Qur'an 21:16). And just as there is no limb in the limbs of your body except for a benefit, so there is no limb in the limbs of the body of the world except for a benefit. The entire world is like a single person, and its individual bodies are like limbs for it, cooperating as the limbs of your body cooperate within the totality of your body. Elaborating on this would be lengthy.

You should not think that believing the stars, the sun, and the moon are subjugated by the command of God, the Exalted, in matters made to be causes for them by the decree of Wisdom, contradicts the Sacred Law due to what is reported therein of the prohibition against believing the astrologers and against the science of the stars. Rather, what is prohibited regarding the stars is two matters: First, that you believe they are agents producing their effects independently and that they are not subjugated under the management of a Manager who created and overpowered them—this is disbelief. Second, believing the astrologers in the details of what they inform about of effects which all of creation does not commonly perceive, for they say that out of ignorance. Indeed, the knowledge of the decrees of the stars was a miracle for some of the prophets, peace be upon them, then that knowledge became effaced, so nothing remained except what is mixed, wherein correctness is not distinguished from error. Thus, believing the planets are causes for effects that occur by the creation of God, the Exalted, on earth, in plants, and in animals, is not detrimental to the religion; rather, it is true. But claiming knowledge of those effects in detail while being ignorant is detrimental to the religion.

Therefore, if you have a garment you washed and wish to dry it, and someone else says to you, "Take out the garment and spread it, for the sun has risen and the day has grown hot, and the air [is favorable]," you are not obliged to disbelieve him, nor are you obliged to deny him by attributing the heat of the air to the rising of the sun. And if you ask about a change in a person's face and he says, "The sun struck me on the road, so my face darkened," you are not obliged to disbelieve him in that. Judge by this all other effects, except that some effects are known and some are unknown. The unknown is not permissible to claim knowledge of. The known: some of it is known to all people, like the occurrence of light and heat with the rising of the sun; and some of it is known to some people, like the occurrence of a cold with the rising of the moon. Therefore, the celestial bodies were not created in vain; rather, within them are numerous, uncountable wisdoms.

For this reason, the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, looked at the sky and recited the saying of the Exalted: "Our Lord, You have not created this in vain; glory be to You! So protect us from the punishment of the Fire" (Qur'an 3:191). Then he, peace be upon him, said: "Woe to one who recites this verse and then wipes his mustache with it." Its meaning is that he recites and leaves off contemplation, limiting his understanding of the dominion of the heavens to knowing the color of the sky and the light of the stars—and that is something even beasts know. So whoever is content with knowing only that is the one who has wiped his mustache with it. For God, the Exalted, in the dominion of the heavens, the horizons, the souls, and the animals, has wonders which those who love God, the Exalted, seek to know. For whoever loves a scholar is constantly occupied with seeking his compositions to increase, by further standing before the wonders of his knowledge, in love for him. Such is the affair with the wonders of God's, the Exalted, craftsmanship, for the entire world is from His composition. Indeed, the composition of composers is from His composition which He composed by means of the hearts of His servants. So if you marvel at a composition, do not marvel at the composer, but at the One who subjugated the composer for his composition by what He bestowed upon him of His guidance, correction, and instruction. Just as if you see the puppets of a magician dancing and moving in measured, proportionate movements, do not marvel at the puppets, for they are moved puppets, not movers. But marvel at the skill of the magician who moves them by subtle, hidden strings. Therefore, the intended meaning is that the nourishment of plants is not complete except by water, air, the sun, the moon, and the stars, and that is not complete except by the celestial spheres in which they are fixed, and the spheres are not complete except by their movements, and their movements are not complete except by celestial angels who move them. And so this continues to distant causes which we have omitted mentioning, indicating by what we have mentioned what we have omitted. Let us limit ourselves to this in mentioning the causes of plant nourishment.

(The Fifth Aspect: On the Graces of God, the Exalted, in the Means that Convey Food to You)
Know that all these foods are not found in every place; rather, they have specific conditions for which they exist in some places and not others. People are spread across the face of the earth, and foods may be distant from them, with seas and deserts intervening between them and the food. So observe how God, the Exalted, has subjugated the merchants and imposed upon them the greed of love for wealth and the desire for profit, while in most cases nothing suffices them, but...

They gather wealth, only for ships to sink with it, or for highway robbers to plunder it, or for them to die in some lands, whereupon rulers seize it. The best of their situations is that their heirs take it—and they are their fiercest enemies, if only they knew. So observe how God has subjected them to ignorance and heedlessness, such that they endure hardships in pursuit of profit, risk dangers, and gamble with their lives by sailing the seas. They carry foods and various necessities from the farthest East and West to you. And observe how God, exalted is He, taught them the craft of shipbuilding and the manner of sailing them. And observe how He created animals and subdued them for riding and carrying loads across deserts. Look at the camel, how it was created; at the horse, how it was endowed with swift movement; at the donkey, how it was made patient with fatigue; and at the camels, how they traverse deserts and cover stages under heavy burdens while hungry and thirsty. And observe how God, exalted is He, set them in motion by means of ships and animals on land and sea, to carry to you foods and all other necessities. Ponder what the animals require in terms of their provisions, tools, and fodder, and what the ships require. Indeed, God, exalted is He, created all of that to the extent of need and beyond need. Enumerating it is not possible, and this extends to matters beyond counting, which we omit for the sake of brevity.

(Sixth Aspect: On the Preparation of Foods)
Know that what grows in the earth from plants and what is created of animals cannot be bitten and eaten as they are. Rather, each one inevitably requires preparation, cooking, combining, and cleaning by discarding some parts and keeping others, among countless other matters. To detail this for every food would be lengthy, so let us take a single loaf of bread and consider what is needed for that one loaf to become round and suitable for eating, from after the seed is cast into the earth. First, the farmer is needed to plow and prepare the earth, then the ox that tills the soil, the plow, and all its implements. Then, after that, the tending by watering for a period, then clearing the earth of weeds, then harvesting, then threshing and cleaning, then grinding, then kneading the dough, then baking. So reflect on the number of these actions we have mentioned and those we have not, and the number of persons performing them, and the number of tools required from iron, wood, stone, and other materials. And look at the work of craftsmen in preparing the tools of plowing, grinding, and baking—from carpenter and blacksmith and others. And consider the blacksmith’s need for iron, lead, and copper. And observe how God, exalted is He, created mountains, stones, and minerals, and how He made the earth in adjoining, varied pieces. If you investigate, you will know that a single loaf does not become round and suitable for your eating, O poor one, unless more than a thousand craftsmen have worked upon it. Begin from the King who drives the clouds to release water, down to the last of the works from the side of the angels, until the turn reaches the work of man. When it becomes round, its requirement approaches nearly seven thousand craftsmen, each craftsman a foundation among the foundations of crafts by which the welfare of creation is perfected. Then ponder the multitude of human actions in those tools, to the extent that the needle—a small tool whose benefit is sewing the garment that protects you from cold—its form is not completed from iron suitable for a needle except after passing through the hands of the needle-maker twenty-five times, undertaking a task each time. If God, exalted is He, had not gathered the lands and subdued the servants, and you were in need of making the sickle with which you harvest wheat, for example, after it grows, your lifetime would expire and you would be incapable of it. Do you not see how God has guided His servant, whom He created from a filthy drop, to perform these wondrous works and strange crafts? Look at the scissors, for example: two matching blades, one closing upon the other, so they take the thing together and cut it swiftly. Had God, exalted is He, not unveiled the way of making it through His grace and generosity to those before us, and we were in need of deducing the method for it through our thought, then extracting iron from stone, and obtaining the tools with which the scissors are made—even if one of us had the lifespan of Noah and were given the most complete intellects, his life would fall short of deducing the method for perfecting this tool alone, let alone others. So glory be to Him who joined the sighted with the blind, and glory be to Him who withheld [prophethood] from the prophets despite this clarity. Now consider if your town were devoid of, for example, the miller, or the blacksmith, or the cupper—who is the lowliest of workers—or the weaver, or any one from the totality of craftsmen, what harm would befall you and how all your affairs would be thrown into disorder. So glory be to Him who subdued some servants to others, such that His will is accomplished through them and His wisdom is perfected. Let us also be brief in this class, for the purpose is to alert to the blessings.

Without exhaustive enumeration.
                      (The Seventh Aspect: On the Reformers of Affairs)

Know that these craftsmen who reform foods and other matters—if their opinions were to diverge and their natures were to clash, clashing like the natures of wild beasts, they would be scattered and distanced, and none would benefit from another. Rather, they would be like wild beasts, not contained in a single place nor united by a single purpose. So observe how God, Exalted is He, has harmonized their hearts and subjected them to familiarity and love: "If you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have harmonized their hearts, but God harmonized them." Thus, for the sake of harmony and the mutual recognition of spirits, they gathered and united, building cities and towns, arranging dwellings and houses close and neighboring, and organizing markets, caravanserais, and all other kinds of places, the enumeration of which would be lengthy. Then, this love vanishes due to objectives they compete for and vie over, for in human nature lie anger, envy, and rivalry, which lead to fighting and discord. So observe how God, Exalted is He, empowered rulers and supported them with strength, preparation, and means, casting their awe into the hearts of the subjects until they submitted to them willingly and unwillingly, and how He guided the rulers to the path of reforming the lands until they arranged the parts of a land as if they were parts of a single person, cooperating for a single purpose, each part benefiting from the others. Thus, they appointed chiefs, judges, prisons, and market overseers, compelling the creation to the law of justice and obliging them to mutual assistance and cooperation, until the blacksmith benefits from the butcher, the baker, and all the people of the town, and all of them benefit from the blacksmith; and the cupper benefits from the plowman, and the plowman from the cupper, and each one benefits from every other due to their arrangement, gathering, and discipline under the order and gathering of the ruler, just as all the limbs of the body cooperate and some benefit from others. And observe how He sent the prophets, peace be upon them, until they reformed the rulers who reform the subjects, and taught them the laws of the Sacred Law in preserving justice among creation and the laws of governance in controlling them, and they unveiled from the rulings of leadership and sovereignty and the rulings of jurisprudence that by which they were guided to reforming the world, let alone what they directed them to in reforming religion. And observe how God, Exalted is He, reformed the prophets through the angels, and how the angels reformed one another until it culminates in the intimate angel who has no intermediary between him and God, Exalted is He. Thus, the baker bakes the dough, the miller reforms the grain by grinding, the plowman reforms it by harvesting, the blacksmith reforms the tools of the plowman, the carpenter reforms the tools of the blacksmith, and likewise all masters of crafts who reform the tools of foods; and the ruler reforms the craftsmen, and the prophets reform the scholars who are their heirs, and the scholars reform the rulers, and the angels reform the prophets until it culminates in the presence of Lordship, which is the fountainhead of every order, the dawning place of every beauty and comeliness, and the origin of every arrangement and composition. All of that is a favor from the Lord of lords and the Causer of causes. Were it not for His grace and generosity when He, Exalted is He, said: "And those who strive in Us—We will surely guide them to Our ways," we would not have been guided to this small portion of the favors of God, Exalted is He. And were it not that He prevented us from aspiring with the eye of greed to encompass the reality of His favors, we would have yearned to seek encompassing and exhaustive enumeration. But He, Exalted is He, prevented us by the decree of overpowering might and power, as He, Exalted is He, said: "And if you should count the favors of God, you could not enumerate them." So if we speak, it is by His permission we expand; and if we are silent, it is by His overpowering we contract. For there is no giver of what He withholds, and no withholder of what He gives, for in every moment of life before death we hear with the hearing of the hearts the call of the Compelling Sovereign: "To whom belongs the dominion this day? To God, the One, the Overpowering." So praise be to God who distinguished us from the disbelievers and made us hear this call before the expiration of lifespans.

    (The Eighth Aspect: On Clarifying the Favor of God, Exalted is He, in Creating the Angels, peace be upon them)

What has preceded concerning the favor of God in creating the angels by reforming the prophets, peace be upon them, guiding them, and delivering revelation to them is not hidden from you. And do not think that their actions are limited to that extent alone. Rather, the categories of angels, despite their multitude and the ordering of their ranks, are generally confined to three categories: the earthly angels, the heavenly angels, and the bearers of the Throne. So observe how God, Exalted is He, has entrusted them with you concerning what relates to eating and nourishment that we have mentioned, apart from what goes beyond that of guidance, instruction, and others. And know that every part of your body, indeed every part of a plant, does not receive nourishment except that seven angels are entrusted with it—that being the least—up to ten, up to a hundred, up to beyond that.

The explanation is that nourishment means one part of the food replaces another part that has perished. That food ultimately becomes blood, then turns into flesh and bone. Once it becomes flesh and bone, your nourishment is complete. Blood and flesh are bodies without power, knowledge, or choice; they do not move by themselves nor change by themselves. Mere natural disposition is insufficient for their progression through stages, just as wheat by itself does not become flour, then dough, then a round, baked loaf except through a craftsman. Similarly, blood by itself does not become flesh, bone, veins, and nerves except through a craftsman. The craftsmen inwardly are the angels, just as the craftsmen outwardly are the people of the town. God Almighty has bestowed upon you blessings both apparent and hidden, so you should not be heedless of His hidden blessings.

I say there must be an angel who draws the nourishment to the vicinity of the flesh and bone, for nourishment does not move by itself. There must be another angel who holds the nourishment in its place. There must be a third who clothes it with the form of blood. There must be a fourth who covers it with the form of flesh and veins or bone. There must be a fifth who expels the excess beyond the need of the nourishment. There must be a sixth who attaches what has acquired the quality of bone to the bone and what has acquired the quality of flesh to the flesh, so that it is not separated. There must be a seventh who oversees the measures in attachment, joining to the round what does not nullify its roundness, to the broad what does not remove its breadth, and to the hollow what does not void its hollowness, preserving for each its due measure of need. For if, for example, nourishment were gathered on the child’s nose as much as is gathered on his thigh, his nose would become large, its hollowness would be nullified, and its form and creation would be deformed. Rather, it must be conveyed to the eyelids despite their thinness, to the pupil despite its clarity, to the thighs despite their thickness, and to the bone despite its hardness, what is suitable for each in terms of measure and shape; otherwise the form would be corrupted, some places would swell, and some would weaken. Indeed, if this just angel did not observe this distribution and apportioning, and conveyed to the child’s head and the rest of his body from the nourishment what causes growth, except to one leg for example, that leg would remain as it was in its state of smallness while the entire body grew large. Then you would see a person with the bulk of a man but with one leg like that of a child, so he would not benefit from himself at all. The observance of this geometry in this distribution is entrusted to an angel from the angels. Do not think that blood by its nature engineers its own form, for one who attributes these matters to nature is ignorant and does not know what he says. These are the earthly angels, and they are occupied with you while you rest in sleep and wander in heedlessness, yet they rectify the nourishment within you without you having any awareness of them. This is in every part of your being that is indivisible, until some parts like the eye and the heart require more than a hundred angels—we have omitted detailing that for brevity.

The earthly angels receive support from the heavenly angels in a known order, whose essence is comprehended only by God Almighty. The heavenly angels receive support from the bearers of the Throne, and the Benefactor upon all of them with empowerment, guidance, and rectification is the Guardian, the Holy, the One unique in sovereignty and dominion, might and majesty, the Compeller of the heavens and the earth, the Owner of the Kingdom, Possessor of Glory and Honor. The reports concerning the angels entrusted with the heavens and the earth, and the parts of plants and animals—even every drop of rain and every cloud drifting from one side to another—are too numerous to count, so we have omitted citing them.

If you say: Why were these actions not entrusted to a single angel, and why do I need seven angels? Wheat also needs one to grind it first, then one to separate the bran from it and expel the waste second, then one to pour water on it third, then one to knead it fourth, then one to divide it into round lumps fifth, then one to flatten them into broad loaves sixth, then one to stick them to the oven seventh. Yet all that may be undertaken by a single man who manages it alone. So why are the works of the angels inwardly not like the works of humans outwardly? Know that the creation of the angels differs from the creation of humans. There is not one of them except that he is singular in attribute, with no mixture or composition at all. Thus each of them has only one action, alluded to in His saying, exalted is He: "And there is none of us except that he has a known station." Therefore, there is no rivalry or fighting among them. Rather, their example in the specification of each one’s rank and action is like the example of the five senses: sight does not compete with hearing in perceiving sounds, nor does smell compete with them, nor do they contend over smell. It is not like the hand and foot, for you may strike weakly with the toes of the foot and thereby compete with the hand, or you may strike another with your head and thereby compete with the hand.

It is an instrument for striking, unlike a single human who personally undertakes grinding, kneading, and baking. This represents a kind of deviation and swerving from justice, caused by the differing attributes and varying motives of man. For he is not singular in attribute, and thus cannot be singular in action. Therefore, we see man obeying God at one time and disobeying Him at another, due to the variance of his motives and attributes. This is not possible in the nature of the angels; rather, they are created for obedience—may God be pleased with him, peace be upon him, may God be pleased with him, may God be pleased with him, may God be pleased with him—there is no scope for disobedience in their case. Thus, they do not disobey God in what He commands them, and they do what they are commanded, glorifying Him night and day without ceasing. The one bowing among them is ever bowing, the one prostrating is ever prostrating, the one standing is ever standing; there is no variation in their actions, nor any weariness. Each one has a known station which he does not transgress, and their obedience to God Almighty, from a place where there is no scope for opposition within them, can be likened to the obedience of your limbs to you. For whenever you decisively will to open the eyelids, the sound eyelid does not hesitate or differ, obeying you at one time and disobeying you at another; rather, it is as if it awaits your command, and thus it opens and closes continuously at your signal. This resembles it in one aspect but differs in another, for the eyelid has no knowledge of the movement it performs, whether opening or closing, while the angels are living beings who know what they do. Therefore, this is God's blessing upon you in the earthly and heavenly angels, and your need for them is only for the purpose of eating, apart from all other movements and needs. We have not prolonged mentioning them, for this is another category of blessings, and the totality of categories cannot be enumerated, let alone the individual items encompassed within the totalities of categories. Thus, God Almighty has showered His blessings upon you, both apparent and hidden. Then He said: "And leave the outward sin and the inward." (Qur'an 6:120) Abandoning the inward sin, which the creation does not recognize—such as envy, ill thoughts, innovation, harboring malice towards people, and other sins of the hearts—is gratitude for the hidden blessings. And abandoning outward sin with the limbs is gratitude for the apparent blessing. Nay, I say: whoever disobeys God Almighty, even in a single trifle, such as opening his eyelid where lowering the gaze is obligatory, has indeed disbelieved in every blessing of God Almighty upon him in the heavens and the earth and what is between them. For everything God Almighty has created, even the angels, the heavens, the earth, animals, and plants in their entirety, is a blessing upon every one of the servants, by which his benefit is perfected, even if others also benefit from it. For God Almighty has in every trifle of the eyelid two blessings: in the eyelid itself, for He created beneath each eyelid muscles with tendons and ligaments connected to the nerves of the brain, by which the lowering of the upper lid and the raising of the lower lid is accomplished; and on each eyelid are black lashes, and God's blessing in their blackness is that they gather the light of the eye, for whiteness scatters light and blackness gathers it; and God's blessing in their arrangement in a single row is that it is a barrier against creeping insects from crawling into the inner eye and a trap for the specks that scatter in the air. And in each hair of them are two blessings: from the softness of its root, and with the softness, the firmness of its erectness. And in the interlocking of the lashes is a blessing greater than all: that the dust of the air might prevent the opening of the eye, and if it were closed, one would not see; so the eyelids gather to the extent that the lashes interlace, and one looks from behind the lattice of hair, so the lattice of hair prevents the reach of debris from outside, yet does not prevent the extension of sight from within. Then, if dust reaches the pupil, the edges of the eyelids are created as servants, closing over the pupil like a polisher for a mirror, so it closes once or twice, and the pupil is polished from the dust, and the debris exits to the corners of the eye. And the fly, since its pupil has no eyelid, He created for it two hands, so you see it constantly wiping its pupils with them to polish them from dust. Since we have left off exhaustive detail of the blessings due to its need for elaboration exceeding the original scope of this book—and perhaps we will resume for it a dedicated book if time permits and success aids, which we shall call "The Wonders of God Almighty's Creation"—let us return to our purpose and say: Whoever looks at what is forbidden has disbelieved, by the opening of the eye, in God Almighty's blessing in the eyelids. And the eyelids are not sustained except by the eye, nor the eye except by the head, nor the head except by the entire body, nor the body except by nourishment, nor nourishment except by water, earth, air, rain, clouds, the sun, and the moon, nor does anything of that stand except by the heavens, nor the heavens except by the angels. For the whole is like a single thing, its parts interconnected like the limbs of the body, one with another. Thus, he has disbelieved in every blessing in existence from...

The farthest reaches of the Pleiades to the farthest depths of the earth—there remains no celestial sphere nor dominion, no animal nor plant nor inanimate object, except that it curses him. Hence, it is reported in the traditions: "The place where people gather will either curse them when they disperse or seek forgiveness for them." Likewise, it is reported that everything seeks forgiveness for the scholar, even the fish in the sea, and that the angels curse the disobedient in numerous expressions beyond enumeration. All this indicates that the disobedient, in a single instant, has wronged all that is in the dominion and the kingdom, and has destroyed himself—unless he follows a misdeed with a good deed that erases it, so the curse is exchanged for forgiveness. Then perhaps God will accept his repentance and pardon him.

And God Almighty revealed to Job, peace be upon him: "O Job, there is no servant of Mine from among the children of Adam except that two angels are with him. When he thanks Me for My blessings, the two angels say: 'O God, increase him in blessings upon blessings, for You are worthy of praise and thanks. Be near to the thankful.' Sufficient is the high station of the thankful, and with Me, I thank their thanks, and My angels supplicate for them, and the places love them, and the traces weep for them."

And just as you know that in every blink of an eye there are many blessings, know that in every breath that expands and contracts there are two blessings: with its expansion, the burnt smoke exits from the heart, and were it not to exit, he would perish; and with its contraction, it gathers the spirit of air to the heart, and were its passage blocked, his heart would burn from the cessation of the spirit of air and its coolness from it, and he would perish. Indeed, the day and night are twenty-four hours, and in every hour there are nearly a thousand breaths, and every breath is nearly ten instants. Thus, upon you in every instant are thousands upon thousands of blessings in every part of your body—nay, in every part of the world. Consider, then, can enumerating that be conceived or not?

And when the reality of God's saying, exalted is He, "And if you should count the favors of God, you could not enumerate them" was unveiled to Moses, peace be upon him, he said: "My Lord, how can I thank You when for every hair on my body there are two blessings: that You softened its root and that You smoothed its tip?" Likewise, it is reported in the tradition: "Whoever does not recognize God's blessings in his food and drink, his knowledge is little and his punishment is imminent." All that we have mentioned returns to food and drink, so consider other blessings by them, for the insightful one does not cast his eye upon anything in the world, nor does his thought touch upon any existent, except that he realizes God has a blessing for him therein. So let us leave exhaustive detail, for that is aspiring to the unattainable.

(Explanation of the Reason Turning Creation Away from Gratitude)

Know that nothing has caused creation to fall short in gratitude for blessings except ignorance and heedlessness. For they are prevented by ignorance and heedlessness from recognizing the blessings, and gratitude for a blessing cannot be conceived except after recognizing it. Then, if they recognize a blessing, they think that gratitude for it is to say with their tongue, 'Praise be to God, thanks be to God,' and they do not know that the meaning of gratitude is to employ the blessing in fulfilling the wisdom for which it was intended, which is obedience to God, mighty and majestic. So nothing prevents gratitude after attaining these two recognitions except the overpowering of desire and the domination of Satan.

As for heedlessness toward blessings, it has causes. One of its causes is that people, due to their ignorance, do not count as a blessing that which is common to creation and granted to them in all their states. Therefore, they are not grateful for the totality of blessings we mentioned, because they are general for creation, lavished upon them in all their states. So each individual among them does not see a particular distinction for himself, thus he does not count it as a blessing. You do not see them thanking God for the spirit of air, yet if their breath were seized for a moment until air was cut off from them, they would die. If they were confined in a steam room with hot air or in a well with air heavy from water's moisture, they would die of distress. If one of them were afflicted with something of that, then delivered, he might consider that a blessing and thank God for it. This is the height of ignorance, for their gratitude becomes contingent upon the blessing being stripped from them, then returned to them in some circumstances, while the blessing in all circumstances is more deserving of gratitude in some of them. Thus, you do not see the insightful one grateful for the health of his sight until his eyes go blind. Then, if his sight were restored to him, he would perceive it, be grateful for it, and count it a blessing. Since God's mercy is vast, He generalized it for creation and lavished it upon them in all circumstances, but the ignorant one does not count it a blessing.

This ignorant one is like a wicked servant whose due is to be beaten constantly, so that if he is left unbeaten for an hour, he considers it a favor. If he is left unbeaten perpetually, insolence overcomes him and he leaves off gratitude. Thus, people only give thanks for wealth, due to the specificity that comes from its abundance or scarcity, and they forget all the blessings of God Almighty upon them. As one complained of his poverty to a person of insight and showed intense grief over it, he said to him: "Would it please you to be blind and have ten thousand dirhams?" He said: "No." He said: "Would it please you to be mute and have ten thousand dirhams?" He said: "No." He said: "Would it please you that I cut off your hands and feet and you have...

Twenty thousand, to which he said no. Then he was asked, "Would you be pleased to be insane and have ten thousand dirhams?" He said no. Then it was said, "Are you not ashamed to complain against your Lord when He has fifty thousand worth of goods in your possession?" It is related that a certain reciter was so severely afflicted by poverty that he became utterly distressed. In a dream, he saw a speaker saying to him, "Would you like us to make you forget Surah al-An'am and give you a thousand dinars?" He said no. "Then Surah Hud?" He said no. "Then Surah Yusuf?" He said no. The speaker enumerated surahs to him, then said, "So you possess the equivalent of a hundred thousand dinars, yet you complain?" He awoke relieved. Ibn al-Sammak entered upon a caliph who was holding a cup of water to drink. He said to him, "Admonish me." Ibn al-Sammak said, "If this drink were not given to you except in exchange for all your wealth, and otherwise you would remain thirsty, would you give it?" He said yes. "And if it were not given except for your entire kingdom, would you relinquish it?" He said yes. He said, "Then do not rejoice in a kingdom that is not worth a drink of water." This shows that God's blessing upon a servant in a drink of water when thirsty is greater than possessing the entire earth. Since human nature tends to value specific blessings over general ones, and we have mentioned the general blessings, let us briefly indicate the specific blessings. We say: There is no servant who, if he reflects deeply on his own conditions, does not see from God a blessing or many blessings specific to him, not shared by all people, but shared by a small number, or perhaps by no one else. Every servant acknowledges this in three matters: in intellect, character, and knowledge. As for intellect, there is no servant of God but that he is content with God regarding his intellect, believing himself to be the most intelligent of people. Few ask God for intellect. Among the nobility of intellect is that one who lacks it rejoices in it just as one endowed with it does. If he believes he is the most intelligent of people, it is incumbent upon him to give thanks, for if it is so, gratitude is obligatory, and if it is not but he believes it to be so, it is a blessing for him. If someone places a treasure underground, he rejoices in it and is grateful for it. If the treasure is taken without his knowledge, his joy remains according to his belief, and his gratitude remains because in his view it is as if it still exists. As for character, there is no servant who does not see in others faults he dislikes and traits he condemns; he condemns them because he sees himself free from them. If he is not occupied with condemning others, he ought to occupy himself with thanking God Almighty for the goodness of his character and for testing others with bad character. As for knowledge, there is no one who does not know the inner aspects of his own affairs and the hidden thoughts he alone possesses. If the veil were lifted so that any creature became aware of it, he would be disgraced—how much more if all people were to see? Therefore, every servant has knowledge of a private matter not shared by any of God's servants. Why then does he not thank God for the beautiful covering He has cast over his faults, revealing the good and concealing the ugly, hiding it from people's eyes and making its knowledge specific to him so that no one becomes aware? These are three specific blessings that every servant acknowledges, either absolutely or in some matters. Let us descend from this level to another, slightly more general level, and say: There is no servant but that God has provided him, in his form, his person, his character, his attributes, his family, his children, his dwelling, his country, his companion, his relatives, his honor, his status, or in all his likes, with things that if they were taken from him and he were given what specifically belongs to another, he would not be content. This is like being made a believer not an unbeliever, alive not inanimate, human not beast, male not female, healthy not sick, sound not defective. All these are specificities, even if they also have generality. If these conditions were exchanged for their opposites, he would not be content. Moreover, he has matters he would not exchange for the conditions of other humans either. That is, either he would not exchange it for what any creature has been specifically given, or he would not exchange it for what the majority have been given. If he would not exchange his own state for that of another, then his state is better than another's. If he does not know a person whose condition he would accept for himself in place of his own, either in general or in a specific matter, then God has blessings upon him that He does not have upon any of His servants besides him. If he would exchange his own state for that of some but not others, let him look at the number of those he considers fortunate; inevitably he will see them as fewer compared to others. Thus, those below him in condition are far more numerous than those above him. Why then does he look at those above him to belittle God's blessings upon himself, and not look at those below him to magnify God's blessings upon him? Why does he not equate his worldly state with his religious state? Does not his soul, when reproaching him for an evil he commits, excuse itself by saying that among the wicked there are many? He always looks in religion at those below him, not above him. Why then does he not look similarly in worldly matters? If the condition of most people in...

If one's religion is better than another's and their worldly condition is superior to that of most people, how can gratitude not be incumbent upon them? For this reason, the Prophet ﷺ said: "Whoever looks in worldly matters to those below him and in religious matters to those above him, God will record him as patient and grateful. And whoever looks in worldly matters to those above him and in religious matters to those below him, God will not record him as patient or grateful." Therefore, whoever reflects upon their own state and examines the many blessings which God Almighty has specifically bestowed upon them—especially those granted the Sunnah, faith, knowledge, the Qur'an, then leisure, health, security, and the like—will understand. Hence it is said:

            Whoever desires a spacious life, extending
            In his religion and then in his world with prosperity,
            Let him look to one above him in piety,
            And let him look to one below him in wealth.

And the Prophet ﷺ said: "Whoever is not enriched by the signs of God, God will not enrich him." This points to the blessing of knowledge. And he, peace be upon him, said: "Indeed, the Qur'an is the richness after which there is no need and with which there is no poverty." And he, peace be upon him, said: "Whoever is given the Qur'an by God and thinks that anyone is richer than him has mocked the signs of God." And he ﷺ said: "He is not of us who does not chant the Qur'an." And he, peace be upon him, said: "Certainty suffices as wealth." Some of the early pious said that God Almighty says in some of the revealed scriptures: "A servant whom I have made independent of three things, I have indeed perfected My favor upon him: from a ruler who comes to him, a physician who treats him, and from what is in his brother's hand." A poet expressed this, saying:

            When sustenance comes to you,
            Likewise health and security,
            And you become a brother of grief,
            Then may grief never leave you.

Rather, the most eloquent expressions and the most articulate words are the speech of the most eloquent of those who spoke Arabic, when he ﷺ conveyed this meaning, saying: "Whoever wakes up secure in his home, healthy in his body, with his daily sustenance, it is as if the entire world has been gathered for him." However much you contemplate people, you find them complaining and suffering from matters beyond these three, even though these are detrimental to them, and they do not thank God for these three blessings, nor do they thank God for the blessing of faith, through which they attain eternal bliss and the great dominion. Rather, the insightful person should only rejoice in knowledge, certainty, and faith. Indeed, we know of scholars who, if all that lies within the power of the kings of the earth from east to west—wealth, followers, and supporters—were handed to them and they were told, "Take it in exchange for your knowledge, nay, for a tenth of a tenth of your knowledge," they would not take it, due to their hope that the blessing of knowledge will lead them to nearness to God Almighty in the Hereafter. Indeed, if it were said to them, "You will have in the Hereafter what you hope for in its entirety, so take these worldly pleasures in exchange for your delight in knowledge in this world and your joy in it," they would not take it, knowing that the pleasure of knowledge is everlasting, uninterrupted, enduring—it cannot be stolen, usurped, or competed for—and it is pure, without any impurity. All worldly pleasures are deficient, tainted, and troubled; their hoped-for benefit does not match their feared harm, their pleasure does not match their pain, nor their joy their sorrow. Thus it has been until now, and thus it will be for as long as time remains. For worldly pleasures were only created to attract deficient intellects and deceive them, until, when they are deceived and bound by them, they turn against them and become recalcitrant, like a beautiful woman whose outward appearance adorns herself for a lustful, wealthy youth until, when his heart is bound to her, she becomes recalcitrant and veils herself from him, leaving him in constant toil and perpetual hardship—all due to his delusion by the pleasure of looking at her for a moment. Had he been wise and lowered his gaze, disdaining that pleasure, he would have been safe for his entire life. Thus have the people of the world fallen into the snares and traps of the world. We should not say that the one who turns away from the world suffers patiently from abstaining from it, for the one who inclines toward it also suffers patiently in preserving it, acquiring it, and defending it from thieves. The suffering of the one who turns away leads to pleasure in the Hereafter, while the suffering of the one who inclines leads to pain in the Hereafter. So let the one who turns away from the world recite upon himself the words of God Almighty: "Do not weaken in pursuit of the enemy. If you are suffering, they are suffering as you are suffering, but you hope from God what they do not hope." Therefore, the path of gratitude has been blocked for creation only due to their ignorance of the varieties of blessings, both apparent and hidden, specific and general.

If you ask: "What is the remedy for these heedless hearts so that they may feel the blessings of God Almighty and perhaps give thanks?" I say: As for insightful hearts, their remedy is contemplation upon what we have alluded to regarding the categories of God Almighty's general blessings. As for the dull hearts that do not consider a blessing a blessing unless it specifically benefits them or they feel affliction alongside it, their way is to always look at those below them and do as some of the pious did.

The Sufis, since they would daily visit the houses of the sick, the graveyards, and the places where legal punishments were carried out, would attend the houses of the sick to witness the various tribulations God Almighty had placed upon them. Then they would reflect upon their own health and well-being, causing their hearts to feel the blessing of health when sensing the affliction of diseases, and thus thank God Almighty.
