[48] A hadith reported by Muslim from the narration of ‘Ā’ishah: “I seek refuge in Your pleasure from Your wrath, and in Your pardon from Your punishment.”

[49] The hadith, “Indeed, a cloudiness comes over my heart…” has preceded in the Book of Repentance and before it in the Book of Supplications.

[50] The hadith of ‘Ā’ishah when she said to him, “May Allah forgive you your past and future sins,” so why this weeping? It is narrated by Abū al-Shaykh, and it is the remainder of the hadith of ‘Atā’ from her, which preceded this by nine hadiths. It is in Muslim from the narration of ‘Urwah from her in a concise form, and likewise it is in the two Ṣaḥīḥ collections concisely from the hadith of al-Mughīrah ibn Shu‘bah.

[51] The hadith, “Act, for everyone is facilitated for what he was created for,” from the narration of ‘Alī and ‘Imrān ibn Ḥuṣayn.

[52] The hadith, “Whoever drinks from a vessel of gold or silver, it is as if he is swallowing the fire of Hell into his belly,” is agreed upon from the narration of Umm Salamah, though the author did not explicitly state it is a hadith.

[53] The hadith, “Were it not that the devils hover around the children of Adam, they would behold the kingdom of the heavens,” has preceded in the Book of Fasting.

[54] The hadith, “When predestination is mentioned, withhold,” is narrated by al-Ṭabarānī from the narration of Ibn Mas‘ūd and has preceded in the Book of Knowledge, though the author did not explicitly state it is a hadith.

[55] The hadith: It was said to him, “It is said that Jesus walked upon water.” He said, “Had his certainty increased, he would have walked upon air.” This is a rejected (munkar) hadith not known as such. The known version is narrated by Ibn Abī al-Dunyā in the Book of Certainty from the saying of Bakr ibn ‘Abd Allāh al-Muzanī: The disciples lost their prophet, so it was said to them, “Head towards the sea.” They went seeking him, and when they reached the sea, behold, he was approaching, walking upon the water. Then he mentioned a hadith in which Jesus said, “If the son of Adam had a mustard seed’s worth of certainty, he would walk upon the water.” And Abū Manṣūr al-Daylamī narrated in *Musnad al-Firdaws* with a weak chain from the hadith of Mu‘ādh ibn Jabal: “If you knew Allah as He truly should be known, you would walk upon the seas, and the mountains would be removed by your supplication.”

[56] The hadith, “There will be rulers over you who will cause corruption, yet through them Allah will bring about more good…” Muslim narrated it from the narration of Umm Salamah: “Rulers will be appointed over you; you will recognize some of their actions and reject others.” Al-Tirmidhī narrated it with the wording, “There will be leaders over you,” and said it is ḥasan ṣaḥīḥ. Al-Bazzār narrated it with a weak chain from the narration of Ibn ‘Umar: “The ruler is the shadow of Allah on earth; every oppressed one among His servants takes refuge in him. If he is just, he has the reward and the subjects owe gratitude. If he is oppressive, unjust, or tyrannical, the sin is upon him and the subjects must be patient.” As for his statement, “and through them Allah will bring about more good,” I have not found it with this wording except that it is understood from the hadith of Ibn Mas‘ūd when people rushed to him, objecting to the conduct of al-Walīd ibn ‘Uqbah. ‘Abd Allāh said, “Be patient, for the injustice of your ruler for fifty years is better than civil strife for a month. For I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say…” and he mentioned a hadith containing, “and a wicked rule is better than civil strife.” Al-Ṭabarānī narrated it in *al-Kabīr* with an acceptable chain.

[57] The hadith of his saying during the digging of the Trench, “There is no life except the life of the Hereafter,” is agreed upon from the narration of Anas.

[58] The hadith of his saying during the Farewell Pilgrimage, “There is no life except the life of the Hereafter,” is narrated by al-Shāfi‘ī as *mursal* and by al-Ḥākim as *muttasil*, who authenticated it. It has preceded in the Book of Pilgrimage.

[59] The hadith: A man said, “O Allah, I ask You for the perfection of blessing…” Al-Tirmidhī narrated it from the narration of Mu‘ādh with a ḥasan chain.

[60] The hadith, “An excellent possession for a righteous man is righteous wealth,” is narrated by Aḥmad, Abū Ya‘lā, and al-Ṭabarānī from the narration of ‘Amr ibn al-‘Āṣ with a good chain.

[61] The hadith, “An excellent aid for God-consciousness is wealth,” is narrated by Abū Manṣūr al-Daylamī in *Musnad al-Firdaws* from the narration of Muḥammad ibn al-Munkadir from Jābir. Abū al-Qāsim al-Baghawī narrated it from the narration of Ibn al-Munkadir as *mursal*, and from his path al-Quḍā‘ī narrated it in *Musnad al-Shihāb* as *mursal*.

[62] The hadith, “Whoever wakes up healthy in his body, secure in his dwelling…” is narrated by al-Tirmidhī, who graded it ḥasan, and by Ibn Mājah from the narration of ‘Ubayd Allāh ibn Miḥṣan al-Anṣārī, and it has preceded.

[63] The hadith, "An excellent aid to religion is a righteous woman," I have not found a chain of transmission for it. Muslim has from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr: "The world is enjoyment, and the best enjoyment of the world is a righteous woman."

[64] The hadith, "When a servant dies, his deeds cease except for three..." Muslim transmitted it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and it was mentioned previously in the Book of Marriage.

[65] The hadith concerning what befell him (peace be upon him) of harm and the like, to the point of being reduced to fleeing and emigration. Al-Bukhari and Muslim transmitted it from the hadith of 'A'ishah, who said to the Prophet (peace be upon him), "Has there come upon you a day more severe than the day of Uhud?" He said, "I have certainly met from your people... and the most severe I met was the day of 'Aqabah, when I presented myself to Ibn 'Abd Yalil..." At-Tirmidhi, who graded it sound, and Ibn Majah transmitted from the hadith of Anas: "I have been made to fear for the sake of Allah, and no one fears as I have feared. I have been harmed for the sake of Allah, and no one is harmed as I have been harmed. Thirty days and nights passed upon me and Bilal without us having any food that a living creature could eat, except what Bilal could conceal under his arm." At-Tirmidhi said the meaning of this is when the Prophet (peace be upon him) went out fleeing from Makkah with Bilal. Al-Bukhari has from 'Urwah who said: I asked 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr about the most severe thing the polytheists did to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). He said, "I saw 'Uqbah ibn Abi Mu'ayt come to the Prophet (peace be upon him) while he was praying and place his garment on his neck, strangling him severely. Then Abu Bakr came and pushed him away..." Al-Bazzar and Abu Ya'la transmitted from the hadith of Anas who said, "They struck the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) until he fell unconscious. Abu Bakr stood up and began calling out, 'Woe to you! Would you kill a man for saying, "My Lord is Allah"?' Its chain is sound according to the conditions of Muslim."

[66] The hadith, "The leaders are from Quraysh," An-Nasa'i and Al-Hakim transmitted it from the hadith of Anas with a sound chain.

[67] The hadith, "He (peace be upon him) was from the noblest of people in lineage from Adam." *Al-Urumah* means origin; this is known. Muslim transmitted from the hadith of Wathilah ibn Al-Asqa', marfu': "Allah chose Kinanah from the children of Isma'il, and chose Quraysh from Kinanah, and chose from Quraysh Banu Hashim, and chose me from Banu Hashim." In a narration of At-Tirmidhi: "Allah chose from the children of Ibrahim, Isma'il..." and he has from the hadith of Al-'Abbas, and he graded it good, and Ibn 'Abbas and Al-Muttalib ibn Rabi'ah, and he authenticated it, and Al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'ah, and he graded it good: "Allah created creation and made me from the best..." In a hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: "What is the matter with people who belittle lineage? By Allah, I am the best of them in lineage and the best of them in status."

[68] The hadith, "Choose for your offspring," Ibn Majah transmitted it from the hadith of 'A'ishah, and it was mentioned previously in the Book of Marriage.

[69] The hadith, "Beware of the lush dung heap," it was also mentioned previously therein.

[70] The hadith, "The best happiness is a long life spent in worship of Allah," is singular with this wording. At-Tirmidhi has from the hadith of Abu Bakrah that a man said, "O Messenger of Allah, which people are best?" He said, "He whose life is long and his deeds are good," and he said it is *hasan sahih*.

[71] The hadith, "Seek good from those with handsome faces," Abu Ya'la transmitted it from the narration of Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash from Khayrah bint Muhammad ibn Thabit ibn Saba' from her mother 'A'ishah. I do not know the condition of Khayrah and her mother. Ibn Hibban transmitted it from another route in *Ad-Du'afa'*, and Al-Bayhaqi in *Ash-Shu'ab* from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. It has routes, all of which are weak.

[72] The hadith censuring wealth and status. At-Tirmidhi transmitted it from the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik: "Two hungry wolves sent among sheep do not cause more corruption to them than a man's love of wealth and status does to his religion." It was mentioned previously in the censure of wealth and stinginess.

[73] The hadith, "I am to you only like a father to his child," Muslim transmitted it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah without the phrase "to his child," and it was mentioned previously.

[74] The hadith, "You are plunging into the Fire like moths, and I am seizing you by your waistbands," agreed upon from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah with the wording, "My parable and the parable of the people..." And Muslim said, "The parable of my community is like a man who lit a fire, and insects and moths began falling into it. I am seizing you by your waistbands, and you are plunging into it." And Muslim has from the hadith of Jabir, "And I am seizing you by your waistbands from the Fire, and you are slipping from my hand."

[75] The hadith, "Let the provision of any one of you from this world be like the provisions of a rider." Ibn Majah and Al-Hakim transmitted it from the hadith of Salman. The wording of Al-Hakim is, "And he said, 'Like the provisions of a rider,' and he said its chain is sound." I say: It is from the narration of Abu Sufyan from his unnamed shaykhs. And Ibn Majah has, "He enjoined upon me that it suffices for any one of you..."

[76] The hadith regarding ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn ‘Awf seeking permission to give away all that he possessed when he was told that the wealthy would enter Paradise with difficulty. Permission was granted to him, whereupon Gabriel descended and said, "Command him to feed the poor." This hadith is reported by al-Hakim from the narration of ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn ‘Awf, who said its chain is sound. I [al-Ghazali] say: No, for within it is Khalid ibn Abi Malik, who is very weak.

[77] The hadith: "No one will enter Paradise except by the mercy of Allah," agreed upon as sound from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "None of you will enter Paradise by his deeds." They said, "Not even you, O Messenger of Allah?" He said, "Not even I, unless Allah envelops me with His bounty and mercy." In a narration of Muslim: "No one will be admitted to Paradise by his deeds..." The hadith. Both [al-Bukhari and Muslim] agreed upon it from the narration of ‘A’ishah, and Muslim alone reported it from the narration of Jabir, as previously mentioned.

[78] The hadith that he was asked about the spirit, and he did not add except to say, "The spirit is of the command of my Lord," agreed upon as sound from the narration of Ibn Mas‘ud, as previously mentioned in the explanation of the wonders of the heart.

[79] The hadith prohibiting belief in astrologers and the study of stars, reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah with a sound chain from the narration of Ibn ‘Abbas: "Whoever acquires a branch of the knowledge of stars has acquired a branch of sorcery; the more he adds, the more he adds." And by al-Tabarani from the narration of Ibn Mas‘ud and Thawban: "When the stars are mentioned, refrain." Their chains are weak, as previously mentioned in the chapter on knowledge. And in Muslim from the narration of Mu‘awiyah ibn al-Hakam al-Sulami, who said: I said, "O Messenger of Allah, there were matters we used to do in the pre-Islamic period of ignorance; we used to visit soothsayers." He said, "Do not visit soothsayers..." The hadith.

[80] The hadith: He recited the saying of the Almighty: "Our Lord, You have not created this in vain. Glory be to You! So protect us from the punishment of the Fire." Then he said, "Woe to him who recites this verse and then wipes his forehead with it," meaning he neglected to contemplate it. Reported by al-Tha‘labi from the narration of Ibn ‘Abbas with the wording: "and did not reflect upon it." Within it is Abu Janab Yahya ibn Abi Hibah, who is weak.

[81] The reports concerning the angels entrusted with the heavens and the earths, and the parts of plants and animals, even every drop of rain and every cloud driven from one side to another. In the two Sahih collections from the narration of Abu Dharr in the story of the Night Journey: Gabriel said to the keeper of the lowest heaven, "Open." And in it: He came to the second heaven and said to its keeper, "Open..." The hadith. And in both from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "Indeed, Allah has angels who travel about conveying to me the greetings from my nation." And in the two Sahih collections from the narration of ‘A’ishah in the story of him offering himself to ‘Abd Yalayl, the angel of the mountains called to me: "If you wish, I will cause the two mountains to close upon them..." The hadith. And in both from the narration of Anas: "Indeed, Allah has entrusted an angel with the womb..." The hadith. And Abu Mansur al-Daylami reported in *Musnad al-Firdaws* from the narration of Buraydah al-Aslami: "There is no plant that grows except that there is an angel entrusted beneath it until it is harvested..." The hadith. Within it are Muhammad ibn Salih al-Tabari and Abu Bahr al-Bakrawi, whose name is ‘Uthman ibn ‘Abd al-Rahman, and both are weak. And by al-Tabarani from the narration of Abu al-Darda’ with a weak chain: "Indeed, Allah has angels who descend every night, removing fatigue from the mounts of the warriors, except for a mount with a bell on its neck." And by al-Tirmidhi, who graded it good, from the narration of Ibn ‘Abbas: The Jews said, "O Abu al-Qasim, inform us about thunder." He said, "It is an angel entrusted with the clouds." And in Muslim from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "While a man was in a desert, he heard a voice from a cloud: 'Water the garden of so-and-so.' That cloud then moved aside and poured its water into a rocky tract..." The hadith.

[82] The hadith: "Indeed, the spot where people gather curses them or seeks forgiveness for them"—I have not found any basis for it.

[83] The hadith: "Indeed, everything seeks forgiveness for the scholar, even the fish in the sea," previously mentioned in the chapter on knowledge.

[84] The hadith: "Indeed, the angels curse the disobedient," reported by Muslim from the narration of Abu Hurayrah: "The angels curse one of you if he points at his brother with an iron weapon, even if he is his brother from his father and mother."

[85] The hadith: "Whoever looks in worldly matters to those below him and in religious matters to those above him, Allah will record him as patient and grateful." The hadith is reported by al-Tirmidhi from the narration of ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Amr, and he said it is rare. Within it is al-Muthanna ibn al-Sabbah, who is weak.

[86] The hadith: "Whoever is not enriched by the signs of Allah, Allah will not enrich him"—I have not found it with this wording.

[87] The hadith: "Indeed, the Qur'an is the enrichment; there is no enrichment after it, nor poverty with it," reported by Abu Ya‘la.

Al-Tabarani narrates from the hadith of Anas with a weak chain, wording: "The Qur'an is richness; there is no poverty after it, nor richness beyond it." Al-Daraqutni said: "Abu Mu'awiyah narrated it from al-A'mash from Yazid al-Raqashi from al-Hasan as mursal, and that is more likely correct."

[88] Hadith: "Whoever Allah grants the Qur'an, and he thinks that anyone is richer than him, has mocked the verses of Allah." Al-Bukhari recorded it in al-Tarikh from the hadith of Raja' al-Fanawi, wording: "Whoever Allah grants the memorization of His Book, and he thinks that anyone has been given better than what he has been given, has belittled the greatest blessings." It has preceded in the merits of the Qur'an. Raja' is disputed regarding his companionship. It is reported from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr, Jabir, and al-Bara' similarly, and all are weak.

[89] Hadith: "He is not from us who does not chant the Qur'an." It has preceded in the etiquettes of recitation.

[90] Hadith: "Certainty suffices as richness." Al-Tabarani narrates it from the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, and Ibn Abi al-Dunya narrates it in al-Qana'ah as mawquf upon him. It has preceded.

[91] Hadith: "Whoever wakes up secure in his home..." The hadith has preceded multiple times.

[92] Hadith: "Whenever Allah's favor upon a servant increases, the needs of people toward him increase." Ibn 'Adi and Ibn Hibban in al-Du'afa' narrate it from the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, wording: "Except that the burdens of people upon him increase. So whoever does not bear those burdens..." Ibn Hibban in al-Du'afa' narrates it from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas and said it is fabricated upon Hajjaj al-A'war.

[93] Hadith: "Indeed Allah protects His servant from the world..." Al-Tirmidhi narrates it and graded it hasan, and al-Hakim graded it sahih. It has preceded.

[94] Hadith: "When a servant commits a sin and is afflicted with hardship and trial in the world, Allah is more generous than to punish him a second time." Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah narrate it from the hadith of 'Ali: "Whoever commits a sin in the world and is punished for it, Allah is more just than to impose His punishment upon His servant." This is the wording of Ibn Majah. Al-Tirmidhi said: "Whoever commits a crime and his punishment is hastened in the world," and he said it is hasan. Al-Bukhari and Muslim have from the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit: "Whoever commits any of that and is punished for it, it is an expiation for him."

[95] Hadith: "A man said to him: 'Advise me.' He said: 'Do not accuse Allah regarding anything He has decreed for you.'" Ahmad and al-Tabarani narrate it from the hadith of 'Ubadah with an addition at the beginning, and in its chain is Ibn Lahi'ah.

[96] Hadith: "He looked at the sky and laughed, and was asked. He said: 'I marvel at Allah's decree for the believer...'" Muslim narrates it from the hadith of Suhayb without mentioning his looking at the sky and laughing: "I marvel at the affair of the believer. Indeed, all his affair is good, and that is for no one except the believer. If good befalls him, he is grateful, and that is good for him. If harm befalls him, he is patient, and that is good for him." Al-Nasa'i in al-Yawm wa al-Laylah narrates from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: "I marvel at Allah's pleasure for the believer. If good befalls him, he praises his Lord and is grateful..."

[97] Hadith: "The world is the prison of the believer and the paradise of the disbeliever." Muslim narrates it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah. It has preceded.

[98] Hadith: "Whomever Allah intends good for, He afflicts him." Al-Bukhari narrates it from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah.

[99] Hadith: "A man said: 'O Messenger of Allah, my wealth is gone and my body is sick.' He said: 'There is no good in a servant whose wealth does not depart and whose body does not become sick. Indeed, when Allah loves a servant, He tests him, and when He tests him, He grants him patience.'" Ibn Abi al-Dunya narrates it in Kitab al-Marad wa al-Kaffarat from the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri with a chain containing leniency.

[100] Hadith: "Indeed, a man may have a rank with Allah that he cannot attain by his deeds, until he is tested with an affliction in his body, and thus attains it." Abu Dawud narrates it in the narration of Ibn Dasah and Ibn al-'Abd from the hadith of Muhammad ibn Khalid al-Sulami from his father from his grandfather. It is not in the narration of al-Lu'lu'i. Ahmad, Abu Ya'la, and al-Tabarani narrate it from this avenue. Muhammad ibn Khalid was only narrated from by Abu al-Malih al-Hasan ibn 'Umar al-Raqqi. Likewise, only his son Muhammad narrated from Khalid. Abu Nu'aym mentioned that Ibn Mandah named his grandfather al-Lajlaj ibn Sulaym, but Allah knows best. On this basis, his son is Khalid ibn al-Lajlaj al-'Amiri, that one is well-known; a group narrated from him. Ibn Mandah, Abu Nu'aym, and Ibn 'Abd al-Barr narrate it in al-Sahabah from the narration of 'Abdullah ibn Abi Iyas ibn Abi Fatimah from his father from his grandfather.

Al-Bayhaqi narrates from the chain of Ibrahim al-Sulami from his father from his grandfather, but God knows best.

[101] The hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Arat: We came to the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, while he was reclining on his cloak in the shade of the Kaaba, and we complained to him of the persecution we faced.

[102] The hadith of Anas: When God intends good for a servant and wishes to purify him, He pours tribulation upon him profusely. Ibn Abi al-Dunya recorded it in the Book of Sickness from the narration of Bakr ibn Khunays from Yazid al-Raqashi from Anas, in a shorter version without the words, "Then on the Day of Resurrection..." to the end. Both Bakr ibn Khunays and al-Raqashi are weak narrators. Al-Isfahani recorded it in full in "Al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib," inserting between Bakr and al-Raqashi the name of Darar ibn 'Amr, who is also weak.

[103] The hadith: When the verse was revealed, "Whoever does an evil deed will be recompensed for it," Abu Bakr al-Siddiq said, "How can one rejoice after this verse?" The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, replied, "May God forgive you, O Abu Bakr. Do you not fall ill...?" This is narrated by an unnamed narrator from Abu Bakr. Al-Tirmidhi recorded it through another chain with different wording and deemed it weak, saying it has no sound chain. Al-Daraqutni said it was also narrated from the hadith of 'Umar and from the hadith of al-Zubayr, but none of them are established.

[104] The hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir: If you see a person to whom God gives what he loves while he persists in disobedience, know that this is a gradual enticement. Narrated by Ahmad, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi in "Al-Shu'ab" with a good chain.

[105] The hadith of al-Hasan al-Basri concerning a man who saw a woman and kept turning to look at her as he walked, then he struck a wall. In it is: When God intends good for a servant, He hastens the punishment for his sin in this world. Ahmad and al-Tabarani recorded it with a sound chain from the narration of al-Hasan from 'Abdullah ibn Ma'qil, raised to the Prophet and connected. Al-Tabarani also connected it through the narration of al-Hasan from 'Ammar ibn Yasir and from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas. Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah recorded the raised portion from the hadith of Anas, and al-Tirmidhi graded it as good.

[106] The hadith of Anas: No servant ever swallows two draughts more beloved to God than a draught of anger he restrains with forbearance, and a draught of affliction for which he exercises patience. Abu Bakr ibn Lal recorded it in "Makārim al-Akhlaq" from the hadith of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib without mentioning the two draughts, and in its chain is Muhammad ibn Sadaqah, who is al-Farisi, a narrator of rejected hadith. Ibn Majah recorded from the hadith of Ibn 'Umar with a sound chain: No draught is greater with God than a draught of anger which a servant suppresses seeking the Face of God. Abu Mansur al-Daylami recorded in "Musnad al-Firdaws" from the hadith of Abu Umamah: No drop has ever fallen upon the earth more beloved to God Almighty than the blood of a Muslim spilled in the path of God or a tear shed in the darkness of night. In its chain is Muhammad ibn Sadaqah, who is al-Farisi, a narrator of rejected hadith.

[107] The hadith that he, peace be upon him, used to seek refuge in his supplication from the tribulations of this world and the tribulations of the Hereafter. Ahmad narrated it from the hadith of Bishr ibn Abi Artah with the wording, "Protect us from the disgrace of this world and the punishment of the Hereafter," and its chain is sound. Abu Dawud has it from the hadith of 'A'ishah: O God, I seek refuge in You from the distress of this world and the distress of the Day of Resurrection. In its chain is Baqiyyah, who is a mudallis, and he narrated it with 'an'anah.

[108] The hadith: He and the prophets, peace be upon them, used to say, "Our Lord, grant us good in this world and good in the Hereafter, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire." Al-Bukhari and Muslim recorded it from the hadith of Anas: The supplication the Prophet, peace be upon him, most frequently made was: O God, grant us in this world... Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i have it from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib who said: I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, say between the two corners (of the Kaaba): Our Lord, grant us...

[109] The hadith: He used to seek refuge from the gloating of enemies. Previously mentioned in the chapter on supplications.

[110] The hadith: 'Ali, may God be pleased with him, said, "O God, I ask You for patience." He, peace be upon him, said, "You have asked God for tribulation; rather, ask Him for well-being." Al-Tirmidhi recorded it from the hadith of Mu'adh within a longer hadith and graded it as good, but he did not name 'Ali; he only said, "He heard a man..." Al-Nasa'i has it in "Al-Yawm wa al-Laylah" from the hadith of 'Ali: I was sitting when the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, passed by me while I was saying... In it is: "If it is tribulation, then grant me patience." He struck me with his foot and said, "O God, grant him well-being and healing," and said it is good and sound.

[111] The hadith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, "Ask Allah for well-being," was reported by Ibn Majah and al-Nasa'i in "Al-Yawm wa al-Laylah" with a good chain, and it has preceded.
[112] The hadith, "And Your well-being is more beloved to me," was mentioned by Ibn Ishaq in "Al-Sirah" in his supplication on the day he set out for Ta'if with the wording, "And Your well-being is more expansive for me." Similarly, Ibn Abi al-Dunya reported it in "Al-Du'a'" from the narration of Hassan ibn 'Atiyyah as a *mursal* report. Abu 'Abdullah ibn Mandah reported it from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far as a *musnad* report, and it contains someone unknown.
[113] The hadith, "The best of what you have been given is certainty and the resolve of patience," has preceded.
[114] The hadith, "The most grateful person on earth will be brought forth, and Allah will reward him with the reward of the grateful, and the most patient person on earth will be brought forth..." I did not find an origin for it.
[115] The hadith, "The grateful eater is in the station of the fasting, patient person," was reported by al-Tirmidhi, who graded it *hasan*, and by Ibn Majah from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and it has preceded.
[116] The hadith, "Friday is the Hajj of the poor, and the jihad of a woman is good conduct towards her husband," was reported by al-Harith ibn Abi Usamah in his *Musnad* with the first part from the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas with a weak chain, or by al-Tabarani with the second part from his hadith also with a weak chain: A woman said, "Allah has prescribed jihad for men, so what is the equivalent of that from their acts of obedience?" He said, "Obedience to their husbands." In another narration: "What is the reward for a woman's military expedition?" He said, "Obedience to the husband." The hadith contains al-Qasim ibn Fayyad; Abu Dawud declared him trustworthy, while Ibn Ma'in weakened him, and the rest of its narrators are reliable.
[117] The hadith, "The drinker of wine is like a worshipper of idols," was reported by Ibn Majah from the hadith of Abu Hurayrah with the wording "the addict of wine," and al-Harith ibn Abi Usamah reported it with the wording "the drinker" from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar. Both are weak. Ibn 'Adi said regarding the hadith of Abu Hurayrah that Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Isbahani erred in it.
[118] The hadith, "The last of the prophets to enter Paradise is Sulayman ibn Dawud because of his kingdom, and the last of my companions to enter Paradise is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf because of his wealth," was reported by al-Tabarani in "Al-Awsat" from the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal: "All the prophets will enter Paradise forty years before Dawud and Sulayman." He said, "Only Shu'ayb ibn Khalid reported it, and he is a reliable Kufan." Al-Bazzar reported from the hadith of Anas: "The first of the wealthy of my nation to enter Paradise is 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf." It contains Aghlab ibn Tamim, who is weak.
[119] The hadith, "Sulayman, the servant of the prophets, will enter after forty autumns," has preceded in the hadith of Mu'adh before it. Abu Mansur al-Daylami reported it in "Musnad al-Firdaws" from the narration of Dinar from Anas ibn Malik. Dinar al-Habashi is one of the liars upon Anas, and the hadith is rejected.
[120] The hadith, "All the gates of Paradise have two leaves except the gate of patience, for it is a single gate," I did not find an origin for it, nor in the hadiths concerning the leaves of the gates of Paradise is there a distinction. Muslim reported from the hadith of Anas concerning intercession, "By the One in Whose hand is the soul of Muhammad, the distance between the two leaves of the gates of Paradise is like the distance between Makkah and Busra." In the two *Sahih* collections, in the sermon of 'Utbah ibn Ghazwan, "We have been informed that the distance between the two leaves of the gates of Paradise is a journey of forty years, and a day will come upon it when it is crowded with throngs."
[121] The hadith prohibiting the earnings of a cupper has preceded.
[122] The hadith concerning his abstention from charity, calling it the filth of people, and honoring the people of his household by preserving them from it, was reported by Muslim from the hadith of 'Abd al-Muttalib ibn Rabi'ah: "This charity is not lawful for us; it is but the filth of the people, and it is not lawful for Muhammad nor for the family of Muhammad." In another narration of his: "the filth of people."
[123] The hadith, "Whoever is not grateful to people is not grateful to Allah," has preceded in the chapter on Zakat.
